# Conditions & Auto-configuration

> The seven designs (conditions SPI, condition-family, condition-report, configuration-classes, import-composition, auto-config-ordering, auto-configuration) cover the Spring reference's center-to-outer rings well and are notably coherent on the load-bearing intents: the pure-predicate/two-phase model, AND-fold + nested booleans, deferral-for-conditional-correctness, the three-pass deterministic sort, three-source exclusion merge, lite-only auto-configs, OnMissingBean back-off, and the accountable condition-report bridge. The Rust reframings (OnClass->cfg/feature, CGLIB-illusion designed-out, ordering-as-data, names-as-identity) are consistent and the cross-cutting Phase-2 keystones (compile-vs-runtime blend, cross-crate identity, anti-DCE self-check, WASM second-classpath) are surfaced identically across features. The gaps are mostly at the OUTER auto-configuration ring's Spring-specific machinery (default-base-package, class-rename replacements/aliases, import-filter/listener SPI, the curated nested-config fast-path idiom) and one semantic subtlety inside conditions (non-cascade to independently-discovered nested configs). A few coherence frictions exist around where attribute-conflict/`@Enable*` resolution lives, the FailureAnalyzer "loud-later" rendering side of the report bridge, and a duplicated cross-tier-report/anti-DCE-self-check mechanism that two features both reach for.

_7 feature designs. Implementation-agnostic — candidate realizations for Phase 2/3, not decisions._

## @Configuration / @Bean Factory Methods  `[configuration-classes]`

Spring lets Java code declare bean definitions imperatively via `@Bean` factory METHODS grouped on a `@Configuration` class — the tool for third-party/legacy types you can't annotate, or where construction needs real logic (`@Bean DataSource ds() { return HikariBuilder...build(); }`). A `@Bean` method's name defaults to the method name (overridable, multi-alias), its return type is the bean type (declare the MOST CONCRETE type so the container predicts it for matching), and it carries the same metadata levers as a component (`@Scope`+proxyMode, `initMethod`/`destroyMethod` with the close()/shutdown() destroy-INFERENCE footgun, `@Lazy`, `@Primary`/`@Fallback`, `@Order`, `@Conditional`, qualifiers). The marquee mechanic — the section I was told to replicate — is FULL vs LITE mode. In FULL mode (the `@Configuration(proxyBeanMethods=true)` default), `ConfigurationClassPostProcessor` CGLIB-SUBCLASSES the config class so each `@Bean` method is overridden to first consult the bean factory for the already-created singleton and only run the real body on a cache miss. The point is purely SEMANTIC, not a flag: it lets Java config READ LIKE PLAIN JAVA — `beanOne() { return new BeanOne(beanTwo()); }` — while still upholding the singleton contract; without interception that nested `beanTwo()` call would silently fabricate a SECOND unmanaged instance, a subtle correctness bug. CGLIB makes the intuitive syntax also the correct semantics. The cost imposed by subclassing: full-mode classes can't be `final`, `@Bean` methods can't be `private`/`final`, and it's GraalVM-native-hostile. LITE mode (`proxyBeanMethods=false`, or `@Bean` inside a plain `@Component`, or every `@AutoConfiguration` class which hardwires it) skips the subclass: `@Bean` methods become "a general-purpose factory method mechanism without special runtime processing." There, a method-to-method call is an ordinary Java call returning a NEW instance every time — and the reference docs say lite-mode `@Bean` methods are "not meant to declare inter-bean dependencies AT ALL": collaborators MUST arrive as autowired METHOD PARAMETERS (constructor-injection-equivalent), never via intra-class calls. Lite mode exists so authors can DECLARE INTENT ("I wire only via parameters; don't make me pay for proxying") — faster startup, smaller footprint, native-friendly, no final/private restrictions; Boot's recommendation is "use proxyBeanMethods=false unless you specifically rely on inter-bean method-call interception," and it forces lite on all auto-config so framework code models exemplary parameter-injection style. Two ownership models matter: `@Component` = "the container instantiates THIS class"; `@Bean` = "this method is a factory the developer wrote that PRODUCES a bean" — and `@Configuration` IS a `@Component` whose only added power is opting its `@Bean` methods into full-mode interception. leaf must replicate this INTENT — grouped, developer-written factory functions producing managed beans with full per-bean metadata, the parameter-injected lite default, and SOME mechanism to give the full-mode "inter-factory references return the managed singleton" guarantee — WITHOUT importing CGLIB (Rust has no runtime subclassing of a user struct, and a plain Rust method call `self.bean_two()` is statically resolved and CANNOT be intercepted by any proxy). The construction recipe in leaf is a typed factory the macro emits over a `@Bean`-annotated fn (the bean-definition `Factory` handle), parameter-autowired via autowiring-resolution; the deep open question is how, or whether, to reproduce full-mode's intra-config singleton-routing at all when the JVM trick that motivates it doesn't exist.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Lite-only canonical: `@Bean` is a parameter-injected typed factory fn; full-mode 'illusion' is DESIGNED OUT, not emulated
Lean on the deepest rustClash as a design SIMPLIFICATION rather than a problem to emulate: since Rust cannot intercept an intra-`impl` method call, do not pretend to. Make the LITE model the ONLY model — exactly what Spring tells everyone to do anyway (auto-config is lite-only; the official best practice is proxyBeanMethods=false). `#[configuration] impl AppConfig { #[bean] async fn pool(&self, cfg: &DbConfig) -> Result<Pool> { Pool::connect(cfg.url()).await } #[bean] fn repo(&self, pool: &Pool) -> Repo { Repo::new(pool.clone()) } }`. The macro reads each `#[bean]` fn and emits, per method, ONE `RawBeanDefinition` seed (bean-definition's metamodel keystone) whose `Factory` is a thin typed closure: `|ctx| Box::pin(async move { let cfg = ctx.resolve::<DbConfig>().await?; let pool = ctx.resolve::<Pool>().await?; AppConfig::pool(&this, cfg).await })` — i.e. each fn PARAMETER becomes an injection point resolved through autowiring-resolution (origin-agnostic: the same `ResolveCtx` could pull a native, test-double, or WASM-module bean). The config struct itself is a registered bean (so it can hold injected state / shared fields the methods read via `&self`); methods take `&self` plus autowired params. Bean name = method name by default (bean-naming); return type = bean type (collection-injection / candidate-resolver match on it); `#[bean(scope=…, init=…, destroy=…, primary, lazy, order=…)]` and `#[conditional(...)]` map straight onto definition metadata. CRUCIALLY: intra-config calls are simply not how you wire — and because the macro can SEE the method bodies it can lint/hard-error if a `@Bean` fn body calls another `@Bean` fn on `&self` (the thin-macro stays honest: it emits a `compile_error!` with the exact rewrite hint 'take `repo: &Repo` as a parameter instead', turning Spring's silent lite-mode footgun into a loud compile diagnostic Spring never had). Full-mode is thus not 'lost' — it is rendered UNNECESSARY because the only correct wiring is parameter injection, which is always singleton-correct by construction.

**Pros:** Sidesteps the CGLIB-has-no-Rust-analogue clash entirely by adopting the model Spring itself recommends — zero proxy/interception machinery, smallest possible mechanism (DX #1 via simplicity; low-overhead #2 trivially: no subclass, no runtime method routing).; Singleton-correctness is structural: a parameter is resolved ONCE through autowiring-resolution to the managed singleton, so the 'second unmanaged instance' bug Spring's CGLIB exists to prevent is impossible here — the intent (inter-factory refs yield the managed bean) is met by the wiring model, not by interception.; Best AOT/native posture (the lineage Spring's lite mode and `@AutoConfiguration` chase): typed factory fns are fully monomorphizable, no `final`/`private` restrictions, no GraalVM hostility analogue — squarely serves the compile-vs-runtime split leaning toward build-time.; The macro can turn Spring's most notorious lite-mode footgun (silently calling `beanTwo()` and getting a fresh instance) into a precise compile_error with a rewrite hint — strictly better diagnostics (§2.9) than Spring, because leaf's macro CAN see the body Spring's bytecode enhancer treats opaquely.; Thinnest macro: one `RawBeanDefinition` seed per method + a param-resolving closure, all hand-writable against public APIs (§2.10) — `cargo expand` shows exactly the factory you'd write yourself.

**Cons:** Drops a real (if discouraged) Spring affordance: the ergonomic `new BeanOne(beanTwo())` style that reads like plain Java is simply unavailable — a porting-friction and teachability cost for users who learned full mode as the default.; Pushes ALL wiring into parameter lists; a config method needing many collaborators gets a long signature (Spring full mode let you call helpers freely) — though this is exactly the discipline lite mode enforces.; The 'lint intra-config calls' guarantee is only as good as the macro's body inspection: a call routed through a helper fn or a trait method the macro can't statically see escapes the lint, re-opening a narrow silent-footgun window (mitigated, not eliminated).; If a config genuinely wants a private intra-class helper that BUILDS part of a bean (not a managed bean, just a sub-step), the macro must distinguish 'helper fn' from '`@Bean` fn' cleanly so it doesn't false-positive the lint — a small authoring-rule surface.; Forecloses, at the feature level, any future where leaf DOES want full-mode-style sugar — though nothing stops Phase 2 from adding R2/R3 on top later.

**Mechanisms considered:** proc-macro emits one thin `RawBeanDefinition` seed per `#[bean]` fn (bean-definition substrate); no full-mode path at all; each fn parameter → an autowiring-resolution injection point resolved via an origin-agnostic `ResolveCtx` (native/test/WASM-module indistinguishable); `&self` config bean is itself a registered bean so methods can read shared injected/field state; macro body-inspection LINT: `compile_error!` on an intra-config `@Bean`→`@Bean` call with a 'use a parameter' rewrite hint (turns Spring's silent footgun loud); bean metadata (`scope/init/destroy/primary/fallback/lazy/order/qualifiers/conditional`) as attribute args mapped onto the definition; destroy-method INFERENCE policy decision (auto close()/shutdown() vs explicit) surfaced as an attribute, defaulting to EXPLICIT to avoid Spring's silent-teardown trap

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Substrate-neutral: the macro emits the SAME `RawBeanDefinition` seeds whether collected via linkme distributed-slice (Arch A/B), build.rs codegen (Arch C), or explicit `with()` (Arch D) — `@Bean` methods are just more contributors to the one descriptor stream, no special path. Contributing crates depend only on leaf-core (where `RawBeanDefinition`/`Factory`/`ResolveCtx`/`Role` live); the emitted seed uses absolute paths (`::leaf_core::RawBeanDefinition{..}`). A `@Configuration` impl in a downstream/integration crate contributes its `@Bean` definitions exactly like any component, so this is the natural Rust home for library-supplied `@Bean @Fallback` defaults (primary-fallback) across crate boundaries. Inherits the Layer-0 silent-DCE hazard identically: a config crate the binary never path-references contributes ZERO `@Bean` definitions and the features they back silently vanish — the mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found definitions per source crate, fail loud) is the defense, and it must count `@Bean`-derived definitions too. Generics can't register (no `'static` symbol/TypeId until instantiated) → macro hard-errors on a generic `@Bean` fn or a generic config impl, offering a per-instantiation `register_bean!(ConcreteType)` shim. The two-source duality applies cleanly: the static link-time registry contributes native `@Bean` definitions; an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source could contribute definitions whose `Factory` bridges into the module — both feed ONE definition stream, CANDIDATES not a decision. No proxy/interception machinery means nothing extra to make origin-agnostic.

**T2 — execution context:** Two phases under refresh-lifecycle. (1) DEFINITION phase, cold/single-threaded around main: the `@Bean`-derived `RawBeanDefinition` seeds are registered (configuration-classes is the marquee BDRPP-analogue per post-processor-spi — it ADDS definitions before any other definition-edit runs, so e.g. placeholder resolution can act on `@Bean`-defined beans); no instances yet, the macro-emitted seeds are pure data. (2) INSTANTIATION phase (bean-instantiation drives it): each `@Bean` Factory is invoked async — `async fn` `@Bean` methods are first-class (DataSource/Pool construction genuinely awaits IO), parameters resolved via autowiring-resolution through `ResolveCtx` (which may itself await constructing collaborators), all inside the per-bean creation guard (never a global lock, §2.5). A `@Bean` fn MUST NOT block the executor (blocking construction → spawn_blocking, execution-context discipline; Phase 2 owns propagation). The config `&self` bean is constructed first (it's an ordinary bean); singletons are eager-instantiated (fail-fast at boot). Errors are rich: a `@Bean` factory returning `Err` aborts that bean's eager build all-or-nothing, with a diagnostic naming the config impl + method + the param that failed to resolve, folded into the assembly chain (§2.9). Because the Factory is a boxed-future fn-pointer at the dyn boundary (RPITIT/AFIT not dyn-safe), there's an alloc per construction — cold/cheap for singletons, a Phase-2 hot-path concern for prototype/scoped `@Bean`s. No async Drop: a `@Bean` with `destroy=` participates in context-close's explicit `shutdown().await` in reverse dependency order, not Drop; cancellation of an in-flight `@Bean` future unwinds the partially-built bean out of the creation set.

#### R2 — Two authoring SHAPES sharing one factory substrate: lite = free fns / `&self` methods; full = a typed `BeanCtx` handle methods call to fetch managed singletons (explicit, no proxy)
Honor BOTH modes' INTENT but realize full mode WITHOUT interception: replace CGLIB's invisible rerouting of `self.beanTwo()` with a VISIBLE, typed container handle the method calls. Lite shape is R1 (parameter injection). Full shape changes the `@Bean` method signature so intra-config references go through a context object instead of a self-call: `#[configuration(full)] impl AppConfig { #[bean] fn bean_two(&self, _: &BeanCtx) -> BeanTwo { BeanTwo::new() } #[bean] fn bean_one(&self, cx: &BeanCtx) -> BeanOne { BeanOne::new(cx.bean::<BeanTwo>()) } }` — `cx.bean::<BeanTwo>()` consults the bean-registry singleton cache and returns the MANAGED instance (creating it on miss), exactly Spring full mode's 'consult factory, run body only on miss' semantics, but as an explicit method call with no magic. The macro still emits one `RawBeanDefinition` per method; the difference is the Factory closure threads a `&BeanCtx` (a thin façade over `ResolveCtx`/the engine's singleton cache, origin-agnostic) into the method, and full-mode `@Bean` methods are REQUIRED (by macro signature rule) to take `cx: &BeanCtx` to fetch collaborators rather than calling sibling methods. `proxyBeanMethods`-equivalent becomes `#[configuration(full)]` vs `#[configuration]` (lite default), preserving Spring's per-class intent-declaration. The teaching parity holds: full mode is for 'I want to express construction as code that references other managed beans'; lite is 'pure parameter wiring.' The full-mode singleton-routing is achieved because `cx.bean::<T>()` is THE managed-singleton lookup — the same guarantee CGLIB gives, made explicit. Reentrancy/cycles during a full-mode method's `cx.bean()` call ride the same early-reference/creation-guard machinery as ordinary resolution (circular-references).

**Pros:** Faithfully preserves the FULL-vs-LITE user-facing distinction and Spring's per-class intent-declaration (`#[configuration(full)]` ≈ proxyBeanMethods=true) — highest teachability for Spring users; the mental model 'a @Bean ref yields the managed singleton' survives.; Realizes full-mode's guarantee with ZERO interception/proxy machinery — `cx.bean::<T>()` is an explicit, honest, debuggable lookup; no CGLIB, no subclassing, no `final`/`private` restriction analogue, no GraalVM-hostility — the intent without the JVM mechanism (intent-parity §2.2).; One shared factory substrate: both shapes emit the SAME `RawBeanDefinition` + boxed Factory; the only delta is whether the closure threads a `&BeanCtx` — so full/lite is a thin authoring variation over one mechanism (unification §2.11), not two subsystems.; Makes the cost VISIBLE and opt-in exactly as Spring intends: lite has no `cx` param and pays nothing; full threads a context handle — the author consciously chooses, and there's no silent fabrication of a second instance because `cx.bean()` always returns the managed one.; `BeanCtx` is a clean origin-agnostic seam: `cx.bean::<T>()` could resolve a native, test-double, or WASM-module bean identically, and it reuses the bean-registry singleton cache rather than inventing a parallel one.

**Cons:** The full-mode ergonomic prize is only PARTLY recovered: `cx.bean::<BeanTwo>()` does not read as cleanly as Spring's `beanTwo()` (the whole reason CGLIB exists was to make it read like plain Java) — so leaf's full mode is more honest but less 'magical', a DX trade.; Introduces a second authoring shape and a `BeanCtx` capability surface (what can you call on it? only `bean::<T>()`, or also `bean_named`, optional/provider lookups?) — more concepts than R1's single shape, cutting against simplicity-as-DX.; `cx.bean::<T>()` inside a full-mode method is a RUNTIME resolution mid-construction, so it must integrate with the creation guard and cycle detection (circular-references); a full-mode method that does `cx.bean::<Self-product>()` or forms a cycle needs the same early-reference story the rest of the container has — coupling this feature to the (undecided) cycle/early-ref design.; Two return-type/typing rules to specify (lite param-injected vs full cx-threaded) and a macro rule that full-mode methods may NOT self-call siblings (must use `cx`) — an authoring-rule surface and a lint to enforce it.; Threading `&BeanCtx` makes the `@Bean` method aware of the container (mild IoC leak — the method now references a leaf type), which lite mode and Spring's parameter-injection style deliberately avoid; some users will see it as less pure than R1.

**Mechanisms considered:** two authoring shapes over ONE factory substrate: lite (param-injected, R1) + full (`&BeanCtx`-threaded); `#[configuration(full)]` vs `#[configuration]` (lite default) as the proxyBeanMethods-equivalent per-class intent declaration; `BeanCtx::bean::<T>()` = explicit managed-singleton lookup over the bean-registry cache (origin-agnostic; reuses, not duplicates, resolution); macro signature rule: full-mode `@Bean` methods take `cx: &BeanCtx`; macro lints/forbids intra-config sibling self-calls in full mode; full-mode `cx.bean()` reentrancy rides the existing per-bean creation guard + early-reference path (circular-references), not a bespoke cache; both shapes emit identical `RawBeanDefinition` seeds; only the Factory closure's body differs (threads cx or not)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same descriptor-stream neutrality as R1 (linkme/codegen/explicit all emit identical seeds; `@Bean` methods are ordinary contributors). The added cross-crate surface is `BeanCtx` itself: it lives in leaf-core (the minimal, ultra-stable registration/resolution ABI the macro hard-codes paths to), so a full-mode config in any crate threads the same `&BeanCtx`. Because `cx.bean::<T>()` resolves against the live registry at construction time, a full-mode config in crate A can reference a managed bean contributed by crate B with no compile-time coupling beyond the type — natural cross-crate inter-bean wiring. Inherits the Layer-0 DCE hazard identically (a dropped config crate → missing definitions, silent), so the same expected-vs-found self-check applies; the self-check should also surface that a full-mode config's `cx.bean::<T>()` target type was never registered (turning a would-be runtime no-candidate into an earlier, richer diagnostic where possible). Generics still can't register (macro hard-error + concrete shim). The origin-agnostic `BeanCtx` means a WASM-module-contributed bean is fetchable via `cx.bean()` indistinguishably from a native one; the two-source duality (static link-time registry + optional dynamic WASM-module source) feeds the one registry `BeanCtx` reads — CANDIDATES, not a decision.

**T2 — execution context:** Definition phase identical to R1 (cold, single-threaded, configuration-classes adds `@Bean` defs as the BDRPP-analogue before other definition edits). Instantiation phase: lite `@Bean` factories behave as R1. FULL-mode factories differ in execution context: when a full-mode method calls `cx.bean::<T>()`, that is a (possibly async) RESOLUTION happening MID-CONSTRUCTION of the calling bean — it runs inside the calling bean's creation guard and may itself await constructing `T` (recursively, through bean-instantiation). This is the key T2 subtlety: a full-mode `@Bean` fn is not a leaf in the construction graph but an interior node that triggers further resolution, so cancellation of the outer construction must unwind any inner `cx.bean()`-triggered partial builds, and a cycle reached via `cx.bean()` must hit the same early-reference/`BeanCurrentlyInCreation`-analogue path (circular-references), never deadlock or spin (reactive, not poll, §2.4). `cx.bean()` returning a managed singleton is a cache read (cheap) on a hit; on a miss it constructs (async). Still no global lock; still boxed-future Factories at the dyn edge. A full-mode method that performs the `cx.bean()` lookup synchronously over an already-cached singleton is the hot, cheap case; one that triggers async construction is the cold case. Errors from `cx.bean::<T>()` (no candidate, ambiguous, construction failed) propagate out of the full-mode factory as that bean's construction error, richly attributed (config + method + requested type). No async Drop; destroy hooks via context-close as in R1.

#### R3 — Build-time PLAN expansion: `@Configuration` is a compile/codegen-time grouping that lowers each `@Bean` into a first-class definition with statically-resolved inter-factory edges; no runtime config object
Question whether `@Configuration` needs to be a runtime BEAN at all, or whether it is purely a COMPILE-TIME ORGANIZING construct. Spring makes the config a managed bean because the JVM discovers and enhances it reflectively at runtime; leaf has a codegen seam (charter §3) and can LOWER the whole config class at build/plan time. The macro/codegen layer reads the `#[configuration]` impl and emits, into the assembly plan, one fully-formed bean definition PER `@Bean` method — with the config grouping dissolved away (no runtime `AppConfig` instance unless a method actually needs shared state, in which case the shared state becomes its own small bean). Inter-`@Bean` references are resolved AT PLAN TIME into explicit dependency EDGES: a full-mode-style `bean_one() { BeanOne::new(bean_two()) }` is recognized by the codegen as 'bean_one depends on the managed bean_two' and lowered to a factory that receives the managed `bean_two` as an injected input — so the full-mode singleton guarantee is delivered by STATIC GRAPH ANALYSIS, not runtime interception OR an explicit `cx` handle. Lite mode is the same lowering without the intra-reference recognition (params only). The config class becomes, in effect, a NAMESPACE the codegen flattens; `@Bean` definitions are emitted as if hand-written `#[bean]` free functions with their dependency edges pre-computed. This is the AOT-extreme: the inter-factory edges that Spring computes at runtime via CGLIB are computed at build time and frozen into the plan, surfacing unsatisfiable references (a `@Bean` referencing a type no bean produces) as a BUILD/plan-validation error — the earliest, richest diagnostic.

**Pros:** Most AOT-faithful and lowest-overhead: inter-factory edges are frozen at build/plan time, so there's no runtime config bean, no `cx` handle, no interception, and the full-mode guarantee is a property of the generated graph (best fit for the compile-vs-runtime split leaning build-time; serves §2.4/§2.5 — nothing extra on the instance path).; Earliest-richest diagnostic (§2.9): a `@Bean` that references a type no bean produces, or forms an unsatisfiable inter-factory cycle, fails at a dedicated plan-validation pass BEFORE any instance — strictly earlier than R1/R2's runtime resolution; the codegen can name the exact method and the missing producer.; Delivers full-mode's 'inter-factory ref = managed singleton' INTENT with neither CGLIB nor an explicit lookup handle — the cleanest realization of the intent (the reference just IS an edge to the managed bean), arguably the truest intent-parity (§2.2) of the three.; Dissolving the config into per-`@Bean` definitions unifies `@Bean` with component beans at the definition level (one kind of definition in the plan), and aligns with programmatic-registration's AOT-analyzable lineage — the config grouping is sugar the plan erases (unification §2.11).; No `final`/`private` analogue, no GraalVM hostility, no runtime config-object lifecycle to manage — the cost Spring's full mode imposes is simply absent.

**Cons:** PRE-DECIDES the metadata/codegen boundary and the compile-vs-runtime split — both explicit Phase-2 keystones (§3); presenting build-time edge-resolution as THE shape biases that signal, so it must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, not a leaning.; Static recognition of an 'inter-factory reference' is fragile: the codegen must reliably detect that `bean_two()` inside `bean_one`'s body means 'the managed bean_two' — but a reference routed through a variable, a helper, a closure, or a trait method is opaque to static analysis, so the recognition is partial and the rest must fall back to params (re-introducing an authoring rule and a potential silent gap).; Loses runtime dynamism Spring's full mode quietly allows (a `@Bean` body doing conditional/imperative construction that references siblings under runtime branches) — build-time edge extraction can't see runtime branches, so such configs must be rewritten as params or programmatic-registration.; Config classes that genuinely need shared MUTABLE/injected state across methods (Spring's `@Autowired` config fields) don't dissolve cleanly — the shared state must be reified as its own bean and threaded, complicating the 'config is just a namespace' story.; Heaviest codegen and most macro/plan logic of the three (must parse bodies, build edges, validate the graph) — in tension with thin-macros (§2.10) UNLESS the heavy logic lives in a normal leaf-codegen crate the macro merely invokes (which the charter does allow); still the most machinery to specify and test.; If Phase 2 chooses a runtime-dominant resolution model, this realization's build-time edge-freezing is largely wasted — it's the most coupled to an undecided meta-architecture call.

**Mechanisms considered:** build/codegen-time lowering of each `#[bean]` method into a first-class plan definition; config grouping dissolved to a namespace; static extraction of intra-config references into explicit dependency EDGES (full-mode guarantee via graph analysis, no runtime interception/handle); plan-validation pass that fails at build time on an unsatisfiable inter-factory reference or cycle (earliest diagnostic); shared config state reified as its own small bean when methods need it; otherwise no runtime config object; heavy edge-extraction/validation logic in a normal leaf-codegen crate (keeps the proc-macro thin per §2.10); fallback to parameter injection when a body reference is not statically recognizable (partial recognition, explicit rule)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Strongest fit for the build-time-codegen substrate (Arch C, sqlx model): the codegen walks the resolved config impls and emits explicit per-`@Bean` definitions + their edges, sidestepping the link-time DCE layers entirely for `@Bean` definitions authored in crates the codegen knows about. BUT cross-crate inter-factory edges are the hard case: a `@Bean` in crate A referencing a managed bean PRODUCED in crate B cannot be statically edge-resolved by A's macro (a proc-macro sees only its own invocation; build.rs sees only its own crate) — so cross-crate references MUST fall back to a runtime/param resolution by TYPE (the edge is 'needs a bean of type T', resolved at assembly from the whole-binary descriptor stream), and only INTRA-crate, intra-config references can be frozen at build time. This is the central T1 limitation of R3 and a Phase-2 question. leaf-core hosts the definition/plan ABI; leaf-codegen owns the lowering; the binary/app-root force-links contributing config crates and runs the plan-validation + anti-DCE self-check together (a missing producer for an inter-factory edge becomes a loud plan-time error with provenance). Generics still can't register (hard-error). The dynamic WASM-module source has NO build-time presence, so any `@Bean` edge to a WASM-module bean can ONLY be a runtime/type-resolved edge — flagged as a tension with the freeze-at-build shape (CANDIDATE, not a decision).

**T2 — execution context:** Plan/lowering/validation is SYNCHRONOUS cold-path at build or startup-validation time, single-threaded, around (or before) main: the codegen produces definitions and intra-crate edges as pure data; the only async is the later instantiation. Because inter-factory edges are pre-resolved (intra-crate) or type-resolved (cross-crate), the INSTANCE phase carries no runtime config object and no interception cost — each `@Bean` Factory runs async during bean-instantiation with its inputs already wired by edge, inside the per-bean creation guard, never blocking the executor (spawn_blocking for blocking construction). A statically-frozen intra-config edge means the managed `bean_two` is constructed (async, once) and handed to `bean_one`'s factory as an input — the singleton guarantee with zero runtime lookup. Cross-crate type-resolved edges run as ordinary autowiring-resolution at construction (R1-like). Errors split by timing: unsatisfiable INTRA-crate edges and cycles fail at the cold plan-validation pass (earliest, richest — names method + missing producer); cross-crate no-candidate failures surface at construction, attributed to the `@Bean` + requested type. Boxed-future Factories at the dyn edge as in R1/R2 (alloc per construction; cold for singletons). No async Drop → destroy hooks via context-close. Cancellation unwinds a partially-built bean; since there's no interior `cx.bean()` reentrancy (edges are inputs), the unwind graph is simpler than R2's.

### Rust clashes
- CGLIB subclass interception has NO Rust analogue — full mode's entire mechanism is generating a runtime subclass of the user's `@Configuration` class that OVERRIDES each `@Bean` method to consult the factory first. Rust cannot subclass a user struct, cannot override a user's inherent method, and a plain method call `self.bean_two()` inside a `@Bean` body is STATICALLY resolved by the compiler — no proxy, vtable, or enhancer can intercept it. So 'inter-bean method calls return the managed singleton' cannot be replicated by interception at all. The realizations diverge precisely on this: R1 designs the need away (parameter injection is always singleton-correct, the model Spring itself recommends), R2 replaces the invisible reroute with an explicit `cx.bean::<T>()` handle, R3 freezes the inter-factory reference into a static dependency edge at build time. None proxies a method call, because nothing can.
- `@Configuration` as a managed runtime bean vs a compile-time grouping — Spring makes the config a `@Component`-meta-annotated managed bean because it's discovered and CGLIB-enhanced reflectively at runtime. In Rust there's no reason the grouping must survive to runtime: the config can be a runtime bean holding shared `&self` state (R1/R2) OR a pure compile/codegen-time namespace the plan dissolves into per-`@Bean` definitions (R3). The 'is the config object alive at runtime?' question has no forced answer and trades runtime shared-state ergonomics against AOT cleanliness — and it pre-touches the metadata/codegen boundary (§3), so it stays a candidate axis, not a decision.
- Reflective factory-method invocation vs a typed factory closure — Spring invokes a `@Bean` method reflectively (`factoryBeanName`+`factoryMethodName`) and autowires its parameters by runtime type-walk. Rust has no reflective invocation: the macro must emit a typed `Factory` closure (bean-definition's recipe handle) that calls the concrete fn and resolves each parameter through autowiring-resolution's `ResolveCtx`. This is mostly a clean win (typed, monomorphizable), but it means a `@Bean` fn's parameters become injection points the MACRO must wire at emit time — and the closure is a boxed-future fn-pointer at the dyn boundary (RPITIT/AFIT aren't dyn-safe), an alloc per construction (cold for singletons, a Phase-2 hot-path concern for prototype/scoped `@Bean`s).
- Async `@Bean` factories vs Spring's synchronous reflective instantiation — leaf is async-first, so a `@Bean` fn is naturally `async` (a DataSource/Pool/client genuinely awaits IO during construction). Spring instantiates synchronously. This is an improvement, but it forces the execution-context discipline (§2.3): a `@Bean` factory may `.await` but MUST NOT block the executor (blocking construction → spawn_blocking), and in R2 a full-mode method's `cx.bean::<T>()` is an async resolution happening MID-construction of the calling bean — an interior node that can trigger recursive async construction, cancellation unwinding, and cycle detection, unlike Spring's synchronous self-call.
- The `final`/`private`-method restriction footgun simply doesn't transfer — Spring's full mode forbids `final`/`private` `@Bean` methods because CGLIB can't override them, and silently breaks interception otherwise. Since leaf has no subclassing, there is no such restriction in R1/R2/R3; the corresponding leaf concern flips to the opposite end: leaf's macro CAN see method bodies, so it can turn Spring's silent lite-mode footgun (calling a sibling `@Bean` and getting a fresh instance) into a LOUD compile_error — but only for references it can statically recognize (a reference through a variable/helper/trait-method may escape detection), so the 'no silent second instance' guarantee is structural in R1 (params can't fabricate) but only best-effort where body-inspection is involved.
- No runtime type-walk for parameter autowiring — Spring resolves `@Bean` method parameters by walking the live bean population by type/qualifier. Rust has no such walk; parameter resolution must go through autowiring-resolution keyed on concrete TypeIds from the descriptor stream. Generic `@Bean` fns or generic config impls have no `'static` symbol/TypeId until instantiated, so the macro must HARD-ERROR on them with a `register_bean!(ConcreteType)` per-instantiation shim — Spring's open-generic `@Bean` methods (resolved via ResolvableType) have no direct analogue.
- Destroy-method INFERENCE is a silent-teardown trap that should NOT be ported as-is — Spring's `@Bean` auto-infers a public `close()`/`shutdown()` as the destroy callback, silently tearing down pools/clients (and a documented trap for resources Spring doesn't own, needing `destroyMethod=""`). In Rust there's no async Drop, so teardown is already explicit via context-close's `shutdown().await`; replicating Spring's silent inference would fight the rich-diagnostics invariant. The leaf-native stance is to make destroy EXPLICIT by default (an attribute), surfacing 'this bean has no registered teardown' rather than silently calling a `close()` the author didn't intend — an intent-parity divergence from Spring's mechanism.
- Cross-crate inter-factory references can't be statically edge-resolved (R3-specific) — a proc-macro sees only its own invocation and build.rs sees only its own crate, so a `@Bean` in crate A referencing a managed bean PRODUCED in crate B cannot have its edge frozen at build time; it must degrade to a runtime type-resolved edge over the whole-binary descriptor stream. Spring's runtime classpath makes all inter-bean references uniform; leaf's lack of a build-time classpath splits 'intra-crate (statically resolvable) vs cross-crate (runtime-resolved)' references — a real asymmetry the AOT-extreme realization must live with.

### Interactions
- **bean-definition** — Each `@Bean` method LOWERS to exactly one `BeanDefinition` whose `Factory` is the typed closure the macro emits over the fn — the construction recipe is a `@Bean` definition's reason to exist. The return type becomes the produced TypeId (declare the MOST CONCRETE type so candidate-resolver/collection-injection match it; the getObjectType/produced-type-vs-defining-type distinction from bean-definition applies directly). All `@Bean` metadata (scope/lazy/init/destroy/primary/fallback/order/qualifiers) are definition fields. This feature is the marquee PRODUCER of definitions that are NOT component-scanned classes.
- **post-processor-spi** — configuration-classes IS the highest-precedence definition-registry processor (the ConfigurationClassPostProcessor / BDRPP analogue): it parses `@Configuration`/`@Bean` and ADDS the derived definitions during the registry-edit phase, strictly BEFORE other definition-edit processors run, so e.g. value-injection's placeholder resolution can act on `@Bean`-defined beans. The 'static `@Bean` methods for post-processors' Spring rule (a `@Bean` producing a BFPP/BPP must be instantiable very early without forcing the config's full init) maps to: a `@Bean` that PRODUCES a post-processor must be a dependency-light factory the engine can run during the front-loaded processor-instantiation step.
- **autowiring-resolution** — `@Bean` method PARAMETERS are injection points resolved by autowiring-resolution's fail-fast layered policy (type → generics → qualifier → primary/fallback → name) through the `ResolveCtx`. This is THE wiring mechanism for lite mode (parameters are constructor-injection-equivalent) and the universal correct default; in R2 full mode's `cx.bean::<T>()` also routes through resolution. Lite mode's 'collaborators MUST be parameters' rule is exactly 'every collaborator is an autowiring-resolution injection point.'
- **import-composition** — Sibling feature in the same area: `@Import` composes `@Configuration` classes (and selectors/registrars) — it is how configs pull in other configs. configuration-classes provides the `@Bean`-bearing config unit that import-composition arranges/orders/defers; the `@Enable*`-via-`@Import`+ImportAware backbone reads attributes off the importing config. The two are designed together: this feature = the config unit + its `@Bean` factories; import-composition = composing units at four altitudes.
- **conditions** — `@Bean @Conditional`/`@ConditionalOnMissingBean` gates whether a `@Bean` definition is registered at all (two-phase parse-vs-register). The Spring 'OnClass safety on `@Bean` methods' sharp edge (the method's param/return types load before a method-level class-condition runs, requiring hoisting onto a nested config) is a JVM-loading artifact leaf likely SHEDS (no class-loading-on-reference), but the parse-vs-register gating itself is core: a false condition = no `@Bean` definition, surfacing later as a no-candidate via candidate-resolver. condition-report must explain a backed-off `@Bean`.
- **auto-configuration** — `@AutoConfiguration` classes are `@Configuration(proxyBeanMethods=false)` — i.e. ALWAYS lite — full of `@Bean @ConditionalOnMissingBean` factories that back off in favor of user beans. This feature provides the lite `@Bean` factory model auto-configuration is built on; the 'framework code is lite-only, models exemplary parameter-injection' intent means leaf's auto-config equivalent should also be lite-only (R1's model is the natural fit), reinforcing parameter injection ecosystem-wide.
- **programmatic-registration** — The BeanRegistrar functional contract is the imperative/looping/conditional ALTERNATIVE to declarative `@Bean` methods (Spring's AOT-friendly replacement for hand-rolled BDRPP/registrar). Where a `@Bean` method is one-bean-per-method declarative, programmatic-registration mints definitions in loops/branches via the same registration API + instance-supplier (= the same `Factory` handle). R3's build-time lowering and programmatic-registration share the AOT-analyzable lineage; both write the same definition shape.
- **bean-naming** — A `@Bean` method's name defaults to the METHOD name (decapitalized class name is for components); `#[bean(name=["a","b"])]` supports multiple aliases with the first canonical. Collisions (two `@Bean`s, or a `@Bean` and a component, claiming a name) are loud override/conflict errors per bean-naming's contract, not silent shadowing.
- **scopes** — `#[bean(scope=…)]` sets the produced bean's scope (singleton/prototype/request/custom via the Scope SPI); `@Scope` proxyMode/scoped-proxy interplay carries over. A prototype `@Bean` means the Factory runs per resolution (and the boxed-future alloc-per-construction becomes a hot-path concern, unlike a singleton `@Bean` run once).
- **lifecycle-callbacks** — `#[bean(init=…, destroy=…)]` name init/destroy callbacks; `@PostConstruct`/`@PreDestroy`/InitializingBean/DisposableBean/Aware all work on `@Bean`-produced beans. The destroy-method INFERENCE footgun (auto close()/shutdown()) is a deliberate leaf divergence (explicit-by-default) since teardown is already explicit via context-close (no async Drop).
- **factory-bean** — Conceptual neighbour: factory-bean is a bean that programmatically produces ANOTHER bean (the product is what consumers resolve), with the `&` dereference escape hatch. A `@Bean` method is the lighter, annotation-driven 'factory method' form of the same 'developer writes the construction' idea — both produce a managed bean whose producing-vs-produced types may differ (the produced-type metadata from bean-definition serves both).
- **component-stereotypes** — `@Configuration` IS a `@Component` (its only added power is opting `@Bean` methods into full mode); `@Bean` inside a plain `@Component` is always lite. This feature and component-stereotypes are the two bean-DECLARATION styles: `@Component` = 'container instantiates this class', `@Bean` = 'this method is a developer-written factory' — different ownership models, both producing definitions. component-scanning discovers the config class as a candidate.
- **primary-fallback** — `#[bean(primary)]` / `#[bean(fallback)]` flags ride the produced definition as autowire tie-breakers; `@Bean @Fallback` is the canonical way a LIBRARY ships a default that a user's `@Bean` (in another crate) transparently supersedes — a key cross-crate pattern this feature enables. Note Spring's `@Priority`-can't-annotate-`@Bean` quirk → leaf expresses ordering intent via `#[bean(order=…)]` + primary/fallback.
- **value-injection** — `@Bean` method parameters can be `${placeholder}`/`#{expr}` value injections (not just bean refs), resolved at the injection point with type conversion. Because configuration-classes runs as the highest-precedence definition processor, value-injection's placeholder resolution acts on `@Bean`-defined beans afterward — the BDRPP-before-BFPP ordering (post-processor-spi) exists precisely so `${...}` inside `@Bean`-defined beans resolves.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Does leaf reproduce full-mode's 'inter-factory reference yields the managed singleton' guarantee AT ALL, and if so HOW — lite-only (R1: design the need away, the model Spring itself recommends), an explicit `cx.bean::<T>()` handle (R2: intent without interception, mild IoC leak), or build-time edge-resolution (R3: AOT-extreme, partial static recognition)? Since Rust cannot intercept a method call, there is no faithful CGLIB analogue; this is a genuine intent-vs-affordance call that cross-cuts the proxy/AOP story (none of which can reroute a Rust self-call) and the compile-vs-runtime split.
- Is `@Configuration` a RUNTIME managed bean (holding shared `&self`/injected state, R1/R2) or a pure COMPILE/CODEGEN-TIME grouping the plan dissolves into per-`@Bean` definitions (R3)? This pre-touches the metadata/codegen boundary (§3) and the compile-vs-runtime split, and determines whether config-shared-state ergonomics (Spring's `@Autowired` config fields) survive or must be reified as their own bean. Cross-cuts component-stereotypes (config-as-component) and programmatic-registration.
- How much of `@Bean` wiring resolves at BUILD/plan time vs runtime (§3 compile-vs-runtime)? R3 freezes intra-crate inter-factory edges and validates the graph at a plan-validation pass (earliest-richest diagnostic, fewest runtime hops); R1/R2 resolve `@Bean` parameters at runtime via autowiring-resolution. The diagnostic timing (§2.9), the alloc-per-construction cost, and whether unsatisfiable inter-factory references fail at build vs runtime all hinge here — and it interacts with the conditional strategy and the registry substrate.
- Cross-crate inter-factory references (R3-critical, but general): a `@Bean` in crate A referencing a managed bean PRODUCED in crate B cannot be statically edge-resolved (proc-macro/build.rs see only their own crate), so such edges must degrade to runtime type-resolution over the whole-binary descriptor stream while intra-crate edges could freeze at build time. How is this intra-vs-cross-crate asymmetry expressed, and does it confuse the user model? Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model and bean-definition's Factory ABI.
- What is the alloc/boxing standard for `@Bean` Factories on the construction path? The Factory must be dyn-storable and origin-agnostic (native/test/WASM-module), but RPITIT/AFIT aren't dyn-safe → boxed-future fn-pointer, an alloc per construction. Cold/cheap for singleton `@Bean`s; a real cost for prototype/scoped `@Bean`s run repeatedly. Is the standard boxed-future-at-the-dyn-edge, or a monomorphized fast path for hot prototype/scoped factories? The async-execution-model decision (§3) viewed through `@Bean` construction.
- Destroy-method INFERENCE: does leaf port Spring's auto-detect-`close()`/`shutdown()` (convenient but a silent-teardown trap Spring documents) or make `@Bean` teardown EXPLICIT by default (surfacing 'no registered destroy' rather than silently calling close())? Since leaf has no async Drop and teardown is already explicit via context-close, the leaf-native leaning is explicit-by-default — but that is an intent-parity divergence to ratify, and it cross-cuts lifecycle-callbacks and context-close.
- How is the full-vs-lite INTENT-DECLARATION surfaced if full mode is realized differently (or not at all)? Spring's `proxyBeanMethods=true/false` is a conscious per-class opt-in/out of an expensive feature. R1 has no full mode (one shape), R2 uses `#[configuration(full)]`, R3 makes it a static property of the plan. Whether leaf KEEPS a user-facing full/lite distinction at all — and what it MEANS when the mechanism isn't proxying — is a DX call cross-cutting auto-configuration (which is lite-only by design).
- The two-source duality for `@Bean` definitions: the static link-time registry (default 'classpath') contributes native `@Bean` definitions; an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source could contribute definitions whose Factory bridges into the module. But R3's build-time edge-freezing has NO build-time presence for WASM-module beans (their edges can only be runtime/type-resolved), while R1/R2 accommodate them naturally. How the dynamic source reconciles with any build-time lowering is unresolved — a candidate, not a decision.
- The anti-DCE self-check for `@Bean` definitions specifically: a dropped config crate yields zero `@Bean` definitions and the features they back silently vanish (the worst-case 'plain BeanFactory' symptom for an unintended reason). What counts a config's expected `@Bean` definitions, and (R2/R3) how does the self-check surface a missing PRODUCER for an inter-factory reference as an early rich diagnostic rather than a runtime no-candidate? Does the manifest differ across linkme vs codegen vs explicit substrates?

### Notes
Confidence: high on intent. I read the dedicated section twice ('@Configuration: full mode and the CGLIB illusion' 978-992, lite mode 994-1009, @Bean method semantics 1011-1019 incl. the destroy-INFERENCE / static-@Bean-for-post-processors / field-injection-forces-early-init hidden concepts, @Bean-vs-@Component 1021-1025, and the full-vs-lite dogfood note 934-936). I confirmed the marquee mechanic precisely: full mode = CGLIB-subclass overriding each @Bean method to consult the factory first so a nested self-call returns the MANAGED singleton (the 'reads like plain Java but is still singleton-correct' illusion); lite mode = plain factory method, NO inter-bean method calls at all, collaborators MUST be autowired parameters; @AutoConfiguration hardwires lite (1186-1188); proxyBeanMethods is the per-class intent declaration. I grounded the single deepest clash — CGLIB has no Rust analogue because a `self.bean_two()` call is statically resolved and uninterceptable — against the nightly doc (RPITIT/AFIT not dyn-safe → boxed-future Factory at the dyn edge 160-182; no async Drop as a first-class constraint 273-281; const TypeId/Any backbone) and the cross-crate doc (Layer-0/A/B silent-DCE 135-152, self-check mandate 152/345/360, linkme-default + thin-const-descriptor + ordering-as-data 165-171, Architectures A/B/C/D 277-337, generics-cannot-register, proc-macro/build.rs single-crate-scope walls 62-102). T2 against charter §2.3 async-first/explicit-execution-context, §2.4 reactive-hot/poll-cold, §2.5 no-global-lock/minimal-boxing, §2.9 rich-early diagnostics, §2.10 thin-macros/escape-hatch, §2.11 unification.

The three realizations are genuinely divergent on the axis that matters for THIS feature — WHETHER and HOW to realize full-mode's inter-factory singleton guarantee given no interception primitive exists: R1 = lite-only canonical, the need DESIGNED OUT (parameter injection is always singleton-correct, exactly Spring's own best practice; the macro can even turn Spring's silent lite footgun into a loud compile_error) — smallest mechanism, best AOT, but drops the read-like-plain-Java affordance; R2 = two authoring shapes over one factory substrate, full mode realized via an explicit `cx.bean::<T>()` handle that consults the singleton cache (intent without proxy, mild IoC leak, couples to the cycle/early-ref story because cx.bean() is a mid-construction resolution); R3 = build-time PLAN lowering that dissolves the config to per-@Bean definitions and freezes intra-config references into static dependency EDGES (AOT-extreme, earliest diagnostics, truest intent-parity for the guarantee — but pre-decides the codegen/compile-vs-runtime boundary and only intra-crate references can be statically resolved). R1 vs R2 differ on no-full-mode-vs-explicit-handle; R3 differs on runtime-vs-build-time edge resolution.

Things I deliberately did NOT decide (held as Phase-2 questions): whether full mode exists at all and how; whether @Configuration is a runtime bean or a compile-time grouping; how much @Bean wiring is build-time vs runtime; the intra-vs-cross-crate edge-resolution asymmetry; the boxed-future-vs-monomorphized Factory standard for hot prototype/scoped @Beans; whether to port the destroy-method INFERENCE footgun (I lean leaf-native explicit-by-default, flagged for ratification); how the full/lite intent-declaration surfaces; the two-source (link-time + WASM-module) duality vs a build-time-freeze shape; and the @Bean-specific anti-DCE self-check. Every realization keeps the Factory ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a @Bean's Factory and R2's cx.bean() resolve native/test-double/WASM-module beans identically) and emits thin descriptor seeds the macro could route through linkme/codegen/explicit (Arch A/B/C/D). I built concretely on the two provided upstream designs: bean-definition (each @Bean = one RawBeanDefinition with a typed Factory; produced-vs-defining type; metadata fields) and post-processor-spi (configuration-classes is the highest-precedence BDRPP-analogue adding definitions before other definition-edits; the static-@Bean-for-post-processors rule maps to dependency-light early-instantiable processor factories).

Naming ('#[configuration]', '#[bean]', 'BeanCtx', 'ResolveCtx', 'RawBeanDefinition', 'Factory', full/lite) is Phase-1 placeholder. I wrote no files. Relevant grounded source paths (all absolute): /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md (978-1025 the feature section incl. full/lite/CGLIB-illusion + @Bean semantics + hidden concepts; 934-936 full-vs-lite dogfood; 1186-1188 @AutoConfiguration-is-lite rationale; 924/932 ConfigurationClassPostProcessor as HIGHEST_PRECEDENCE BDRPP; 1011-1019 destroy-inference/static-@Bean/field-injection-early-init; 743 @Priority-cant-annotate-@Bean); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-14-leaf-charter-design.md (invariants §2, deferred keystones §3, topology §6); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md (135-171 DCE layers + linkme-default + thin-descriptor + ordering-as-data + self-check; 277-362 Architectures A-D + hard constraints + scope-discovery-not-global); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md (160-182 RPITIT/AFIT-not-dyn-safe; 258-281 dyn+Send boxing + no async Drop; 81 const TypeId/Any backbone).

## @Import Family & Configuration Composition  `[import-composition]`

Spring's `@Import` is the single seam through which configuration COMPOSES, deliberately layered into FOUR ALTITUDES so a contributor plugs in at exactly the decision-point its problem needs, without forcing everyone down to the most opaque mechanism: (1) IMPORT A CONFIG/COMPONENT CLASS — pull another `@Configuration`/`@Component` in directly, registering its bean definitions (the recursive composition primitive; configuration-classes is the unit being composed); (2) `ImportSelector` — `selectImports(AnnotationMetadata) -> String[]` returns config-class NAMES to import, evaluated IMMEDIATELY during the parse pass ('which configs, decided from the importer's metadata, early'); (3) `DeferredImportSelector` — same shape but DEFERRED until ALL user `@Configuration` is parsed, with a `Group` (`getImportGroup()`) that COLLECTS candidates across every selector sharing that group and returns ONE merged, de-duplicated, `@Order`-sorted batch ('which configs, decided after seeing the user's whole config, merged/ordered GLOBALLY across dozens of contributors' — this is literally the engine behind Boot's `AutoConfigurationImportSelector`); (4) `ImportBeanDefinitionRegistrar` — `registerBeanDefinitions(metadata, registry, nameGen)` for fully imperative, hand-minted `BeanDefinition`s below the `@Bean`-method level (the explicit escape hatch). Crowning the whole family is `ImportAware`: an imported config receives `setImportMetadata(AnnotationMetadata)` — the metadata of the class that IMPORTED it — so it can read attributes the importer declared. This is THE backbone of every `@Enable*` annotation: `@EnableScheduling`/`@EnableTransactionManagement`/`@EnableAsync` are 'just sugar over `@Import` + metadata introspection' — the imported config reads the importer's proxy-mode/attribute knobs and wires itself accordingly, with NO special 'enable' machinery, avoiding globals/thread-locals. Three hidden intents matter: (a) DEFERRAL EXISTS FOR `@Conditional` CORRECTNESS, NOT PERFORMANCE — deferring guarantees `@ConditionalOnMissingBean` on imported/auto-config sees the FINAL set of user beans so it can back off (it only looks like a scheduling tweak); (b) selectors/registrars get container handles (`Environment`/`BeanFactory`/`ClassLoader`/`ResourceLoader`) via either `*Aware` callbacks (which fire BEFORE `registerBeanDefinitions`) or single-constructor injection; (c) a registrar may NOT register a BDRPP (it already runs after the BDRPP phase — too late). v7 also makes `@Import` on INTERFACES implemented by a config honored, and Spring 7 adds `BeanRegistrar` (a functional `register(BeanRegistry, Environment)` imported via `@Import`, the AOT-friendly modern successor to `ImportBeanDefinitionRegistrar`/BDRPP with an instance-supplier `.supplier(ctx -> ...)` model, also `ImportAware`-capable). leaf must replicate the INTENT — composition at graded altitudes, GLOBAL deferred-conditional-batch merging/ordering as the auto-config backbone, and importer-metadata-driven `@Enable*` feature toggles — WITHOUT the JVM mechanism it rests on: a runtime classpath, reflective class-name resolution (`selectImports` returns STRINGS resolved against the classloader), and runtime annotation-metadata walking. The deep question is which altitudes survive as distinct constructs versus collapsing into leaf's single cross-crate descriptor-contribution stream, since 'import a class to register its definitions' is, in Rust, mostly what link-time/build-time contribution already does.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Import-as-edges over the unified descriptor stream: `@Import` declares CONTRIBUTOR EDGES + a typed `EnableConfig<A>` carries importer attributes; deferral/grouping is a runtime BATCH phase
Treat `@Import` not as 'fetch and parse another class' (Spring's classpath idiom) but as DECLARING A DEPENDENCY EDGE between contributors over leaf's one descriptor stream (the same stream configuration-classes' `#[bean]` seeds and component-scan feed). Each altitude becomes a thin annotation the macro lowers to descriptor metadata, NOT a separate subsystem:

Altitude 1 (import a config): `#[configuration] #[import(DbConfig, MetricsConfig)] struct AppConfig;` — the macro emits, alongside AppConfig's own bean seeds, an `ImportEdge { from: TypeId<AppConfig>, to: &[TypeId<DbConfig>, TypeId<MetricsConfig>] }` descriptor. At assembly the engine ensures every transitively-imported config's seeds are INCLUDED in the active set and de-duplicated by TypeId (idempotent diamond imports). No class-name strings, no reflective resolution — the importee is a real type the importer path-references, which ALSO solves Layer-0 DCE for that edge for free (the `use`-reference is implied by naming the type).

Altitude 2 (immediate selector): `#[import_selector(MySelector)]` where `trait ImportSelector { fn select(&self, meta: &ImportMetadata) -> Vec<ImportRef>; }` runs during the (cold, single-threaded) parse/plan phase and returns typed `ImportRef`s (a TypeId or a registered marker), evaluated immediately. `ImportRef` is a closed enum over the binary's registered configs — the macro turns the user's referenced types into the closed set, so there is no 'resolve this string' step.

Altitude 3 (deferred + group): `#[deferred_import_selector(group = AutoConfigGroup)] impl ...` — deferred selectors do NOT contribute during the first pass; instead they register into a named GROUP. The engine runs a single DEFERRED BATCH PHASE after all eager configs+user beans are in the definition set: each group's selectors are collected, the group's `merge(&[Entry]) -> Vec<Entry>` de-dups + topo-sorts (ordering-as-DATA on each entry, never link order — directly serves auto-config-ordering and auto-configuration's 'back off after user config' correctness intent).

Altitude 4 (registrar): `trait ImportRegistrar { fn register(&self, reg: &mut DefinitionRegistry, meta: &ImportMetadata, env: &Environment); }` — the imperative escape hatch, mints `RawBeanDefinition`s by hand (shares programmatic-registration's API), with a macro lint forbidding registering a definition-phase post-processor from inside it (Spring's 'registrar can't register a BDRPP' rule made a loud compile/plan error).

ImportAware / `@Enable*`: instead of a stringly `setImportMetadata`, the importer's attributes are a TYPED struct. `#[derive(EnableAttrs)] struct EnableScheduling { pool_size: usize }` and the imported config receives `EnableConfig<EnableScheduling>` (the importer's attribute values) as an injectable / a parameter to its selector/registrar — so `@Enable*` is 'a typed attribute struct + an import edge', the rust-native form of 'sugar over @Import + metadata introspection', with attributes checked at compile time instead of read reflectively.

**Pros:** Maximal UNIFICATION (§2.11): all four altitudes are thin metadata over the ONE descriptor stream configuration-classes/component-scanning already feed — `@Import` adds edges + a runtime batch phase, not four subsystems. The engine has a single 'active definition set' assembled from edges + selectors + groups.; Typed importer metadata (`EnableConfig<A>`) replaces Spring's stringly `setImportMetadata` reflection — `@Enable*` knobs are compile-checked, autocompleted, and refactor-safe, strictly better DX (§2.1) and richer diagnostics (§2.9) than reading attributes off `AnnotationMetadata` at runtime.; Import edges naming real TYPES path-reference the importee, so altitude-1 composition SOLVES Layer-0 DCE for imported configs for free (the importer crate references the importee type) — no extra force-link needed for the import graph itself; the anti-DCE self-check only has to cover ENTRY-point configs.; Deferral/grouping is realized as an explicit runtime BATCH PHASE with ordering-as-data + topo-sort — faithfully reproduces the deferral-for-conditional-correctness intent (§ the hidden 'correctness not performance' concept) and is exactly the seam auto-configuration / auto-config-ordering plug into.; Thin macros (§2.10): each altitude lowers to a hand-writable descriptor (`ImportEdge`, a registered selector/registrar impl, a group tag) — `cargo expand` shows the edge and the trait impl you could have written; the heavy merge/topo logic lives in a normal engine crate, not the macro.

**Cons:** Does NOT support Spring's open `selectImports` returning arbitrary runtime-decided class NAMES (a string the classloader resolves) — `ImportRef` must be a CLOSED set of types the binary already links, so a selector that wants to pull in a config decided purely from a runtime string (e.g. a property value naming a class) has no analogue; that dynamism must be reframed as conditions over a pre-registered candidate set.; Four altitudes still means four annotation surfaces + two traits (`ImportSelector`, `ImportRegistrar`) + a group concept — more concepts to teach than a pure 'just contribute' model (R2), even though they share one stream underneath.; The deferred BATCH PHASE is a distinct lifecycle step the engine must run between definition-assembly and instantiation, coupling this feature to refresh-lifecycle's phase ordering and to the (Phase-2-undecided) conditional strategy — when conditions are evaluated relative to the batch determines correctness.; `EnableConfig<A>` requires the importer's attribute struct to be a registered, type-keyed value threaded to the importee — a small new injection kind (importer-metadata injection) distinct from ordinary bean injection, with its own resolution rule (whose importer's attrs, if a config is imported by two importers?).; Import edges across crates (config in crate A imports config in crate B) are statically resolvable (A references B's type), but a deferred selector contributed by crate C that wants to merge into a group DEFINED in crate A still rides the link-time-collection DCE hazard like any contributor — the unification doesn't erase that for the selector-discovery path.

**Mechanisms considered:** proc-macro lowers each altitude to thin descriptors over the SHARED stream: `#[import(...)]` -> `ImportEdge{from,to:&[TypeId]}`; selector/registrar -> registered trait-object descriptors; group -> a named-group tag; closed-set `ImportRef` enum (TypeId / registered marker) instead of Spring's open class-name strings — no reflective name resolution; runtime DEFERRED BATCH PHASE in the engine: collect group selectors after eager assembly, `Group::merge` de-dups + topo-sorts via ordering-as-DATA (never link order) — the auto-config backbone; typed `EnableConfig<A>` importer-attribute struct threaded to the importee (replaces stringly `setImportMetadata`); `@Enable*` = attribute struct + import edge; link-time distributed-slice (default 'classpath') for discovering selectors/registrars/groups PLUS optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source contributing import edges/definitions — CANDIDATES, both feed the one active set; macro lint: registrar may not register a definition-phase post-processor (Spring's BDRPP rule -> loud compile/plan error); `*Aware`-vs-constructor handle access collapses to ordinary parameter/handle injection on the selector/registrar

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Substrate-neutral over the same descriptor stream as configuration-classes: `#[import]` edges, selector/registrar impls, and group tags are thin descriptors emitted identically whether collected via linkme distributed-slice (Arch A/B), build.rs codegen (Arch C), or explicit `with()` (Arch D). KEY T1 WIN: an altitude-1 import names a real importee TYPE, which path-references it, so the import GRAPH is largely immune to Layer-0 DCE — importing crate A's config pulls in crate B's importee by reference (this is the rust-native analogue of Spring's '@Import a class' being inherently safe). The residual DCE hazard is for DISCOVERY of selectors/registrars/groups contributed by a crate the binary never path-references (the classic 'registration-only crate vanishes' Layer-0 trap) and for ENTRY-point configs — the mandated expected-vs-found anti-DCE self-check (count import edges, registered selectors, group members per source crate; fail loud) must cover these. The deferred-GROUP merge is the natural home for cross-crate global ordering: dozens of crates each contribute deferred selectors into one group, merged/de-duped/topo-sorted in a single pass — exactly how auto-configuration assembles a coherent batch from many crates. Cross-crate constraint: a group must be DEFINED in a crate both contributor and consumer depend on (typically leaf-core or a shared crate), since the group tag is a type/marker contributors reference — contributors depend UP onto where the group lives (the inward-dependency rule). Generics can't register (a generic config/selector has no '`static` TypeId until instantiated) -> macro hard-errors with a `register_import!(ConcreteType)` shim. Two-source duality applies: the static link-time slice is the default 'classpath' of importable configs/selectors; an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source could contribute import edges or whole configs whose definitions bridge into the module — both feed ONE active set; CANDIDATE, not a decision. `ImportRef` being a closed set of LINKED types is what makes leaf's 'classpath' honest: you can only import what is actually on the link/codegen graph, surfaced early rather than as a runtime ClassNotFound.

**T2 — execution context:** Three execution phases under refresh-lifecycle, all import-PLANNING is COLD/single-threaded around (or before) main; only the eventual bean construction is async/hot. (1) EAGER PARSE/PLAN phase: altitude-1 import edges are walked to compute the transitive active config set (de-dup by TypeId, diamond-safe); immediate `ImportSelector::select` runs here, pure/synchronous, returning typed `ImportRef`s — no IO, no blocking, no async (a selector that needs IO is a design smell; it observes plan state and the Environment and votes, mirroring the read-mostly ConditionContext discipline). (2) DEFERRED BATCH phase: after ALL eager configs + user definitions are in the set, each named group collects its deferred selectors and runs `Group::merge` — synchronous, deterministic, ordering-as-data topo-sort with explicit CYCLE DETECTION emitting a rich diagnostic ('import/auto-config cycle A -> B -> A' naming the contributors). This phase is WHERE deferral buys `@Conditional` correctness: conditions on deferred/auto-config definitions are evaluated against the now-complete user-definition set so `OnMissingBean` backs off correctly. ImportRegistrar::register runs here too, mutating the DefinitionRegistry — synchronous, no instances yet, may read Environment but MUST NOT block or do IO (it mints definitions, not objects). (3) INSTANTIATION: unchanged from configuration-classes — the assembled definitions' async Factories run under per-bean creation guards (never a global lock §2.5), boxed-future at the dyn edge. Errors: an unresolvable import edge (importee type not in the active set), an ambiguous group merge, or a registrar violation fails at the COLD plan/batch phase — the earliest, richest point (§2.9), naming the importer, the altitude, and the offending edge — strictly before any async construction. `EnableConfig<A>` attribute values are frozen plan-time data, read by selectors/registrars/the importee with no runtime metadata walk. Cancellation only matters in phase 3 (construction); the planning phases are short, synchronous, and pre-runtime, so there is nothing to cancel there.

#### R2 — Composition by PLAIN CONTRIBUTION: collapse altitudes 1-3 into the descriptor stream; keep only a typed `Enable<A>` feature-toggle + a `BeanRegistrar`-style imperative hook (no Selector/Group subsystem)
Lean on the deepest rustClash as a SIMPLIFICATION: Spring needs four altitudes because the JVM discovers config reflectively over a classpath and `selectImports` must return STRINGS resolved late; leaf has no runtime classpath — discovery IS link-time/build-time contribution. So DISSOLVE most of the family.

Altitude 1 (import a config) -> just CONTRIBUTE. A config in any crate is already a contributor to the one stream (configuration-classes); 'importing' it is making the binary reference its crate (the scan!/enable! list, the honest analogue of `@ComponentScan basePackages`/the starter list). There is no separate `@Import(OtherConfig)` mechanism for 'register its definitions' — that's what contribution already does. Optional grouping sugar `#[bundle] struct WebStack(DbConfig, MetricsConfig);` is pure ergonomics that re-exports a set of contributors, lowering to the same seeds.

Altitude 2/3 (selectors + deferred groups) -> there is NO 'return class names to import' construct, because every candidate config is ALREADY contributed; the only real question a selector answered is 'should this candidate be ACTIVE?', which is a CONDITION (conditions / condition-family). So deferred-selector + group merging collapses into: all auto-config-style candidates are contributed but GATED by conditions, and the engine's single conditional-evaluation pass (run after user definitions, for back-off correctness) + ordering-as-data IS the 'deferred batch'. No `ImportSelector`/`DeferredImportSelector`/`Group` types at all — the 'which configs activate, decided after seeing the whole config, merged/ordered globally' intent is delivered by (conditions over the whole contributed set) + (auto-config-ordering's topo-sort), which leaf needs ANYWAY.

Altitude 4 (imperative registration) -> KEEP, as the one explicit programmatic hook, unified with programmatic-registration: `trait Registrar { fn register(&self, reg: &mut DefinitionRegistry, env: &Environment); }` for loops/branches/multiple-bean minting — Spring 7's own `BeanRegistrar` direction (the modern, AOT-friendly successor that DEPRECATES `ImportBeanDefinitionRegistrar`).

`@Enable*` / ImportAware -> a typed `Enable<A>` toggle: `#[enable] struct EnableScheduling { pool_size: usize }` ACTIVATES the scheduling feature's contributed (conditional) configs AND carries the typed attributes the feature reads via `Enable<EnableScheduling>` injection. So '@Enable* is sugar over @Import + metadata' becomes '@Enable* is a typed activation toggle that gates a feature's contributors and supplies their attributes' — same intent, no selector/registrar machinery.

**Pros:** Smallest possible mechanism and biggest unification (§2.11, §2.1): three of four altitudes EVAPORATE into 'contribute + condition + order' — primitives leaf already builds for component-scanning, conditions, and auto-config-ordering — so import-composition adds almost no new surface. Fewest concepts to teach.; Most HONEST about Rust reality: there is no classpath, so 'import to register definitions' and 'return class names to import' are reframed as what link/build-time contribution already does, plus runtime conditions — directly the intent-not-mechanism invariant (§2.2) and the cross-crate doc's 'scope discovery, don't make it global; conditions decide what DOES wire' guidance.; `Enable<A>` is a typed, compile-checked feature toggle — better DX and diagnostics than Spring's reflective attribute reading, and it cleanly expresses the `@Enable*` family (the feature's whole reason for being) without any 'enable machinery'.; Keeping exactly ONE imperative hook (`Registrar`, = programmatic-registration / Spring 7 `BeanRegistrar`) follows Spring's OWN modernization (BeanRegistrar deprecates ImportBeanDefinitionRegistrar) and is the AOT-analyzable instance-supplier shape — aligns with the compile-vs-runtime lineage.; No deferred-Selector/Group subsystem to specify, order, or make origin-agnostic — the deferral-for-correctness intent is satisfied by the conditional pass leaf must run regardless, so this feature stops being a distinct lifecycle subsystem.

**Cons:** Sheds the EXPLICIT four-altitude vocabulary Spring users know — there is no `ImportSelector`/`DeferredImportSelector`/`Group` to port, so a Spring user looking for 'where do I write my selector' finds 'contribute the configs and gate them with conditions' instead; a teachability/porting-friction cost and a parity-surface judgment call.; Folds the 'decide which configs from importer metadata' decision entirely into CONDITIONS — if a real use case needs to choose among candidates by a computation richer than a predicate (Spring's `selectImports` can run arbitrary logic returning a dynamic list), it must be expressed either as a `Registrar` (imperative) or as a richer condition, which may be awkward — the selector's expressive middle ground is gone.; Risks UNDER-powering: by asserting 'selectors are just conditions', it pre-judges that no genuine import-time-computation altitude is needed — but that is partly a Phase-2 conditional-strategy question; if conditions turn out to be pure cfg/predicate with no import-time compute, some selector use cases have no home.; The 'deferred batch = the conditional pass' equivalence tightly couples this feature's correctness to WHEN conditions run relative to definition assembly (the undecided conditional strategy) — if conditions are partly compile-time (cfg), the 'back off after seeing all user beans' guarantee needs careful design to preserve.; Cross-crate ACTIVATION of a feature's contributors via `Enable<A>` still needs the contributors to be on the link/codegen graph (Layer-0) — `Enable<A>` gates ACTIVE-ness but cannot conjure a crate that was never referenced; the enable!/force-link discipline and anti-DCE self-check remain mandatory, just as in R1.

**Mechanisms considered:** dissolve altitude-1 import into ordinary cross-crate CONTRIBUTION (the enable!/scan! crate list = the honest @ComponentScan-basePackages analogue); optional `#[bundle]` re-export sugar; dissolve altitudes 2/3 (selectors + deferred groups) into CONDITIONS over the whole contributed candidate set + auto-config-ordering's topo-sort — no Selector/Group types; keep ONE imperative hook = `Registrar` unified with programmatic-registration (Spring 7 BeanRegistrar direction; instance-supplier, AOT-analyzable); typed `Enable<A>` activation toggle that gates a feature's conditional contributors AND supplies their attributes (the `@Enable*`/ImportAware replacement); single conditional-evaluation pass run AFTER user definitions for back-off correctness (delivers the deferral-for-correctness intent without a deferred-selector subsystem); link-time slice / build-time codegen / explicit `with()` all feed the one contributed candidate set; optional dynamic WASM-module source contributes candidates too — CANDIDATES not a decision

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This realization is the cleanest mapping of Spring's `@Import` onto Rust's actual cross-crate model: 'composition' IS contribution to the descriptor stream, so the cross-crate story is identical to component-scanning/configuration-classes — contributors depend UP onto leaf-core, the binary force-links via the enable!/scan! list (the explicit opt-in the cross-crate doc endorses as the predictable, non-global default), and the anti-DCE self-check counts contributed configs per crate. Because there is NO Selector/Group discovery subsystem, there is one FEWER link-time-collected kind to worry about than R1 — only the candidate configs themselves and `Registrar`s are collected. `Enable<A>` activation is a runtime gate over already-linked contributors: turning a feature on is making the binary link the feature crate (a `dep:`-hidden umbrella feature, Spring-starter analogue) AND setting `Enable<EnableX>` — both required; a feature flag alone compiles registrations but does not force linkage (the cfg-gates-compilation-not-linkage trap), so the self-check must warn when an enabled feature contributed ZERO candidates. The deferred-global-ordering need (dozens of crates' auto-configs as one coherent batch) is met by auto-config-ordering's topo-sort over the whole contributed set, not a per-import group — strictly simpler cross-crate. Generics still can't register (hard-error + concrete shim). Two-source duality: the static link-time/codegen set is the default 'classpath' of candidate configs; an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source contributes additional candidates (gated by the same conditions) — CANDIDATE. The honest limit: leaf cannot 'discover' a config in a crate the build never references; like Spring's basePackages, discovery is SCOPED to what the app opts in — which this realization makes explicit rather than pretending at a global classpath.

**T2 — execution context:** Two cold planning sub-phases + the usual async instantiation, fewer moving parts than R1. (1) ASSEMBLY: the contributed candidate set is gathered (link-time slice / codegen / explicit) — pure data, single-threaded, around main. (2) CONDITIONAL/ORDERING pass: conditions are evaluated over the WHOLE candidate set AFTER user definitions are present (the back-off-correctness guarantee), then auto-config-ordering topo-sorts the survivors with cycle detection (rich diagnostic on a cycle). `Enable<A>` toggles are read here as plan-time data to gate feature contributors and freeze their attribute values. `Registrar::register` runs in this phase: synchronous, mutates the DefinitionRegistry, may read Environment, MUST NOT block/IO/async (mints definitions, not instances) — and a lint forbids it from registering a definition-phase post-processor (Spring's BDRPP rule).
