Each member declares its `Phase` as a CONST associated with its ConditionId (OnFeature/OnProperty/OnResource = Parse; OnBean/OnMissingBean/OnSingleCandidate = Register), so the SPI's two-pass planner phases them correctly with no author action. SearchStrategy (CURRENT/ANCESTORS/ALL) is an attribute the OnBean family reads to scope its hierarchy-aware registry query. OnSingleCandidate's verdict is delegated to the autowiring-resolution/candidate-resolver primitive ('would by-type resolution succeed?'), not reimplemented. Booleans are themselves catalog members (`AnyOf`/`AllOf`/`NoneOf` Conditions taking a slice of child ConditionIds+attrs), recursively evaluated. The family crate populates the ConditionId->Condition registry the SPI resolves against at startup.

**Pros:** Maximally faithful to Spring's 'thin shells over one SPI' intent (#2): every On-X is a tiny impl + tiny macro; adding OnJndi/OnCheckpointRestore later is just one more impl+id, no engine change — best DX for FAMILY authors.; Clean separation of concerns: the family crate owns ONLY the per-kind predicate logic + attribute schemas; the SPI owns evaluation/phasing/report-threading. Each impl is independently unit-testable against a mock ConditionContext (no container, no macro) — strong testability and thin-macro (#10) compliance.; Origin-agnostic by construction: because every member is a runtime predicate over the collected descriptor table, a definition contributed by a static link-time crate OR a future dynamic/WASM source is gated by the SAME OnProperty/OnBean impl — no member assumes native construction.; Rich diagnostics for free (#9): each impl writes a kind-specific reason ('OnProperty x.enabled: found value "false", expected "true"'; 'OnMissingBean(Foo): found 1 existing bean named bar'), and condition-report records it with no extra author work; a miss is a graceful no-bean, never an error.; Booleans-as-members keeps conceptual economy — AnyOf/AllOf/NoneOf are ordinary catalog entries reusing the same evaluate path, so the nested-helper boilerplate Spring forces (subclass AnyNestedCondition) disappears.

**Cons:** OnClass/OnMissingClass cannot be honestly expressed as a pure runtime impl: a linked Rust type is ALWAYS present, so OnFeatureCondition can only test a capability/cfg fact, which must be CAPTURED into a descriptor at compile time (a feature/cfg the family macro reads) — so this realization alone is incomplete for the OnClass sub-intent and must lean on the cfg tier for that one member family.; Every member pays a cold-path runtime evaluation cost per guarded definition; auto-config has hundreds of candidates, so the catalog relies on the SPI's cheap-Parse-prune to stay within low-overhead (#2) — a large flat table of OnProperty/OnFeature probes is bounded but non-trivial.; The ConditionId->impl registry is a second cross-crate discovery surface inheriting the DCE/Layer-0 hazard: if the family crate isn't force-linked, the built-in OnProperty impl silently fails to register and EVERY @on_property either always-passes or always-fails — must be self-checked at startup (assert the expected built-ins resolved).; Attribute schemas are stringly/loosely typed in the descriptor (Attr::Str/Attr::Bool slices), so a typo like `having_valeu=` is only caught when the impl reads attrs (startup) unless the member macro validates its own known keys — pushes a validation burden into each thin macro.; Per-member macros multiply the macro surface (one `#[on_property]`, one `#[on_bean]`, ...); without a shared attribute-parsing helper this risks drift in how each parses/spans/errors.

**Mechanisms considered:** per-member concrete `Condition` impl in a normal `leaf-conditions` family crate, addressed by stable `ConditionId`; thin per-member attribute macro emitting a const `ConditionEntry{id, attrs}` onto the annotation-model descriptor; Phase declared as a const property of each ConditionId (Parse vs Register) so the SPI planner phases members automatically; OnFeature as the cfg/feature-captured OnClass analogue (descriptor records a compile-time capability fact); OnSingleCandidate delegating to autowiring-resolution's 'would resolve unambiguously' check rather than counting beans; AnyOf/AllOf/NoneOf as ordinary catalog members for nested booleans; family crate populating the ConditionId->Condition registry (linkme slice default; inventory only if a member needs a non-const value); startup self-check on expected built-ins

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Two cross-crate surfaces, both inheriting the doc's hazards. (a) The condition ENTRIES ride the SAME descriptor table as the components/definitions they gate (no separate channel) — origin-agnostic const data carried on the annotation-model descriptor, default link-time `linkme` slice + optional dynamic/WASM source. (b) The ConditionId->Condition IMPLEMENTATION registry that the family crate populates is its own discovery surface: the family crate must be force-linked (Layer-0: `use leaf_conditions as _;` from the generated app-root, or the umbrella re-exporting it) or the built-ins vanish and a startup self-check (expected-built-in-count assertion) must fire — an empty condition registry is the silent-failure trap. The `ConditionId` constants and the `Attr`/`ConditionEntry`/`Phase` ABI live in `leaf-core` (ultra-stable, emitted code hard-codes absolute paths). OnFeature is the cfg-coupled member: the family macro reads which capability features are active in THIS crate, but per the cross-crate doc a feature gates COMPILATION not LINK retention, so OnFeature's 'present' verdict must agree with the binary's final resolved feature set (documented to differ between `-p` and `--workspace`, resolver=3 required to avoid dev/build features leaking). Generics: a guard on `Foo<T>` has no symbol, so the member macro hard-errors or demands per-instantiation registration (same limit as component discovery). Ordering across crates is by declared Phase data, never section/constructor order.

**T2 — execution context:** Strictly COLD-PATH. Every member's `matches` runs inside the registration planner during refresh-lifecycle bring-up, AFTER the Environment is sealed and (for Register members) after all definitions are collected, but BEFORE any eager singleton is built and before any bean future is spawned. Members are SYNCHRONOUS by SPI contract: OnProperty/OnBean/OnResource/OnFeature are pure reads over already-materialized snapshots (PropertyResolver, registry view, capability set) — no `.await`, no blocking (an OnResource that wanted to stat a network path is disallowed; it reads the resource-loader's already-resolved view). OnExpression is the sharp edge: it must NOT trigger bean construction (Spring's 'referencing a bean forces very early init' hazard) — leaf forbids the member from resolving live beans, restricting it to the read-mostly context. Cancellation: the planner phase is a bounded, non-cancellable cold step. Errors: a member returns a graceful no-match-with-reason for a normal miss; a structural fault (malformed attrs, unresolved ConditionId) is aggregated into the startup validation diagnostic (#9) BEFORE wiring proceeds — never a panic, never async cancellation. Register members observe a documented happens-before (full definition set known) so OnMissingBean's back-off answer is stable.

#### R2 — Tiered family: each On-X declares an 'earliest-decidable tier' so the SAME annotation resolves cfg/build-time when possible and runtime otherwise (the family as the seam over R2/R1 SPI tiers)
Rather than make every member a runtime impl (R1) or push everything static, classify the FAMILY by Spring's own intent and bind each kind to its rust-native earliest-decidable tier — making condition-family the concrete realization of the SPI's static/runtime seam (R2+R1). Three tiers, declared per ConditionId in the kernel so all macros agree: TIER-CFG (compile-time fact) — OnClass/OnMissingClass map to `#[cfg(feature="redis")]`/`cfg(...)`; the family macro emits the guarded definition's descriptor INSIDE a cfg attribute so an absent optional dependency is physically removed from compilation (the cleanest rust-native 'read without loading' — naming a missing capability can never error). OnWarDeployment/some OnCloudPlatform/OnThreading-target facts that are knowable from target cfg also live here. TIER-BUILD (build-time const-fold) — conditions whose inputs are knowable at build time (a fixed build-config value, `cfg(target_arch)` for a platform OnCloudPlatform) fold to a `const MATCHED: bool` via leaf-codegen and the descriptor is emitted under `if const { MATCHED }`. TIER-RUNTIME — everything decided by live state (OnBean/OnMissingBean/OnSingleCandidate needing the registry, OnProperty/OnBooleanProperty over runtime-overlaid env, OnProfile, OnResource over a runtime resource view, runtime OnCloudPlatform) stays a runtime Condition impl exactly as R1. The family macro for each member consults the kernel tier-map and chooses cfg-emit vs const-fold vs runtime-defer; the AUTHORING syntax is identical (`#[on_class(...)]` always looks the same) so DX is uniform while the realization varies by kind. A single member can even be split: `OnClass` gates the nested config at cfg-tier while `OnMissingBean` inside it stays runtime — exactly Spring's recommended 'nested @Configuration guarded by OnClass with @Bean @ConditionalOnMissingBean inside' pattern, realized natively.

**Pros:** Directly realizes Spring's two-phase performance intent the rust-native way: cfg-tier members are PRUNED FROM THE BINARY (zero runtime cost, the strongest possible low-overhead #2), mirroring Boot's build-time spring-autoconfigure-metadata pre-filter that discards most candidates before the expensive parse.; Strongest, most honest 'read without loading' (#5/intent) for OnClass: cfg-gating physically removes the absent optional-dependency type, so naming it can never cause a build/link error — a cleaner guarantee than Spring's ASM trick and it eliminates DCE-on-unused-registration for gated-out items (they don't exist).; Earliest, richest diagnostics for the static members (#9): a misspelled feature or an impossible `cfg(all(a, not(a)))` OnClass is a COMPILE error with a span; the family can `compile_error!` on a statically-contradictory guard — beating Spring's runtime no-match.; Encodes the family's design knowledge where it belongs: the per-kind tier-map IS the statement 'OnClass is a build fact, OnBean is a runtime fact', which is the acid-test mapping Phase 2 must get right; this realization makes that mapping a first-class, reviewable artifact.; Realizes Spring's recommended nesting pattern natively (OnClass-at-cfg guarding a config whose inner OnMissingBean is runtime), so the family composes across tiers within ONE element without the author thinking about tiers.

**Cons:** Two evaluation LOCATIONS per the family (compile-time cfg/const vs runtime planner) doubles the mental model and the places a 'why did/didn't this register' answer comes from — must be reconciled into ONE condition-report view (some entries 'gated out at compile time', some 'no-match at startup') to stay accountable.; cfg-as-condition collides with Cargo feature semantics: features only OR-on, can't be un-set, and a sibling test/example can flip an OnClass-feature on for a binary that never asked (unification) — so ONLY genuinely additive capability-presence conditions fit TIER-CFG; any 'backend A xor B' MUST stay TIER-RUNTIME/profile, a discipline the family must enforce (and document) per member.; cfg gating compilation does NOT force LINK retention (Layer 0): a cfg-true OnClass member must ALSO trigger the force-link of the integration crate, coupling condition-family to the discovery-substrate decision in a way R1 avoids — the cfg verdict and the force-link must be kept consistent or the gated-in registration silently vanishes.; build.rs/codegen sees only its OWN crate (no sibling visibility), so TIER-BUILD members are limited to local + target-cfg + build-config inputs; they CANNOT answer cross-crate questions ('is bean X defined elsewhere') — that is structurally TIER-RUNTIME, so the tier-map must be conservative or it will mis-promote a member.; The tier classification is a design commitment baked into the kernel ABI; getting a kind's tier wrong (e.g. assuming OnCloudPlatform is always build-time when some platforms are only detectable at runtime) forces an ABI-affecting reclassification later — higher change cost than R1's uniform-runtime treatment.

**Mechanisms considered:** per-ConditionId 'earliest-decidable tier' map (CFG/BUILD/RUNTIME) living in the kernel so all family macros agree; TIER-CFG: family macro emits the descriptor under `#[cfg(feature=...)]`/`cfg(...)` (OnClass = capability/integration-crate compiled in); TIER-BUILD: leaf-codegen/build.rs folds build-knowable predicates into `const MATCHED: bool` + inline `const {}` guard (target-cfg OnCloudPlatform/OnThreading); TIER-RUNTIME: R1-style runtime Condition impls for OnBean/OnProperty/OnProfile/OnResource and runtime-detected platform facts; identical authoring syntax across tiers; macro picks emit-strategy from the tier-map; `compile_error!` on statically-contradictory cfg-tier guards; explicit cfg-true => force-link coupling so a gated-in registration is actually linked; native realization of Spring's nested OnClass-config + inner-OnMissingBean pattern across tiers

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The realization MOST entangled with T1. TIER-CFG leans on Cargo features+cfg: a feature gates whether a family member's descriptor is compiled, but per the doc this does NOT guarantee linkage, so a cfg-true OnClass must be paired with the binary-level force-link (`use leaf_redis as _;`) the discovery substrate emits — otherwise empty-registry trap. resolver=3 is mandatory so a sibling/test/build feature doesn't flip a cfg-tier member on for a production binary that never asked (feature unification correctness variable, documented to differ between `-p` and `--workspace`). TIER-BUILD's build.rs sees only its own crate + `CARGO_CFG_*` target cfgs, never sibling identities, so build-folded members are local+target+build-config only — 'is bean X defined in another crate' is structurally TIER-RUNTIME. The per-kind tier-map MUST live in the `leaf-core` ABI so macros across the workspace classify identically; TIER-RUNTIME members ride the same descriptor table + ConditionId->impl registry as R1 (same DCE/Layer-0/self-check obligations). wasm/embedded targets (no reliable link sections) push more of the family toward TIER-CFG/TIER-BUILD (the doc's Architecture C), making this the more portable substrate there — but the runtime members still need the codegen-emitted explicit-registration fallback. Generics: a cfg-tier guard on a generic item still needs a concrete per-instantiation shim; the macro hard-errors otherwise.

**T2 — execution context:** Split across compile/build-time and cold runtime. TIER-CFG members are decided at COMPILATION (no executor, nothing async) — the guarded descriptor is simply present or absent; the only failure surface is `compile_error!`/`cargo::error` for unknown features or contradictions (#9, earliest possible). TIER-BUILD members are const-folded in leaf-codegen/build.rs (host process, cold one-shot, no async). TIER-RUNTIME members behave exactly as R1: synchronous reads in the registration planner on the cold refresh-lifecycle path, Register members held to the second pass after the full definition set exists, no `.await`/no blocking, graceful no-match for misses, structural faults aggregated into the startup validation diagnostic. Cancellation: none of the tiers expose a cancellation surface (compile-time has none; runtime planner is a bounded non-cancellable cold step). The cross-tier reconciliation point is the report: a cfg-pruned member contributes a 'compile-time gated out' entry, a runtime member a 'startup no-match' entry — both threaded to condition-report so the account is single and coherent.

#### R3 — Family as a parameterized PRESET grammar over the typed CondExpr algebra (declarative On-X presets + first-class nested booleans, phase auto-inferred)
Build the family as a layer of named PRESET CONSTRUCTORS over the SPI's R3 typed CondExpr algebra (`enum CondExpr { Leaf(ConditionId, AttrSlice), All(&[CondExpr]), Any(&[CondExpr]), Not(&[CondExpr]) }`). Each Conditional-On-X is a preset that expands to a CondExpr LEAF (or small subtree) with its attributes baked in: `on_class("redis")` -> `Leaf(ON_CLASS, [...])`, `on_property(name=..,having_value=..)` -> `Leaf(ON_PROPERTY, [...])`, `on_web_application(REACTIVE)` -> `Leaf(ON_WEB_APP, [Variant::Reactive])`, `on_profile("prod")` -> `Leaf(ON_PROFILE, ...)` (profiles ARE a preset, not a parallel engine). The NESTED-BOOLEAN helpers become PURE SYNTAX, not subclass-boilerplate: `#[conditional(all(on_class("redis"), any(on_property("a"), on_property("b")), not(on_bean(MyClient))))]` emits one const CondExpr tree; AND (Spring's stacked default) is just `All([...])` when multiple #[on_*] attrs are stacked. CRUCIALLY the family declares each member's PHASE CLASS (parse vs register) and earliest-decidable tier as a property of its ConditionId, and the SPI infers the expression's phase as `max(leaf phases)` — so an author who nests `on_bean` anywhere AUTOMATICALLY defers the whole guard to the register pass, making Spring's #1 authoring bug (forgetting to declare REGISTER on a bean-introspecting condition) structurally impossible. The container conditions (OnProperties/OnBooleanProperties) are sugar for `All([Leaf(ON_PROPERTY,..), ...])`. A member's Leaf can resolve to a const-folded fact (the R2 cfg/build tier, when its kind is statically decidable) OR a runtime predicate (R1), so a single tree can const-fold its cheap leaves (on_class) and runtime-eval its order-sensitive ones (on_missing_bean) — the family IS the composition surface where the SPI's tiers blend.

**Pros:** Best DX for the nested-boolean intent (#1): all/any/not are SYNTAX, so the OR/AND/NOR helpers Spring forces you to subclass (AnyNestedCondition/AllNestedConditions/NoneNestedConditions, choosing phase in a constructor) become zero-ceremony — strictly better than Spring while preserving the stacked=AND default.; Eliminates Spring's #1 family authoring bug by construction: phase is inferred as max over the leaves' declared classes, so nesting an OnBean inside a guard the author thought was a cheap parse-prune AUTOMATICALLY makes the whole guard register-phase — a silent wrong-answer becomes an automatic guarantee (#9 spirit: prevent rather than diagnose late).; Unifies the family with profiles (#11): @Profile is just the on_profile preset over the same CondExpr, so profiles is not a parallel condition engine — maximal shared machinery, the unification invariant.; One structured outcome tree per guard feeds condition-report with full boolean PROVENANCE ('matched All: [on_class redis OK, any: [on_property a NO, on_property b OK], not on_bean MyClient OK]') — richer than Spring's flat outcome list, and it makes the cross-tier story legible (which leaves were compile-gated vs startup-evaluated).; Acts as the natural seam letting condition-family span R2 (cfg-folded on_class leaves) and R1 (runtime on_bean leaves) within ONE element's guard — directly realizing Spring's recommended nested OnClass+inner-OnMissingBean pattern as one data structure, and the charter's 'likely a blend'.

**Cons:** The CondExpr enum becomes a load-bearing kernel ABI that emitted const trees hard-code paths to across the whole workspace — it must be ultra-stable and minimal, raising the cost of ever evolving the family's expression shape (adding a new combinator like xor is an ABI change).; Phase auto-inference is a convenience that can SURPRISE: an author who nests a register-phase on_bean inside what they thought was an early prune silently makes the entire guard late (better than Spring's wrong answer, but the inferred phase MUST be surfaced in the report or it trades one confusion for another).; A single guard straddling compile-time (cfg-folded on_class leaf) and runtime (on_bean leaf) complicates 'when exactly was this decided' reasoning and the report's provenance — some leaves resolved in the member's own crate at compile time, some at the binary/runtime where the full world is visible.; Recursive const CondExpr trees are more elaborate const data than R1's flat entry list; fine on stable but the `&'static [CondExpr]` nesting is heavier for the macro to emit and slightly more runtime work (recursion/indirection) for the purely-runtime case than a flat AND-fold — negligible but non-zero on the cold path.; Still does NOT independently solve 'read without loading' for type-presence: on_class still must delegate to the cfg tier (a linked type is always present), so R3 is a COMPOSITION/authoring layer, not a standalone answer to that sub-intent — it depends on R2 for that one member.

**Mechanisms considered:** named preset constructors (on_class/on_property/on_bean/on_web_application/on_profile/...) expanding to const CondExpr Leaf/subtrees; all/any/not as first-class syntax in `#[conditional(...)]` -> const CondExpr tree (stacked #[on_*] = All); framework-inferred phase = max over leaf-declared phase classes (no author phase declaration — kills the forgot-REGISTER bug); @Profile and OnProperties/OnBooleanProperties as canned preset expressions (unification, not parallel engines); per-Leaf ConditionId resolving to a const-folded fact (R2 cfg/build tier) OR a runtime predicate (R1) — the family as the R1/R2 seam; structured boolean-tree outcome feeding condition-report with full provenance; per-kind phase-class + earliest-decidable tier as ConditionId properties in the kernel

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same kernel residency as R1/R3-SPI: CondExpr, ConditionId, the per-kind phase-class/tier table, Attr, ConditionOutcome live in `leaf-core` with absolute-path references from emitted const trees; ultra-stable+minimal because the whole workspace's macros emit against it. The CondExpr tree is const data riding the SHARED definition-descriptor discovery substrate (link-time slice default + optional dynamic/WASM source), origin-agnostic. Because a Leaf can resolve to a cfg-folded fact OR a runtime predicate, condition-family explicitly spans both cross-crate surfaces: cfg-gated on_class leaves vanish from compilation (no descriptor in that crate) while runtime on_bean leaves ride the table — so the SAME element's guard is partly resolved at compile time (in its own crate) and partly at the binary/runtime (full world visible). The ConditionId->implementation/const resolution registry (populated by the family crate) is the hazard surface to self-check (an unresolved id => loud startup error, never a silent pass-all). resolver=3 still governs whether a sibling flips a cfg-folded leaf. Generics: a guard on `Foo<T>` has no symbol; the macro hard-errors or demands per-instantiation registration. Phase inference + tier selection are pure data computations over the tree, never link/section/constructor order.

**T2 — execution context:** Cold-path like R1, plus the compile-time fold for cfg-tier leaves. The recursive eval runs in the registration planner during refresh-lifecycle bring-up, synchronously, no `.await`, no blocking — the tree is a pure read over already-materialized world state. Phase inference means a tree containing any register-phase leaf (on_bean/on_missing_bean) is automatically held to the second pass after the full definition set is collected, preserving the happens-before OnMissingBean back-off requires. cfg-folded leaves (the R2 seam) are decided at COMPILE/build time and are simply already-true/already-absent by the time the runtime evaluator sees the tree — the evaluator only recurses over the residual runtime leaves. The on_expression preset is the sharp edge: its leaf must NOT trigger bean construction (Spring's 'very early init' hazard), confined to the read-mostly context. Cancellation: none — the planner phase is a bounded non-cancellable cold step; nothing spawns a future or crosses a thread. Errors: a leaf returns graceful no-match-with-reason; a structural fault (unresolved ConditionId, malformed attrs, contradictory cfg) is a compile error (cfg leaves) or aggregated into the startup validation diagnostic (runtime leaves) before wiring (#9).

### Rust clashes
- OnClass/OnMissingClass has NO faithful Rust mechanism. Spring's @ConditionalOnClass reads ASM bytecode so naming an ABSENT optional dependency never throws NoClassDefFoundError — there is no runtime reflection in Rust and a linked type is ALWAYS present; you cannot even name a type that isn't in the dependency graph. The rust-native realization of the INTENT (decide without triggering the cost/failure of the optional dependency) is a Cargo feature / cfg gate: 'class present' becomes 'integration crate/feature compiled in', which physically removes the absent type from compilation. This reframes OnClass from a runtime metadata probe into a compile-time cfg fact — different mechanism, same intent, and the reason the family must straddle compile-time and runtime tiers.
- Spring's OnClass sharp edge (a @Bean method's parameter/return types are JVM-loaded BEFORE the method-level condition runs, forcing the class condition onto a nested @Configuration) is a classloader artifact with no direct Rust analogue — but its rust-native shadow is real: if on_class is realized as cfg, the guarded code referencing the optional type must ITSELF be inside the cfg block, or the compile fails on the absent type. So leaf inherits an isomorphic 'hoist the type reference inside the gate' discipline, but enforced by the COMPILER (a hard error) rather than by a runtime ordering subtlety.
- OnSingleCandidate means 'by-type autowire would resolve unambiguously' (incl. a @Primary among several), NOT 'exactly one bean'. In Rust there is no reflective autowire engine to consult opaquely; the family member must DELEGATE its verdict to leaf's own autowiring-resolution/candidate-resolver primitive (the same layered type/qualifier/primary/fallback policy) rather than count registry entries — otherwise it answers a different question than Spring's.
- OnBean/OnMissingBean order-sensitivity cannot be borrowed from the build system. Spring evaluates them late in a single-threaded reflective parse over a mutable definition set; Rust's link/section/constructor order is UNSPECIFIED (possibly deliberately randomized via -Z layout-seed), so the register-phase ordering must be re-established at RUNTIME as explicit phase DATA on the descriptor, with a documented happens-before (full definition set collected first). The family member declares REGISTER phase; it must never rely on registration order.
- SearchStrategy CURRENT/ANCESTORS/ALL maps onto leaf's container-hierarchy (child sees parent, not vice versa), but Spring's BeanFactory hierarchy and leaf's hierarchy have different visibility/listing rules (listing is local-only in leaf) — the OnBean family must read the hierarchy-aware registry VIEW with the same one-directional semantics, not assume a flat global registry.
- OnProperty/OnBooleanProperty's 'matches when present and not false' / 'matchIfMissing' / 'multiple names must all pass' semantics are portable, but they read the SEALED, read-view Environment/PropertyResolver — which must be fully built BEFORE the condition pass (a refresh-lifecycle ordering constraint). Rust's bias toward eager Result/error tempts treating a missing property as an error; the family must preserve Spring's graceful 'absent -> matchIfMissing decides, no-bean otherwise' (condition-not-met is NOT a failure).
- OnWebApplication(SERVLET/REACTIVE)/OnNotWebApplication assumes a servlet-vs-reactive web-stack distinction that is a JVM-ecosystem artifact; leaf is async-first with no servlet model, so this member must be reframed onto leaf's actual web-integration capability facts (which web integration crate/feature is present, or a runtime web-context flag) — likely a cfg/feature OR runtime-environment fact, not a 1:1 port. Same for OnWarDeployment (no WAR concept) and OnJndi (no JNDI).
- OnThreading (platform vs virtual threads) and OnJava(Range) are JVM-runtime facts; Rust has no virtual-thread/JVM-version axis. OnThreading reframes onto the async-runtime/execution-context capability (which runtime is wired, per the async-first execution-context discipline — NOT a thread-model probe), and OnJava becomes OnRustVersion / a target-cfg fact decided at build time. Intent (gate on the execution substrate's capabilities) survives; the specific axis does not.
- Feature-as-condition (the rust-native OnClass) collides with Cargo feature semantics: features only OR-on and cannot be un-set downstream, and a sibling test/example can flip a feature on for a binary that never asked (unification). Family members modeled on features must be strictly ADDITIVE capability-presence checks; any 'choose backend A xor B' (which Spring would do with mutually-exclusive OnProperty values on a flat mutable classpath) MUST stay a runtime/profile decision — a constraint Spring never faces.
- Spring's nested-boolean helpers force you to subclass AnyNestedCondition/AllNestedConditions/NoneNestedConditions and pick the ConfigurationPhase in the constructor — a footgun (wrong phase = wrong answer). leaf CAN do better by making all/any/not first-class syntax over a typed expression and INFERRING phase from the leaves (R3), but only realizations that model conditions as typed/declared DATA can; an opaque closure-based family member would reproduce Spring's manual-phase footgun.
- Spring's family produces ConditionOutcome reasons recorded into a runtime ConditionEvaluationReport via DEBUG logging; leaf must thread per-member reasons into condition-report as a NON-ERROR side channel while keeping condition-not-met (silent no-bean now) and wiring-broken (loud failure later when something needs the dropped bean) DISTINCT and time-separated. Rust's Result/early-fail bias tempts collapsing them into one eager error — which would destroy the 'opinionated defaults that back off' model.

### Interactions
- **conditions** — Hard upstream dependency and the SOLE substrate. Every family member (OnClass/OnBean/OnProperty/...) is a thin shell over the conditions SPI: it emits a ConditionId+attribute-slice (or a CondExpr leaf), declares its Phase/earliest-decidable-tier per the SPI's contract, and relies on the SPI's two-pass planner, AND-fold, ConditionContext, ConditionOutcome, and graceful-no-bean semantics. The nested-boolean helpers are built on the SPI's AnyOf/AllOf/NoneOf / CondExpr combinators. condition-family adds NO new evaluation engine — it is the parameterized member SET plus presets. Co-review required: the SPI must expose the phase-class/tier declaration hook the family populates.
- **condition-report** — Primary diagnostic consumer. Each family member's job is to produce a kind-specific human-readable reason ('OnProperty x.enabled: found "false", expected "true"'; 'OnMissingBean(Foo): found existing bean bar'; 'OnClass: capability redis not compiled in') which condition-report records as positive/negative/exclusion with provenance. The design rule (from Spring): a member writing a good reason string makes itself debuggable for free. In R3 the report receives the full boolean-tree provenance and must distinguish compile-time-gated-out leaves from runtime no-match leaves. condition-family owns producing the verdict+reason per kind; condition-report owns accounting/presentation.
- **annotation-model** — Hard upstream dependency — the SECOND input each member reads. The triggering On-X annotation's merged, distance-resolved attribute metadata (name/havingValue/matchIfMissing for OnProperty, SearchStrategy/target-type for OnBean, the capability name for OnClass) IS the annotation-model const descriptor, materialized at compile time. Each member reads its own typed attribute slice off that descriptor WITHOUT constructing the guarded bean. Whatever annotation-model picks (compile-time-merged const vs runtime engine) determines how the family's attribute schemas are expressed and validated; co-review required, especially for typed vs stringly attribute slices.
- **auto-configuration / auto-config-ordering** — The principal real-world consumer and the reason the OnBean family + register-phase + deterministic ordering matter. Auto-config beans are guarded by OnMissingBean and ordered to run AFTER all user config so they back off silently when the user defines their own. condition-family's OnMissingBean/OnBean/OnSingleCandidate members, evaluated in the register phase against a complete definition set, are precisely what makes that back-off correct. Per Spring, OnBean-family must be SCOPED to auto-config (the only place 'defined so far' is stable); condition-family must carry that scoping discipline as guidance/diagnostic, not silently allow OnMissingBean on arbitrary user definitions where the answer is ill-defined.
- **profiles** — @Profile IS a family member, not a parallel engine (unification #11). on_profile is a canned preset (Leaf(ON_PROFILE, ...)) reading environment.active_profiles() and evaluating the profile expression. condition-family provides the member shell + presets; profiles provides the !/&/| grammar and the active/include/group levers the member evaluates. Conceptual economy: profiles is just the most ergonomically-named condition preset over the same substrate.
- **environment / property-resolution** — Core ConditionContext input for the property/expression/profile members. OnProperty/OnBooleanProperty/OnExpression/OnProfile/OnCloudPlatform read the sealed, read-view Environment + PropertyResolver (resolved properties + active profiles) synchronously at registration-decision time. The Environment MUST be built/sealed before the condition pass runs (a refresh-lifecycle ordering constraint). condition-family consumes the read-only view; it does not mutate or trigger lazy resolution that could block.
- **bean-registry / bean-definition / container-hierarchy / autowiring-resolution** — The OnBean family reads the read-mostly bean-DEFINITION registry view to probe 'what has been defined so far' (register phase, complete set). SearchStrategy CURRENT/ANCESTORS/ALL maps onto container-hierarchy's one-directional visibility. OnSingleCandidate delegates its 'would by-type autowire resolve unambiguously?' verdict to autowiring-resolution/candidate-resolver (type/qualifier/primary/fallback policy) rather than counting entries. A false condition means the definition is simply never added (graceful no-bean). OnBean reads definitions, not live instances — it must not trigger construction.
- **expression-language** — OnExpression delegates predicate evaluation to the runtime expression layer (#{...} analogue). condition-family provides the on_expression member shell and the ConditionContext the expression evaluates against; expression-language provides the evaluation engine. The sharp edge (from Spring): referencing a bean in such an expression forces very early init — the member must respect the SPI's read-mostly/synchronous/no-construction contract and forbid resolving live beans during evaluation.
- **resource-loading** — OnResource reads the ResourceLoader's already-resolved/abstracted view to test resource presence. Per the SPI's synchronous read-mostly contract, the member must NOT perform blocking/network IO during the cold condition pass — it reads a pre-resolved resource view (the resource-loader abstraction the context exposes), not a live filesystem/network probe.
- **component-scanning / programmatic-registration** — Discovered components and programmatic registrations are gated by family members before becoming live definitions; the condition descriptors ride the SAME cross-crate discovery substrate as the components themselves (shared descriptor table, no separate channel). On-X members gate scanned candidates and registrar emissions identically — origin-agnostic, so a dynamically-discovered (WASM) definition can only be gated by RUNTIME members (it has no compile-time cfg).
- **refresh-lifecycle** — Family-member evaluation is a fixed step in bring-up: the OnClass/cfg tier is decided at compile/build time (before refresh exists); the runtime members (OnProperty/OnBean/OnProfile/OnResource) run during definition-loading/registration, AFTER the Environment is sealed and (for register-phase OnBean) after all definitions are collected, but BEFORE eager singleton instantiation. The parse-vs-register two-pass is a sub-ordering within refresh; condition-family slots into that template, never running ad hoc.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- THE conditional strategy (charter §3, explicitly deferred) decided AT THE FAMILY LEVEL: the per-kind tier-map IS the concrete decision — which member owns which tier (OnClass=cfg, OnBean=runtime, OnCloudPlatform/OnThreading=build-or-runtime?). condition-family's three realizations are candidate packagings of that mapping; Phase 2 must fix the per-kind tier table (it is a load-bearing kernel ABI) without which the macros cannot agree what is static vs deferred. Directly couples to the metadata/codegen-boundary decision.
- Is the rust-native OnClass/OnMissingClass a Cargo feature, a cfg, a runtime capability-registry probe, or a combination — and how does that reconcile with feature additivity (features only OR-on, can't be un-set, a sibling can flip one on via unification)? This decides whether 'optional-dependency presence' is a build fact or a runtime fact and ripples into auto-configuration back-off and the OnMissingClass complement (how do you assert ABSENCE of a capability that features can only turn ON?).
- How are the family's attribute SCHEMAS expressed and validated — typed per-member structs the macro builds (early, span-rich validation of name/havingValue/SearchStrategy) vs a stringly Attr-slice the runtime impl interprets (loose, late validation)? This couples to annotation-model's compile-time-merged-const vs runtime-engine choice and determines where a misspelled attribute key is caught (#9 timing).
- Should the family member's PHASE be author-declared per kind (Spring-faithful, risks the forgot-REGISTER bug for a bean-introspecting member) or framework-INFERRED from the kind's declared class / the CondExpr tree (R3, makes the bug impossible but can surprise)? A DX-vs-faithfulness call coupled to whether members are opaque objects or typed/declared data.
- How is OnWebApplication(SERVLET/REACTIVE)/OnNotWebApplication reframed for an async-first, no-servlet leaf — onto a web-integration capability feature, a runtime web-context flag, or dropped? And similarly OnThreading (onto the async-runtime/execution-context capability), OnWarDeployment, OnJndi, OnCheckpointRestore — which JVM-ecosystem members survive intact, which reframe, which are dropped as Rust-irrelevant? Needs a web/integration co-review.
- Does OnSingleCandidate's 'would autowire resolve unambiguously' verdict reuse EXACTLY the autowiring-resolution/candidate-resolver primitive (unification #11), or does the family carry its own resolution logic? Wants resolution alongside the autowiring/candidate-resolver substrate so there is one definition of 'unambiguous'.
- How do family-member outcomes thread into the unified error/diagnostics + condition-report model so condition-not-met (silent no-bean now) and wiring-broken (loud failure later) stay DISTINCT and time-separated, while a cross-tier guard (some leaves compile-gated, some runtime-evaluated) still yields ONE coherent #9-grade account of why an element did/didn't register? Connects the deferred unified-diagnostics decision with condition-report.
- For the dynamic/WASM-module 'second classpath': a dynamically-discovered definition has no compile-time cfg and no Rust type, so it can ONLY be gated by RUNTIME members — does origin-agnosticism therefore make a runtime evaluation layer MANDATORY for the family even if cfg/build tiers are the default for native crates, and can OnClass even be expressed for a WASM-sourced contribution (no feature to read)?
- Where does the ConditionContext's read-mostly world view come from and what is its ownership/lifetime shape (a borrowed snapshot of the sealed environment + complete definition registry vs an Arc handle) — and must it expose hierarchy-aware (CURRENT/ANCESTORS/ALL) registry views for the OnBean family? An instance of the deferred scope/lifetime/ownership keystone applied to the family's evaluation inputs.
- Is the nested-boolean grammar (all/any/not) first-class macro syntax over a typed CondExpr (R3) or a set of catalog AnyOf/AllOf/NoneOf members (R1), and does xor / count-based combinators get added — i.e. how rich is the family's boolean algebra, and what is the ABI cost of evolving it given emitted const trees hard-code the kernel enum?

### Notes
Scope discipline: I designed condition-family STRICTLY as the rich parameterized member SET (OnClass/OnMissingClass, OnBean/OnMissingBean/OnSingleCandidate, OnProperty/OnBooleanProperty, OnExpression, OnResource, OnWebApplication, OnCloudPlatform, OnJava/OnRustVersion, OnThreading, and the OnProperties/OnBooleanProperties container forms) PLUS the nested-boolean helpers — all as thin shells over the upstream `conditions` SPI. I deliberately did NOT redesign the predicate contract, two-phase planner, ConditionContext, ConditionOutcome, or AND-composition (those are `conditions`, already designed: R1 runtime-table / R2 cfg+codegen / R3 CondExpr algebra). I did NOT design the report accounting (condition-report), the attribute metadata view (annotation-model), or the profile grammar (profiles) — distinct neighbours this feature plugs into.

The genuinely divergent axis for THIS feature is NOT 'where does a predicate evaluate' (that was the SPI's axis) but HOW THE FAMILY IS PACKAGED AND PARAMETERIZED: R1 = a flat CATALOG of concrete per-member Condition impls + thin per-member macros (most faithful 'thin shells' shape, uniform runtime treatment, simplest mental model, but can't honestly express OnClass and pays per-definition cold-path cost); R2 = a TIERED family where each member declares its rust-native earliest-decidable tier (cfg/build/runtime) so the SAME annotation resolves statically when it can — this is where the family ENCODES the design knowledge 'OnClass is a build fact, OnBean is a runtime fact', the acid-test mapping; R3 = the family as a PRESET grammar over the typed CondExpr algebra with first-class all/any/not and inferred phase — best DX for booleans, kills Spring's forgot-REGISTER footgun, and is the natural seam where cfg-folded and runtime leaves blend within one guard.

Strong note for Phase 2/3: these are COMPOSABLE, not exclusive — the likely shape is R3's preset+CondExpr surface as the AUTHORING layer, R2's per-kind tier-map as the realization strategy (cfg for OnClass/optional-dependency presence, runtime for OnBean/profiles/runtime-property), and R1's per-member impls as the concrete predicates for the runtime tier. The single most important Phase-2 artifact this feature forces is the PER-KIND TIER + PHASE TABLE in leaf-core (which member is cfg/build/runtime, parse/register) — it is a load-bearing, ultra-stable ABI that every family macro across the workspace classifies against, and it is the concrete instance of the charter's deferred 'conditional strategy (cfg vs build-time codegen vs runtime — likely a blend)'.

Two sub-intents of 'read without loading' to keep separate in Phase 2: (a) decide WITHOUT running the guarded bean's constructor (every member does this, runtime included) vs (b) Spring's literal 'name a class that may be absent without error' — whose true Rust analogue is cfg/feature compilation-gating (OnClass), NOT a runtime probe, since a linked type is always present.

JVM-ecosystem members need explicit reframing decisions in Phase 2 (flagged in rustClashes + phase2Questions): OnWebApplication SERVLET/REACTIVE (no servlet model in async-first leaf), OnThreading (no virtual-thread axis → execution-context capability), OnJava (→ OnRustVersion / target-cfg), OnWarDeployment/OnJndi/OnCheckpointRestore (likely dropped or reframed). OnSingleCandidate must DELEGATE to autowiring-resolution, not count beans (Spring's 'autowire would succeed', incl. @Primary).

Critical grounding constraints honoured: nothing here needs nightly (runtime trait objects, const data, cfg/features, const-eval folds, linkme/inventory all stable; conditions are synchronous cold-path reads so no async-trait boxing tax). Condition descriptors + the ConditionId->impl registry ride the SAME cross-crate discovery substrate as components/definitions (no separate channel) and inherit its DCE + Layer-0 hazards — a startup self-check must assert both gated definitions AND that the family crate's built-in member impls resolved (an empty condition registry silently passes-all or fails-all). cfg-tier OnClass must be paired with force-link of the integration crate (cfg gates compilation, not link retention). Two-phase ordering must be DATA resolved at runtime, NEVER link/section/constructor order. The co-review partners are `conditions` (the SPI; its phase/tier hook is what the family populates), `auto-configuration` (whose back-off correctness depends on the OnMissingBean register-phase guarantee), `annotation-model` (attribute schemas), and `condition-report` (per-member reason strings). No existing source to build on — leaf has only an empty src/lib.rs.

## Condition Evaluation Report  `[condition-report]`

Spring's ConditionEvaluationReport makes heavy convention-over-configuration ACCOUNTABLE: every condition decision is recorded as a positiveMatch / negativeMatch / exclusion / unconditionalClass, each carrying a human-readable reason from the ConditionOutcome's ConditionMessage ("did not find property", "@ConditionalOnMissingBean found beans of type X"). The account is dumped at startup under --debug and exposed as structured JSON via /actuator/conditions. The PHILOSOPHY (the part leaf must replicate, intent-not-mechanism): auto-configuration is "magic" the framework OWES the developer a clear, machine-readable explanation for — converting an opaque "why is my bean missing?" into a lookup, so trust in opinionated defaults survives. The KEY sharp edge from the Spring research (lines 2229-2235): condition-not-met (a silent no-bean NOW, at definition time, not an error) and wiring-broken (a LOUD failure LATER, when something actually needs the absent bean) are DISTINCT, TIME-SEPARATED failures; the report is the bridge that lets a developer see a bean "backed off" rather than "broke". A corollary the report design must honor: a condition author who writes a good reason string gets debuggability for free — the reason string IS the report's content, so condition-report does not generate reasons, it COLLECTS and PRESENTS them.

SCOPE DISCIPLINE for THIS feature. condition-report is the DIAGNOSTIC ACCOUNTING + PRESENTATION sink, NOT the evaluation engine. It does NOT own: the predicate contract / two-phase model / ConditionContext / ConditionOutcome shape (that is `conditions`, the upstream SPI); the parameterized member set or their reason-string authorship (that is `condition-family`); the attribute-metadata view (`annotation-model`); the profile grammar (`profiles`). It DOES own four things: (1) the RECORD SCHEMA — the per-element account with verdict class (positive/negative/exclusion/unconditional, plus leaf's new compile-gated-out class), the reason string + provenance (source file/line, the element key, the deciding ConditionId/leaf), and for boolean trees the full provenance tree; (2) the COLLECTION POINT + LIFETIME — who owns the growing account during refresh, what its ownership/borrow shape is, when it freezes; (3) PRESENTATION — the startup dump (leaf's --debug analogue), a structured machine-readable export (the /actuator/conditions analogue), and integration into the unified diagnostics model; (4) the TIME-SEPARATION discipline — keeping silent-no-bean-now and loud-failure-later distinct, and making the later NoSuchBean-style failure able to point BACK into the report ("bean X backed off because <reason>"). Rust reframing: Spring records at runtime via DEBUG logging over a single-threaded reflective parse; leaf's conditions may resolve across THREE tiers (compile-time cfg, build-time const-fold, runtime planner per condition-family's tier-map), so leaf's report must RECONCILE compile-gated-out entries (no descriptor in the binary) with runtime no-match entries into ONE coherent account — a problem Spring never has because everything is runtime.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Runtime report SINK: a per-refresh ReportRecorder the conditions-SPI planner writes ConditionOutcome rows into, frozen into an immutable &Report at end-of-refresh, dumped + exported by the diagnostics layer
Model the report as a passive RECORDING SINK that the `conditions` SPI's two-pass planner writes into as it evaluates. The SPI already produces, per guarded element, a verdict + a ConditionOutcome { matched: bool, reason: ReasonMsg, condition_id, provenance } (condition-family authors the reason; conditions threads it). condition-report contributes the SINK trait the planner calls: `trait ConditionReportSink { fn record(&self, entry: ConditionRecord<'_>); }` where `ConditionRecord` carries the element key (a stable ElementId — TypeId / descriptor index / qualified name), the verdict CLASS (Positive / Negative / Exclusion / Unconditional), the per-leaf outcomes (for an AND-fold or a CondExpr tree, the whole list/subtree of (ConditionId, matched, reason, span)), and declaration provenance (file:line:col captured at macro-expansion via the stable `proc_macro::Span` location APIs and baked into the element descriptor as `&'static str` + line). The default sink is a `RefReport` owned BY the refresh-lifecycle on the cold path — a single owner, no Arc, no lock: the planner runs in one task on the cold bring-up path and `&mut`-appends rows (Vec growth amortized, stack-rooted owner). At end of the registration pass the recorder FREEZES into an immutable `Report` (an `&'static`-free owned value: `Box<[ConditionRecord]>` keyed by ElementId) that the container holds for the life of the context. Presentation is two pure readers over the frozen Report: a `render_startup(&Report) -> String` (leaf's `--debug` / `LEAF_DEBUG` analogue — grouped Positive/Negative/Exclusions/Unconditional, each with its reason, mirroring Spring's dump) and a `serialize(&Report) -> ReportJson` (the `/actuator/conditions` analogue: a serde-shaped structured tree any introspection endpoint can emit). The diagnostics-layer hook: when a LATER resolution fails (a NoSuchBean-style error from autowiring-resolution), the error builder QUERIES the frozen Report by the missing type's ElementId and, if that element has a Negative record, appends 'candidate X backed off: <reason>' to the rich error — directly realizing the silent-now / loud-later bridge (charter #9). A null/no-op sink (Spring's 'no-op by default, opt-in recording', mirroring startup-instrumentation) means zero overhead when reporting is off — the planner calls a `&dyn ConditionReportSink` whose default impl discards.

**Pros:** Faithful to Spring's exact shape (positiveMatches/negativeMatches/exclusions/unconditionalClasses + dump + structured export) and to its 'good reason string IS the report' rule — condition-report COLLECTS, condition-family AUTHORS; clean separation of concerns and the simplest mental model (one sink, one frozen value).; Honors the silent-now/loud-later invariant structurally (charter #9): a Negative record is a non-error side channel during refresh, and the later autowiring failure RE-USES it to produce a rich 'backed off because…' message — exactly Spring's 'see that the bean backed off rather than broke', realized as the unified-diagnostics enrichment rather than a separate log to grep.; Memory/concurrency clean (#5): single cold-path owner, &mut append, NO Arc and NO lock — the recorder lives on the refresh stack, freezes to an immutable owned value; no global state, no busy-wait, polling-free (it is a passive sink written by the existing pass, never its own loop).; No-op-by-default = zero overhead when off (#1/#2), mirroring startup-instrumentation's opt-in recording taxonomy; recording on is a bounded Vec append per guarded element on the cold path only.; Stable-only (#8): plain owned structs + serde + the stable proc_macro::Span location APIs for provenance; no nightly, no link-time machinery of its OWN (it rides whatever substrate conditions/condition-family already use to deliver outcomes).

**Cons:** Records ONLY what the runtime planner sees — a condition resolved at COMPILE time (condition-family's cfg-tier OnClass, where the absent dependency is physically removed from compilation) produces NO runtime outcome and thus NO row, so the report is BLIND to compile-gated-out elements unless they are separately surfaced (the cross-tier reconciliation gap; R3 attacks this directly).; The ElementId keying is load-bearing and must agree with the registry/descriptor substrate's own keying (TypeId vs descriptor-index vs qualified name) so the later-failure enrichment can look an element up — couples condition-report to the deferred type-erasure/registry-substrate decision.; A single &mut-owned recorder assumes the planner is single-task on the cold path; if any future variant evaluates conditions concurrently (e.g. background-bootstrap of independent subgraphs), the sink would need a per-shard recorder merged at freeze — a constraint the design must document, not silently assume.; Capturing provenance as &'static str + line per element grows the descriptor footprint slightly for every guarded element even when recording is OFF (the spans are baked at compile time regardless) — small but non-zero binary size cost the no-op path cannot reclaim.; The reason strings are produced by condition-family members; if a member writes a poor message, the report is poor — condition-report can enforce a SHAPE (kind, expected, found) but cannot author content, so report quality is only as good as the family's discipline.

**Mechanisms considered:** a `ConditionReportSink` trait the conditions-SPI planner calls with each `ConditionRecord` (Sink owned by refresh-lifecycle, default no-op); single cold-path &mut-owned recorder, frozen into an immutable owned `Report` at end of registration pass (no Arc/no lock); provenance baked into the element descriptor at macro-expansion via stable `proc_macro::Span` line/file APIs (&'static str + u32 line); serde-shaped structured export (the /actuator/conditions analogue) + a pure `render_startup` text dump (the --debug analogue); diagnostics-layer enrichment: a later NoSuchBean-style error queries the frozen Report by ElementId and appends the 'backed off because…' reason; null/no-op sink for zero-overhead-when-off, mirroring startup-instrumentation's opt-in recording

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The report itself contributes NO new cross-crate discovery surface — it is a runtime sink that consumes outcomes the `conditions`/`condition-family` substrate already delivers, so it inherits (does not add to) that substrate's DCE/Layer-0 hazards. Two T1 facts matter. (a) PROVENANCE crosses crate boundaries as const data: each contributing crate's macros bake file:line into the element descriptor (absolute `proc_macro::Span` text, no runtime path resolution), so a Negative record for a bean declared in `leaf-redis` correctly cites `leaf-redis/src/…:NN` from the final binary; this rides the SAME descriptor channel as the element, no separate registry. (b) COMPLETENESS depends on the same Layer-0 force-link discipline as everything else: if a contributing crate is not linked, its elements (and their would-be records) simply do not exist — the report cannot show what was never compiled in, so the report's own startup self-check should cross-reference the expected-crate manifest (the `scan!`/`enable!` list) and WARN 'integration leaf-redis declared but contributed 0 condition records', turning a silent missing-crate into a visible report annotation (reusing the substrate's expected-count self-check). The `Report`/`ConditionRecord`/verdict-class types live in `leaf-core` (ultra-stable) so any introspection endpoint or integration crate can read the same shape. No build.rs involvement; no sibling-scanning; ordering of records is irrelevant (the report is a set keyed by ElementId, never relies on link/section/constructor order).

**T2 — execution context:** Strictly COLD-PATH, synchronous, single-owner. Recording happens INSIDE the conditions-SPI registration planner during refresh-lifecycle bring-up — after the Environment is sealed and (for register-phase outcomes) after the full definition set is collected, but before any eager singleton is built and before any bean future is spawned. The sink's `record` is a non-blocking, non-async &mut append (or a discard in the no-op default); it never `.await`s, never blocks, never does IO (rendering/serialization is a SEPARATE, later, on-demand read over the frozen Report, also synchronous and cheap). FREEZE is a one-shot transition at end-of-registration; thereafter the Report is immutable and shared by shared-ref (no lock needed for reads). Cancellation: the recording step is part of the bounded, non-cancellable cold bring-up; if refresh is aborted the partially-built recorder is simply dropped (owned on the stack, no cleanup hazard). Errors: recording NEVER errors (it is pure accounting) — a malformed condition is the SPI's concern, surfaced into the startup validation diagnostic; the report merely records the outcome the SPI hands it. The later-failure enrichment runs on whatever path raises the resolution error (could be a runtime hot path if a bean is resolved lazily) but it is a pure immutable-Report lookup — O(1) by ElementId, no lock, no blocking — safe to call from any context.

#### R2 — Report as a structured DIAGNOSTIC EVENT STREAM: each condition decision emits a typed ConditionDecided record onto the unified diagnostics/observation bus; the report is a SUBSCRIBER that materializes the account, and tracing/metrics/actuator are other subscribers
Instead of a dedicated sink owned by refresh, model each condition decision as a typed DIAGNOSTIC EVENT on leaf's (deferred) unified diagnostics/observation channel — the same channel startup-instrumentation, the error model, and tracing-style observation would share (charter #11 unification). As the conditions-SPI planner decides each element it emits a `ConditionDecided { element: ElementId, class: VerdictClass, leaves: &[LeafOutcome], provenance }` observation. The default REPORT is just ONE subscriber: an in-memory materializer that folds the stream into the same frozen `Report` value R1 produces (grouped Positive/Negative/Exclusion/Unconditional). But because it is a stream, OTHER consumers attach without the report knowing them: a `tracing` bridge maps each decision to a structured span/event (weak `tracing` feature, per the cross-crate doc's `pkg?/feat` capability threading) so existing log infra shows backoffs; a metrics bridge counts matches/no-matches per ConditionId; an actuator/introspection endpoint subscribes to expose the live structured account. The emit point is a thin `fn emit(&self, ev: ConditionDecided)` on a `&dyn DiagnosticObserver` the planner holds (no-op observer = zero cost when nothing is attached). Reason strings still come from condition-family; condition-report owns the EVENT SCHEMA (what a ConditionDecided contains) and the default materializer + renderers, not the bus itself. The silent-now/loud-later bridge becomes: the later NoSuchBean error queries the materialized Report (same as R1) OR, richer, the error model and the condition stream are two views of ONE diagnostics model so the 'backed off because' link is a first-class join, not a bolt-on.

**Pros:** Maximal unification (#11): the report stops being a bespoke artifact and becomes one consumer of the SAME observation/diagnostics model that startup-instrumentation (timed step tree), the error model (charter #9), and tracing/metrics share — fewer parallel mechanisms, the explicit goal Phases 2-4 exist for.; Open/closed extensibility for free: an actuator-style live endpoint, a tracing bridge, and a metrics counter all attach as subscribers WITHOUT condition-report knowing about them — directly mirrors Spring exposing the same outcomes via BOTH the --debug dump AND /actuator/conditions, but generalized so future sinks (a TUI, a JSON file for CI) need no changes here.; Decouples PRODUCTION of decisions from CONSUMPTION: condition-report ships the schema + a default materializer, but a user who only wants tracing output pays nothing for the in-memory Report (attach only the tracing subscriber) — finer-grained opt-in than R1's single sink, good for the low-overhead #2 goal.; Naturally accommodates the cross-tier story: a compile-gated-out element can emit a synthetic 'GatedOutAtCompileTime' decision (from a build/codegen-emitted shim) onto the SAME stream as runtime no-matches, so one subscriber materializes a unified account spanning tiers — better than R1's runtime blind spot, short of R3's compile-time manifest.; Provenance + reason ride the event payload, so the structured export is the event schema itself (serde-derive on ConditionDecided) — one definition serves dump, tracing, and JSON export.

**Cons:** Hard dependency on a diagnostics/observation MODEL that does not yet exist and is explicitly DEFERRED to Phase 2 (the unified error/diagnostics model, charter §3) — R2 cannot be fully specified until that meta-decision lands, so it is more a STANCE ('the report should be a subscriber, not an island') than a self-contained realization.; An event-stream framing risks implying a HOT-PATH pub/sub (events feature) on a COLD-PATH concern; must be explicitly constrained to a synchronous cold-path observer call (not the async event-multicaster), or it violates the reactive-hot/polling-cold discipline by over-engineering a startup-only sink into a runtime bus.; Ordering/back-pressure questions the simple sink (R1) never has: subscribers that do IO (a file/JSON-export subscriber) must not block the cold planner — emit must stay non-blocking and defer any IO, or the report mechanism slows bring-up; this is more moving parts to get right than a passive Vec append.; Two consumers of the same stream (in-memory Report + tracing bridge) can drift in what they consider a 'class' (does tracing log Unconditional?) unless the VerdictClass taxonomy is fixed centrally — more coordination surface than R1.; Risk of conceptual over-reach in Phase 1: deciding the report is 'just a subscriber' pre-supposes the shape of the unified diagnostics model, which would bias Phase 2 — must be presented as a candidate coupling, not a commitment.

**Mechanisms considered:** a typed `ConditionDecided` observation emitted by the conditions-SPI planner onto the unified diagnostics/observation channel (no-op observer default); the default report as ONE subscriber that folds the stream into the same frozen `Report` value R1 materializes; additional subscribers (tracing bridge via weak `pkg?/feat`, metrics counters, actuator/introspection endpoint) attaching without report's knowledge; a synchronous COLD-PATH observer call (explicitly NOT the async event-multicaster / hot-path bus); compile-gated-out elements emitting a synthetic 'GatedOutAtCompileTime' decision from a build/codegen shim onto the same stream; serde-derived event schema serving dump + tracing + JSON export uniformly

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Like R1, the report adds NO new discovery surface — decisions are emitted by the existing planner, observers are registered explicitly by the application/binary (the only place the full graph is visible, per the cross-crate doc's role-separation lesson: the binary owns assembly, contribution crates only declare). The `ConditionDecided`/`VerdictClass`/`LeafOutcome` schema lives in `leaf-core` so every potential subscriber crate (a `leaf-actuator`, a `leaf-tracing` bridge) reads the identical shape; bridges to optional ecosystems (tracing/metrics) are threaded with weak features (`tracing?/std`) so a dormant tracing crate is never force-pulled. Compile-gated-out reconciliation is the interesting T1 wrinkle: a synthetic 'GatedOutAtCompileTime' decision must be EMITTED from somewhere that knows the cfg fact — i.e. condition-family's cfg-tier macro would have to emit not just the (absent) element but a residual const breadcrumb 'element E was cfg-gated out' that the runtime can replay onto the stream; that breadcrumb is itself a tiny registration riding the descriptor channel and subject to the same Layer-0/DCE force-link discipline (and a self-check that the breadcrumb crate is linked). Provenance handling identical to R1 (compile-time-baked spans). No build.rs/sibling scanning by the report; subscriber registration order is irrelevant to correctness (the account is keyed by ElementId).

**T2 — execution context:** Cold-path for PRODUCTION (the planner emits during refresh, synchronously, no .await, no blocking — the observer call is a plain function call, no-op when nothing attached) and explicitly NOT the async event-multicaster (which is a hot-path/runtime bus) — this must be stated to avoid conflating a startup diagnostic stream with the runtime event system. CONSUMPTION execution context varies by subscriber and is the discipline point: the in-memory materializer is a synchronous fold (cold, cheap); a tracing bridge does a non-blocking structured log (cold); any subscriber wanting IO (write JSON to disk, push to an endpoint) MUST buffer during the cold planner pass and flush AFTER refresh (or off the bring-up task), never blocking the planner — the emit contract is 'observers must not block; defer IO'. Cancellation: aborting refresh drops the partially-materialized Report; emitted-but-unflushed buffered events in a deferred subscriber are discarded. Errors: emit cannot fail (fire-and-forget observation); a subscriber that errors (e.g. export IO fails) handles its own error out-of-band and must never propagate back into the cold planner (a failed report export must not fail bring-up — the report is diagnostic, not load-bearing). The later-failure enrichment is the same O(1) immutable-Report lookup as R1, callable from any context including a hot resolution path.

#### R3 — Cross-tier ACCOUNTABILITY LEDGER: a compile/build-time-anchored manifest of EVERY guarded element (its tier, its gate, its declared reason template) fused at runtime with the runtime outcomes into one complete account that can explain compile-gated-out elements too
Attack the leaf-specific gap head-on: because conditions resolve across THREE tiers (compile-time cfg, build-time const-fold, runtime planner — condition-family's tier-map), a purely-runtime report (R1/R2) is BLIND to elements pruned at compile time, so it cannot answer 'why did my redis bean not appear?' when the answer is 'the redis capability feature was not compiled in' — the single most important question for opinionated backoff. R3 makes the report a CROSS-TIER LEDGER. At macro-expansion / codegen time, EVERY guarded element emits a static `GuardManifestEntry { element: ElementId, tier: Tier, gate: GateDescriptor (which feature/cfg, which ConditionId leaves, provenance), reason_template }` into a manifest — for cfg-tier members the manifest entry is emitted OUTSIDE the cfg gate (so it survives even when the element itself is cfg'd out, carrying 'this element exists in source but is gated by feature=redis'), while the element's own descriptor is emitted INSIDE the gate. At runtime the report FUSES: (1) the manifest (everything that COULD be guarded, incl. compile-gated-out, known from the always-present manifest entries), (2) the runtime outcomes (R1's planner rows, for the elements that survived to runtime), and (3) the resolved feature/cfg set of the binary (to label a manifest entry whose element is absent as 'gated out: feature redis not enabled' vs 'compiled in'). The result is a COMPLETE account: every element appears exactly once, labeled CompiledOutByCfg(feature) | BuildFoldedFalse(reason) | RuntimePositive(reason) | RuntimeNegative(reason) | Exclusion | Unconditional — the cross-tier reconciliation the leaf-charter and condition-family's openNotes flag as the hard problem. Presentation/export as R1; the later-failure enrichment is now strictly RICHER: a NoSuchBean for the redis client can say 'redis client backed off: capability feature "redis" not enabled in this binary (enable it in Cargo.toml)' — actionable in the Spring 'Action:' spirit (research line 2215), which a runtime-only report literally cannot produce because no runtime outcome exists.

**Pros:** The ONLY realization that closes leaf's defining gap: it can explain a compile-gated-out element ('feature redis not enabled') — the most likely real-world 'why is my bean missing?' under feature-driven OnClass, which R1/R2 are structurally blind to; this is the rust-native completion of Spring's accountability intent, not a port of its runtime-only report.; Produces the most actionable later-failure diagnostics (#9): because the manifest knows the GATE (which feature/cfg), the enrichment can tell the developer WHAT TO DO ('enable feature redis'), echoing Spring's 'Action:' line philosophy (research line 2215) — a strictly richer 'backed off because' than a runtime reason string.; Single coherent account across all three condition tiers (charter's deferred conditional strategy is 'likely a blend' — this realization is the report that survives that blend): every element appears once with a tier-labeled verdict, so the developer never has to reason about WHERE a decision was made to find out WHY.; Doubles as the substrate SELF-CHECK the cross-crate doc demands: the always-present manifest IS the expected-element list, so fusing it with runtime outcomes naturally detects 'manifest says element E from leaf-redis should be considered, but neither a runtime outcome nor a cfg-out label appeared' = a DCE/Layer-0 dropped registration — turning the silent-empty-registry failure into a loud report annotation, exactly the doc's mandated self-check.; Compile-time provenance + gate descriptors give the structured export real semantic richness (tier, gate, feature name) beyond Spring's runtime-only positive/negative lists — better tooling surface for a CI 'why did config differ between builds' check.

**Cons:** A SECOND cross-crate registration surface (the manifest) ON TOP of the element/condition descriptor channel — more const data, more macro emission, and it inherits ALL the Layer-0/DCE hazards (a manifest entry can itself be DCE'd, defeating the very completeness it promises) — heaviest T1 footprint of the three; needs its own force-link + self-check.; Heaviest macro/codegen burden (#10 thin-macros tension): every guarded element now emits TWO things (the gated descriptor INSIDE the cfg + the manifest entry OUTSIDE it) and the manifest entry must encode the gate (feature names, cfg predicates) as const data — more logic pushed near the macro than R1's single sink, risking the 'macros emit only hand-writable code' line (the manifest entry must stay hand-writable const data, not computed logic).; Binary-size cost is unconditional: manifest entries for EVERY guarded element (including compile-gated-out ones, by design) live in the binary even when reporting is OFF — you cannot no-op them away because their whole point is to survive compile-gating; an always-on footprint R1's bake-spans cost is dwarfed by.; Reconciling 'feature X not enabled' requires the report to read the binary's RESOLVED feature/cfg set at runtime — which the cross-crate doc warns is itself subtle (differs between `-p`/`--workspace`, resolver-dependent, can be flipped by a sibling via unification); the report's 'gated out: feature redis off' label is only as trustworthy as that resolved-set introspection.; Over-engineered if Phase 2 decides conditions are PREDOMINANTLY runtime (not a heavy cfg blend) — then most manifest entries duplicate runtime outcomes and the second surface earns little; its value is contingent on the deferred conditional-strategy decision, so committing to it in Phase 1 would pre-bias that decision.

**Mechanisms considered:** a `GuardManifestEntry { element, tier, gate, reason_template }` emitted for EVERY guarded element at macro/codegen time; manifest entry emitted OUTSIDE the cfg gate (survives compile-gating) while the element descriptor is emitted INSIDE — so compile-gated-out elements remain accountable; runtime FUSION of manifest + runtime outcomes + the binary's resolved feature/cfg set into one complete per-element ledger; tier-labeled verdict taxonomy (CompiledOutByCfg / BuildFoldedFalse / RuntimePositive / RuntimeNegative / Exclusion / Unconditional); manifest-as-self-check: fuse detects manifest-present-but-no-outcome-and-no-cfg-label = a DCE/Layer-0 dropped registration (the doc's mandated expected-count check); gate-aware actionable enrichment ('enable feature redis') for the later NoSuchBean failure, in Spring's 'Action:' spirit; build.rs/codegen path (Architecture C) as the portable manifest emitter on wasm/embedded where link sections are unreliable

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization MOST entangled with T1 — it deliberately adds a second const-data registration surface (the manifest) specifically to BEAT the cross-crate completeness problem, so it lives or dies by the substrate discipline. The manifest entries ride a distributed-slice / collected channel like the element descriptors but with the crucial twist that a cfg-tier element's manifest entry is emitted OUTSIDE its cfg gate — meaning the manifest is the binary's record of 'what source declared, regardless of what compiled in'; this is only sound if those entries themselves survive DCE/Layer-0, so the manifest channel needs the SAME force-link guarantee (the `scan!`/`enable!` app-root must reference each contributing crate) and a self-check. The 'feature redis off' label requires reading the binary's resolved cfg/feature set; per the cross-crate doc this must be computed deterministically from the FINAL resolved set (documented to differ between `-p` and `--workspace`, governed by resolver=3) — the report must consume a single authoritative resolved-feature snapshot, not probe cfg ad hoc. On wasm/embedded (no reliable link sections) the manifest is best emitted via build-time codegen (Architecture C) — and notably the manifest's completeness goal makes the codegen path MORE attractive here than for the elements themselves, since codegen can enumerate declared integration crates from `cargo metadata` and emit a guaranteed-complete manifest. Manifest schema (`GuardManifestEntry`, `Tier`, `GateDescriptor`) lives in `leaf-core`. Ordering irrelevant (keyed by ElementId). The manifest doubles as the expected-count self-check the doc mandates — its raison d'être partly IS solving the silent-dropped-registration trap for the whole substrate.

**T2 — execution context:** Spans compile/build-time AND cold runtime. Manifest entries are produced at macro-expansion (compile-time, no executor) or build.rs/codegen (host process, cold one-shot) — purely static, no async, the only failure surface is a compile/codegen error for a malformed gate. The FUSION runs once, synchronously, on the cold refresh-lifecycle path AFTER runtime outcomes are recorded (it needs R1's runtime rows) and after the resolved-feature snapshot is available — a single bounded pass joining manifest ⋈ outcomes ⋈ feature-set into the frozen ledger, no .await, no blocking, single owner (no Arc/lock), then immutable. Cancellation: the fusion is part of bounded cold bring-up; abort drops the partial ledger. Errors: fusion itself cannot fail on normal data; a DETECTED inconsistency (manifest entry with neither outcome nor cfg-out label) is NOT an error but a recorded report annotation ('possible dropped registration — verify force-link') that the startup self-check can ESCALATE to a loud diagnostic per the substrate's reliability mandate — distinct from condition-not-met (silent). The later-failure enrichment is the same O(1) immutable-ledger lookup as R1/R2 but returns a richer, gate-aware, action-bearing reason; safe to call from any context (hot or cold) since the ledger is frozen and read-only.

### Rust clashes
- Spring records the report at RUNTIME via DEBUG logging over a single-threaded reflective parse where EVERY decision is a runtime event; leaf's conditions may resolve at COMPILE time (cfg-tier OnClass physically removes the absent dependency), at BUILD time (const-fold), or at RUNTIME (condition-family's tier-map). So a leaf report that only watches the runtime planner is structurally BLIND to compile-gated-out elements — the exact 'why is my bean missing?' case (answer: 'feature not enabled') that matters most for opinionated backoff. There is no runtime event for a thing the compiler deleted. Closing this requires anchoring accountability data at compile/build time (R3's manifest), a problem Spring never faces because nothing is decided before its runtime.
- Spring's silent-no-bean-now / loud-failure-later separation (research lines 2231-2235) collides with Rust's bias toward eager Result/early-fail. The Rust-idiomatic instinct is to turn a missing dependency into an error AT the decision point; doing so would destroy the back-off model (every optional integration becomes a startup landmine). leaf must preserve the time-separation: condition-not-met is a non-error recorded fact NOW; the failure surfaces LATER only when something actually needs the bean — and the report must be the bridge that lets the later error explain the earlier silent backoff. This is a discipline the report ENFORCES against Rust's grain, not a free inheritance.
- Spring exposes the report via DEBUG logging (--debug) AND a structured actuator JSON endpoint — both assume an always-available logging framework and an HTTP actuator. leaf is async-first with no servlet/actuator model and no mandated logging backend; the 'dump' must be a rust-native renderer (env-flag / explicit call, not a log level it doesn't own) and the 'structured export' must be a serde-shaped value any optional introspection crate can expose — the report cannot assume tracing is present (thread it as a weak `pkg?/feat` capability), so the two Spring delivery channels become a renderer + a serde value, not a log call + an endpoint.
- Spring's ConditionEvaluationReport is keyed by class/configuration name (the JVM's universal identity). Rust has no universal runtime name; an element's identity is whatever the deferred type-erasure/registry substrate picks (TypeId, descriptor index, qualified path) — and a generic guarded element has NO single symbol/identity at all. So the report's ElementId keying is hostage to the registry-substrate decision, and the later-failure enrichment ('look up why bean of type T backed off') depends on that key matching what autowiring-resolution queries by — a coupling Spring never has because class identity is global and uniform.
- Spring records reasons as already-formatted ConditionMessage strings at runtime. leaf's compile-gated-out elements have NO runtime moment to format a message — the reason ('feature redis not enabled') must be assembled from a STATIC gate descriptor (which feature/cfg) baked at compile time and the binary's resolved feature set read at runtime.
