So leaf's reason-authorship is split: runtime members author runtime strings (Spring-like), but cfg-tier members can only contribute a static gate template the report renders later — a dual reason-origin Spring's uniform-runtime model never needs.
- Reading 'which feature/cfg is enabled in THIS binary' to label a gated-out element is itself subtle in Rust (the cross-crate doc: the resolved feature set differs between `-p` and `--workspace`, is resolver-version-dependent, and can be flipped on by a sibling/test/example via unification). Spring's classpath is one unambiguous runtime fact; leaf's 'effective feature set' is a build-configuration-dependent answer the report must consume from a single authoritative snapshot, or its 'gated out: feature X off' labels will be untrustworthy across build invocations.
- Spring's report is populated 'for free' because a condition author writes a good ConditionMessage and the framework logs it. In leaf the report is one thing but the SUBSTRATE completeness is another: a record can be missing not because a condition said no, but because the contributing crate was never linked (Layer 0) or its registration was DCE'd — a silent EMPTY-iterable failure with no analogue in Spring's classpath. So leaf's report must ALSO be a substrate self-check (cross-reference an expected manifest), conflating 'this bean backed off (normal)' with 'this bean's registration silently vanished (a build bug)' as two distinct things the report must keep apart — a burden Spring's report never carries.
- Spring dumps the report via a logging side-channel that is inherently allowed to allocate/format freely at runtime. leaf's charter demands memory/concurrency discipline (#5) and reactive-hot/polling-cold (#4): the recorder must be a cold-path, single-owner, no-Arc/no-lock sink (recording is part of the existing bring-up pass, never its own loop or a hot-path bus), and rendering/export must be a deferred on-demand read — a stricter execution-context contract than Spring's free-wheeling DEBUG log.

### Interactions
- **conditions** — Hard upstream dependency and the PRODUCER of everything the report records. The conditions SPI owns the ConditionOutcome (matched + reason + which ConditionId), the two-phase planner, and the AND-fold / CondExpr evaluation; condition-report is the SINK the planner writes each outcome into. Co-review required: the SPI must expose a recording HOOK (the ConditionReportSink / DiagnosticObserver call point) at exactly the moment each element's verdict is decided, carrying the per-leaf outcomes (not just the final boolean) so the report can show boolean provenance. condition-report adds NO evaluation — it only defines the record schema the SPI emits into and freezes it.
- **condition-family** — The AUTHOR of the reason strings the report displays — the 'writing a good message IS the report output' rule. Each family member (OnProperty/OnBean/OnClass/…) produces the kind-specific human-readable reason ('OnProperty x.enabled: found "false", expected "true"'; 'OnClass: capability redis not compiled in'); condition-report records and presents them but does not author them. The CRITICAL co-design point: condition-family's per-kind TIER-MAP (cfg/build/runtime) is exactly what forces the report to be cross-tier (R3) — a cfg-tier OnClass has no runtime outcome, so condition-family and condition-report must agree on how a compile-gated-out element is made accountable (a static gate breadcrumb the report renders). The report should define a SHAPE for reasons (kind, expected, found) so family members produce consistent, machine-parseable messages.
- **auto-configuration / auto-config-ordering** — The principal real-world REASON the report exists and its heaviest consumer. Auto-config composes dozens of optional modules guarded by OnMissingBean/OnClass that back off silently — precisely the 'magic' that must stay accountable. When a developer asks 'why didn't the auto-configured redis client appear?', the answer is in the report: either 'backed off: user defined their own' (Negative OnMissingBean) or 'feature redis not enabled' (compile-gated-out, R3). condition-report turns auto-config's opaque backoff into a lookup. The report's record class 'Exclusion' maps to auto-config-ordering's exclusion sources (the @ConditionalOnX-independent exclude list); the report must record WHY an auto-config was excluded (explicit exclusion vs condition no-match) distinctly.
- **autowiring-resolution / bean-registry** — The consumer of the silent-now/loud-later BRIDGE. When autowiring-resolution fails to find a required bean (a NoSuchBean-style error), it queries the frozen Report by the missing type's ElementId; if that element has a Negative/compile-gated record, the error is enriched with 'candidate X backed off: <reason>' (R3 adds the actionable 'enable feature redis'). This is the realization of charter #9 (rich, complete, actionable diagnostics) and Spring's 'see that the bean backed off rather than broke'. Co-review: the ElementId the report keys by MUST match the key autowiring-resolution/bean-registry uses to look up candidates, so the join works — coupling both to the deferred registry-substrate keying decision.
- **startup-instrumentation** — Sibling diagnostic with a shared design pattern to reuse (unification #11). startup-instrumentation records a tree of named/timed startup steps, no-op by default, opt-in recording, stable tool-friendly taxonomy — EXACTLY the shape condition-report's recorder should adopt (no-op sink by default, opt-in, stable verdict-class taxonomy, cold-path single-owner). In R2 they are two consumers of the SAME unified diagnostics/observation model. Co-review: align the opt-in toggle, the no-op-default contract, and ideally the underlying observation channel so leaf has ONE startup-diagnostics mechanism, not two parallel ones.
- **environment / property-resolution** — Provides BOTH a condition input (read by OnProperty/OnProfile members whose outcomes the report records) AND the likely control surface for the report itself. The report's 'dump on startup' toggle is a leaf-native analogue of Spring's --debug — most naturally a property/env key (e.g. leaf.condition-report.enabled / a LEAF_DEBUG env var) resolved through the same Environment, read once on the cold path before/at the recording pass. The report reads no live property to RECORD (it records the SPI's outcomes); it reads one property to decide WHETHER to record/dump.
- **profiles** — Profile activation IS a condition (on_profile, a condition-family member over the same SPI), so a profile-gated element's match/no-match is recorded by the report like any other — 'OnProfile(prod): not active' becomes a Negative record. No special handling; profiles is just another reason-producing member whose outcomes the report accounts for. Relevant because 'why is my bean missing?' is very often 'the prod profile isn't active', which the report must surface clearly.
- **annotation-model** — Upstream provider of the element's declaration metadata and, via the stable proc_macro::Span APIs at macro-expansion, the PROVENANCE (file:line:col) the report bakes into each element descriptor so a record can cite the exact source line of the guarded declaration. Whatever annotation-model chooses for its descriptor shape determines where the report attaches its provenance + the gate descriptor; co-review so the report's per-element key and provenance live coherently on the same descriptor the annotation-model materializes.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — Owns the execution context the report records in. Recording is a fixed sub-step of bring-up: it happens during the conditions-SPI registration pass (after Environment sealed, after full definition set collected for register-phase, before eager singleton instantiation); the FREEZE is a one-shot transition at end-of-registration; the optional startup DUMP fires at a defined post-refresh point. The recorder is owned on the refresh stack (single owner, no Arc/lock, cold path). condition-report slots into this template; it never runs ad hoc or spawns its own task.
- **component-scanning / programmatic-registration** — Discovered components and programmatic registrations are guarded by condition-family members and their outcomes are recorded identically — the report is origin-agnostic. A dynamically-discovered (future WASM-sourced) definition has no compile-time cfg, so it can ONLY produce RUNTIME records (no compile-gated-out entry possible) — which means the report's runtime tier (R1) is the floor that must always exist even if R3's compile-time manifest is the default for native crates. Reinforces keeping the report's provider/record abstraction origin-agnostic.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Does condition-report get its OWN bespoke recorder/sink (R1) or is it one SUBSCRIBER on the deferred UNIFIED diagnostics/observation model (R2) shared with startup-instrumentation and the error model? This is the charter §3 'unified error/diagnostics model' decision applied here — resolving it decides whether the report is an island or a view, and whether condition-report even ships an evaluation-time mechanism vs just a schema + materializer.
- The CROSS-TIER reconciliation: is a runtime-only report acceptable (and the cfg-gated-out 'why is my bean missing?' case is answered some OTHER way), or must the report be a cross-tier ledger (R3) that anchors accountability data at compile/build time so compile-gated-out elements stay explainable? This is DIRECTLY contingent on the deferred conditional-strategy decision (cfg vs codegen vs runtime blend) — if conditions are predominantly runtime, R3's manifest earns little; if heavily cfg-driven, a runtime-only report is structurally blind to the most common failure.
- What is the ElementId / element-identity the report keys records by, and does it MATCH the key autowiring-resolution / bean-registry query by (so the silent-now/loud-later enrichment join works)? This is the deferred type-erasure & registry-substrate keystone applied to the report — and it must handle generic guarded elements that have no single symbol/identity.
- How is the binary's RESOLVED feature/cfg set obtained at runtime so the report can label a gated-out element 'feature redis not enabled' trustworthily, given the cross-crate doc's warning that this set differs between `-p`/`--workspace`, is resolver-dependent, and can be flipped by sibling/test/example unification? Needs a single authoritative resolved-feature snapshot mechanism — couples to the metadata/codegen-boundary decision.
- Should the report DOUBLE as the substrate's mandated DCE/Layer-0 self-check (R3's manifest-vs-outcomes cross-reference detecting silently-dropped registrations), or is that self-check a SEPARATE mechanism the report merely consumes? This conflates 'bean backed off (normal)' with 'registration silently vanished (build bug)' unless the boundary is decided — couples to the deferred cross-crate composition & tooling model.
- What are the report's DELIVERY channels in leaf's async-first, no-actuator world — an env/property-toggled text dump (the --debug analogue), a serde structured value an optional introspection/actuator crate exposes (the /actuator/conditions analogue), a tracing bridge (weak feature) — and which is the no-op default? Couples to whether leaf mandates any observation backend and to the bootstrap layer's diagnostic surface.
- Where does the report's IMMUTABLE frozen value live and what is its ownership/lifetime shape (a Box<[Record]> owned by the context vs an Arc handle for the later-failure enrichment callable from a hot resolution path)? An instance of the deferred scope/lifetime/ownership keystone applied to a diagnostic artifact that is written cold but read possibly-hot.
- For the dynamic/WASM 'second classpath': a WASM-sourced contribution has no compile-time cfg and no static manifest entry, so it can only produce RUNTIME records — does origin-agnosticism therefore make the runtime report tier (R1) MANDATORY as the floor even if R3's compile-time manifest is the native default, and how does a WASM-sourced backoff get provenance (no proc_macro::Span to bake)?
- Should the report taxonomy add a leaf-specific verdict class beyond Spring's positive/negative/exclusion/unconditional — specifically CompiledOutByCfg and BuildFoldedFalse for the static tiers — and is this taxonomy frozen in leaf-core ABI (so all producers/subscribers agree), accepting the ABI-evolution cost of changing it later?
- How do the report's reason strings stay machine-PARSEABLE (for tooling / a CI 'config drift' check) while remaining human-readable — does condition-report impose a structured reason shape (kind, expected, found, gate) on condition-family members, or accept free-form strings? Couples to how condition-family expresses attribute schemas (typed vs stringly) in annotation-model.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I designed condition-report STRICTLY as the diagnostic ACCOUNTING + PRESENTATION sink — the record schema (positive/negative/exclusion/unconditional + leaf's compile-gated-out class), the collection point/lifetime, the startup dump + structured export, and the silent-now/loud-later bridge into the error model. I deliberately did NOT redesign the predicate contract / two-phase planner / ConditionOutcome (that is `conditions`), the parameterized member set or their reason-string authorship (`condition-family`), the attribute metadata view (`annotation-model`), or the profile grammar (`profiles`). The report COLLECTS outcomes and reasons; it never evaluates conditions or authors reasons — faithful to Spring's 'a good ConditionMessage IS the report output' rule.

The genuinely divergent axis for THIS feature is NOT 'how is a predicate evaluated' (the SPI's axis) but WHERE AND HOW THE ACCOUNT LIVES AND IS DELIVERED: R1 = a dedicated runtime SINK owned by refresh, frozen to an immutable value, dumped/exported by readers, with a no-op default (simplest, most faithful to Spring's shape, single clean mental model — but BLIND to compile-gated-out elements, the leaf-defining gap); R2 = the report as ONE SUBSCRIBER on a unified diagnostics/observation model shared with startup-instrumentation/error/tracing (maximal unification #11, open/closed extensibility, but depends on a Phase-2-deferred model and risks conflating a cold-path diagnostic with the async hot-path event bus); R3 = a cross-tier ACCOUNTABILITY LEDGER anchoring a compile/build-time manifest of every guarded element fused at runtime with outcomes + the resolved feature set (the ONLY realization that can explain 'feature redis not enabled' — closes leaf's defining gap and yields Spring-'Action:'-grade actionable diagnostics, but adds a second cross-crate surface, unconditional binary-size cost, and is contingent on the deferred conditional-strategy decision).

These are COMPOSABLE, not exclusive — the likely shape is R1's runtime sink as the always-present FLOOR (mandatory because WASM-sourced/dynamic contributions can ONLY produce runtime records), R2's unified-subscriber framing as the DELIVERY/extensibility architecture (so the report, startup-instrumentation, tracing, and an actuator endpoint share one mechanism), and R3's compile-time manifest as the COMPLETENESS layer for native crates (and the doubling-as-substrate-self-check the cross-crate doc mandates). The single most important Phase-2 dependency this feature exposes is that condition-report's depth is HOSTAGE to three deferred meta-decisions at once: the unified diagnostics model (R2's whole premise), the conditional strategy / cfg-vs-runtime blend (whether R3's cross-tier ledger is necessary or over-engineered), and the type-erasure/registry-substrate keying (whether the later-failure enrichment join even works).

Two sub-intents to keep separate in Phase 2: (a) the report as a per-element ACCOUNT of why things did/didn't register (Spring's literal report) vs (b) the report as a SUBSTRATE SELF-CHECK detecting silently-dropped registrations (a leaf-specific need with no Spring analogue, because Rust's empty-iterable DCE failure has no classpath equivalent). R3 deliberately fuses these (the manifest is both the account AND the expected-element list), which is elegant but couples two concerns Phase 2 may want separate.

Critical grounding honored: nothing needs nightly — owned structs + serde for the structured export, the stable proc_macro::Span line/file APIs (1.88) for provenance, the stable diagnostic namespace for the later-failure enrichment, no async-trait tax (recording is synchronous cold-path). Memory/concurrency discipline (#5): the recorder is a single cold-path owner, &mut append, NO Arc/NO lock, frozen to immutable — never a hot-path bus or a polling loop (reactive/cold #4). No-op-by-default mirrors startup-instrumentation's opt-in recording for zero overhead when off (#2). The report adds no NEW cross-crate discovery surface in R1/R2 (it consumes the conditions substrate's outcomes); R3's manifest DOES add one and inherits the full Layer-0/DCE/force-link/self-check obligations — flagged as its heaviest cost. The silent-now/loud-later time-separation (research lines 2231-2235) is the load-bearing invariant the report exists to serve and must NOT collapse into Rust's eager-Result bias. Co-review partners: `conditions` (the recording hook + per-leaf outcomes), `condition-family` (reason-string shape + the cfg-tier gated-out breadcrumb), `startup-instrumentation` (shared no-op/opt-in/cold-path diagnostic pattern), `autowiring-resolution`/`bean-registry` (the ElementId join for later-failure enrichment), and the eventual unified error/diagnostics model. No existing source to build on — leaf has only an empty src/lib.rs.

## Auto-Configuration Engine  `[auto-configuration]`

This feature is the ENGINE that orchestrates leaf's "opinionated defaults that never fight the user." It is Spring Boot's `AutoConfigurationImportSelector` + the surrounding `@EnableAutoConfiguration`/`@SpringBootApplication` wiring (doc 1174-1262) — distinct from its three SUPPLIERS already designed upstream: it CONSUMES import-composition's deferred-group machinery (the WHEN), auto-config-ordering's three-pass sort + exclusion merge (the HOW-ordered), and condition-family's OnMissingBean/OnClass members (the HOW-gated). What auto-configuration OWNS is the assembly pipeline and the philosophy: (1) the CANDIDATE-SET ASSEMBLY from a per-library "imports manifest" — Spring's `META-INF/spring/...AutoConfiguration.imports` (one FQCN/line, every jar contributes its own, `ImportCandidates.load` scans all of them, dedup) — the rust-native analogue of "every library declares its opinionated defaults"; (2) the DEFERRED RUN: auto-config is processed AFTER all user config so `@ConditionalOnMissingBean` sees the FINAL user-bean set and backs off (`DeferredImportSelector`, ORDER=LOWEST_PRECEDENCE-1) — the load-bearing intent is that DEFERRAL EXISTS FOR @Conditional CORRECTNESS, not performance (doc 1204, 1166-1170); (3) the GLOBAL BATCH: `AutoConfigurationGroup` unions every contributor's candidates, subtracts exclusions, sorts the WHOLE set once, registers as one ordered batch (doc 1216); (4) the TWO-PHASE FAST PATH: a build-time annotation processor emits `spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties` so OnClass/OnBean/OnWebApplication PRE-FILTER candidates via ASM metadata WITHOUT loading the class — discarding most of hundreds of candidates cheaply, and why OnClass can name an absent class safely (doc 1220-1226); (5) auto-configs are LITE-ONLY configs by mandate (`@AutoConfiguration` hardwires proxyBeanMethods=false — hundreds of them, CGLIB-proxying each is too expensive; they wire via @Bean-method parameters and never self-call) (doc 1184-1188); (6) the kill-switch `spring.boot.enableautoconfiguration=false` (doc 1218); (7) `@ImportAutoConfiguration` test-slice mode that applies the SAME rules to an explicit curated subset, with `optional:` prefixes (doc 1240-1242); (8) the CONTRACT "names are public API, contents are not" (doc 1244) and `AutoConfigurationExcludeFilter` ensuring a scanned auto-config enters ONLY via the import path, exactly once (doc 1180). The core philosophy (doc 1166-1170): guard every auto-configured bean with OnMissingBean + order strictly after user config, so the user's bean SILENTLY WINS with zero opt-out flags — inverting the usual opt-out-flag default; conditional backoff is declarative and self-documenting, and the ConditionEvaluationReport (doc 1160-1164) keeps the "magic" accountable. leaf must replicate this WHOLE orchestration — multi-crate opinionated-default contribution, deferral-for-correctness, global ordered batch, cheap pre-filter, lite-only configs, kill-switch, exclusions, curated test-slice mode, and accountable backoff — WITHOUT the JVM mechanism it rests on: a runtime classpath, `classLoader.getResources` scanning every jar's .imports file, ASM metadata reading, and reflective FQCN resolution. The deepest question (entangling §3's metadata/codegen-boundary, compile-vs-runtime split, conditional strategy, AND dependency-based-auto-config keystones) is HOW MUCH of this pipeline is build-time-frozen vs runtime, and how a crate's "starter" presence (the Spring-starter analogue) maps onto Cargo features + force-link given Rust has no classpath.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Runtime deferred-batch engine: per-crate AutoConfigManifest contributed over the descriptor stream, assembled + ordered + condition-filtered in a single cold deferred phase after user definitions
Realize the engine as a RUNTIME deferred-batch orchestrator, the most faithful port of `AutoConfigurationImportSelector`. Each leaf integration crate ships an AUTO-CONFIG MANIFEST — the rust-native analogue of `META-INF/spring/...AutoConfiguration.imports`: a `#[auto_configuration]`-marked lite config in the crate emits a thin `const AutoConfigDescriptor` (id/TypeId/stable_name/order/before/after/condition-refs/lite-config seeds) onto the SAME descriptor stream configuration-classes feeds, addressed by the auto-config marker so it is distinguishable from a user config. The engine runs ONE deferred phase in refresh-lifecycle, AFTER all eager user configs + user definitions are registered (the deferral-for-correctness moment):\n\n```\nfn run_autoconfig(env: &Environment, user_defs: &DefinitionRegistry,\n                  candidates: &[&AutoConfigDescriptor]) -> Result<(), AutoConfigError> {\n  if env.flag(\"leaf.enable-autoconfiguration\") == Some(false) { return Ok(()); } // kill-switch\n  let excl = ExclusionSet::merge(typed_exclude, exclude_name, env.list(\"leaf.autoconfigure.exclude\"));\n  let cands = dedup_by_id(candidates).filter(|c| !excl.contains(c));\n  check_excluded(&excl, &whole_binary_inventory)?;            // typo-guard (delegated)\n  let ordered = auto_config_ordering::order_batch(&cands, &excl)?; // delegated 3-pass sort\n  for c in ordered {                                          // batch register, in order\n    if conditions::all_match(c.conditions, &ConditionCtx{ env, defs: user_defs, .. }) {\n      user_defs.register_lite(c.seeds);   // defs now visible to later candidates' OnMissingBean\n    } // else: graceful no-bean, recorded in the report\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe phase is GLOBAL (one batch across every crate, dedup by id, ordered once — import-composition's Group semantics), DEFERRED (after user defs, so OnMissingBean backs off correctly — doc 1166), and INCREMENTAL within the batch (each registered candidate's seeds become visible to LATER candidates' OnMissingBean, mirroring Spring's definition-order-drives-condition-correctness, doc 1234). Auto-configs are LITE-ONLY by the macro mandate (proxyBeanMethods=false has no analogue beyond 'never self-call', which leaf gets for free since #[bean] methods are parameter-injected — the macro can lint a self-call). `@ImportAutoConfiguration` test-slice mode = a `slice!(WebStack, DataLayer)` that runs the SAME engine over an EXPLICIT curated candidate list instead of the full contributed set, with `optional` entries skipped if not linked. The 'starter' analogue: enabling a Cargo feature compiles the integration crate's #[auto_configuration] descriptor AND (via the generated enable!/app-root) force-links it — both required (cfg gates compilation, not linkage).

**Pros:** Most faithful to the Spring engine's vocabulary and the deferral-for-CORRECTNESS soul: a single deferred phase after user defs, incremental in-batch registration so OnMissingBean sees a growing definition set exactly as Spring's definition-order semantics intend (doc 1234) — the 'opinionated but always overridable' philosophy (doc 1166) is realized directly, not approximated.; Origin-agnostic by construction: candidates ride the SAME descriptor stream as user configs, so a native crate, a test-double, or a future dynamic/WASM-module-contributed auto-config is assembled, ordered, and condition-gated by the IDENTICAL engine — no member assumes native construction (the mandated origin-agnostic provider seam).; Cleanly DELEGATES to the three upstream suppliers (import-composition's deferred Group phase = the WHEN; auto-config-ordering's order_batch = the sort/exclusion-merge; condition-family's all_match = the gate), so this feature stays a thin orchestrator — maximal unification (§2.11), minimal new machinery, no reinvention.; Pure runtime function over collected descriptors → trivially unit-testable: feed a candidate list + user defs + env, assert which seeds registered, which backed off, and the report — without a container build, the link step, or a real runtime; highest-confidence validation of the orchestration.; Substrate-neutral and Phase-2-non-committal: the candidate table can arrive via linkme (Arch A/B), build-codegen (Arch C), or explicit with() (Arch D); the engine is identical, so this realization does NOT pre-decide the metadata/codegen boundary.

**Cons:** Pays full RUNTIME assembly cost every startup (dedup + exclusion merge + sort + per-candidate condition eval) over potentially HUNDREDS of candidates — without a cheap pre-filter this is the exact cost Spring's build-time metadata fast-path (doc 1220-1226) exists to avoid; leaf must lean hard on a cheap Parse-phase prune (OnClass-as-cfg already removes absent-capability candidates at COMPILE time) or low-overhead (§2.2) suffers on cold start.; The candidate set's COMPLETENESS rides every cross-crate DCE hazard: an auto-config in a crate the binary never force-links is silently absent (Layer 0), yielding a smaller batch, a silently-different alphabetical base order, and a real exclusion that looks like a typo — so the engine HARD-DEPENDS on the mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per source crate) to avoid shipping a binary silently missing opinionated defaults.; The auto-config descriptor registry is a second cross-crate discovery surface (the 'is-this-an-auto-config' marker channel) inheriting Layer-0/-A/-B hazards distinct from the user-config stream — if the integration crate isn't force-linked, its opinionated default simply never appears, and the only signal is an unexpectedly bare object graph.; Incremental in-batch registration couples the engine tightly to refresh-lifecycle phase ordering AND to the (Phase-2-undecided) conditional strategy: WHEN exactly OnMissingBean is evaluated relative to each candidate's registration determines correctness, and if conditions are partly compile-time (cfg) the 'sees the growing set' guarantee needs care to preserve.; The Cargo-feature-as-starter mapping is leaky: a feature gates COMPILATION but not LINKAGE, so 'enable the redis starter' can compile the auto-config and still leave an empty registry unless force-link fires — coupling this feature's user-facing 'add a starter' mental model to the unresolved cross-crate composition decision, and requiring a self-check that warns when an enabled feature contributed ZERO candidates.

**Mechanisms considered:** per-crate AutoConfigManifest as thin const AutoConfigDescriptor on the SHARED descriptor stream (rust-native analogue of the per-jar .imports file), marked so the engine distinguishes auto-config from user config; single DEFERRED runtime phase in refresh-lifecycle after all user defs (deferral-for-conditional-correctness — doc 1166/1204), with INCREMENTAL in-batch registration so each candidate's seeds feed later candidates' OnMissingBean (doc 1234 definition-order semantics); GLOBAL batch: dedup-by-id + exclusion-subtract + single sort across ALL crates (import-composition Group semantics — doc 1216), delegating the 3-pass sort to auto-config-ordering and the gate to condition-family; kill-switch via leaf.enable-autoconfiguration=false Environment flag short-circuiting the whole batch (doc 1218); three-source exclusion merge (typed + name + Environment property) + check_excluded typo-guard, delegated to auto-config-ordering; slice!() curated-subset mode (= @ImportAutoConfiguration test slices, doc 1240) running the SAME engine over an explicit list with optional-if-absent entries; Cargo-feature-as-starter: feature gates compilation AND triggers force-link via generated enable!/app-root (cfg gates compilation not linkage — both required); self-check warns on enabled-feature-zero-candidates; linkme distributed-slice default 'classpath' of candidates PLUS optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source contributing additional candidates — CANDIDATES, both feed one batch; lite-only mandate enforced + self-call lint by the macro

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization that confronts 'every library declares its opinionated defaults' head-on without a classpath. Spring's `ImportCandidates.load` scans EVERY jar's `.imports` file via `classLoader.getResources`; leaf has no classpath, so the per-crate manifest becomes a thin const AutoConfigDescriptor collected via the substrate (linkme slice default / build-codegen / explicit with()). The 'starter' is a `dep:`-hidden umbrella Cargo feature over the integration crate (the Spring-starter analogue the cross-crate doc endorses): enabling it must do TWO things — gate compilation of the crate's #[auto_configuration] descriptor AND cause the generated app-root to emit a force-link `use leaf_redis as _;` — because a feature alone gates compilation, NOT link retention (doc 201-208), so 'enabled the starter' can still yield an EMPTY registry. The engine therefore MANDATES the anti-DCE self-check: count expected-vs-found auto-config descriptors per source crate (and warn loudly when an enabled feature contributed ZERO), turning a silently-bare object graph into an early rich diagnostic (the worst-trait silent-failure trap, doc 152). The auto-config marker + the whole-binary inventory the typo-guard consults must be complete; a crate the binary never references is absent (Layer 0), making a real exclusion look like a typo — so check_excluded must say 'excluded X — no such auto-config among N candidates from M crates'. Stable cross-crate identity is dual: a TypeId for typed exclude/before/after refs (DCE-safe, path-references the target) plus a canonical module_path-derived stable_name for name-based exclude_name and the leaf.autoconfigure.exclude Environment property (the class-names-as-public-API contract, doc 1244 — resolved at runtime against the candidate name index). Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → macro hard-errors with a register_auto_config!(Concrete) shim. The two-source duality applies: the link-time/codegen candidate set is the default 'classpath'; an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source contributes additional candidates whose seeds bridge into the module — gated by the same runtime conditions, assembled indistinguishably (origin-agnostic) — CANDIDATE, not a decision. leaf-core hosts the AutoConfigDescriptor/marker/condition-ref ABI (absolute paths in emitted code); leaf-boot hosts the engine (matching charter §6 topology).

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely COLD-PATH, single-threaded planning logic — there is no hot path and nothing async in the engine itself; only the eventual lite-config #[bean] Factories run async/hot. The deferred phase runs ONCE, synchronously, in the refresh-lifecycle planning window AFTER the Environment is sealed and ALL eager user configs + user definitions are registered (the deferral moment that makes OnMissingBean backoff correct), and BEFORE any bean Factory is invoked. It is pure CPU + in-memory reads: read the kill-switch flag (sync in-memory), merge exclusions (one source is the leaf.autoconfigure.exclude property — a sync in-memory read; the Environment is populated this early), dedup, delegate to the sort, then iterate the ordered batch evaluating each candidate's conditions against the read-mostly ConditionCtx (env + the growing definition set) and registering seeds incrementally. It MUST NOT block, do IO, or be async — mirroring the read-mostly ConditionContext discipline (doc 1116-1124); any candidate condition that 'wants to await' (e.g. probe a network) is a design smell whose work belongs to a bean Factory, not the planning phase. Cancellation is irrelevant (short synchronous phase; if startup is cancelled it simply isn't called). ERRORS propagate as a planning-phase Result (AutoConfigError): a kill-switch is not an error, a graceful condition no-match is a recorded report entry (NOT an error — preserving 'opinionated defaults that back off', doc 1166), but a typo-guarded bad exclusion, an ordering cycle (from the delegated sort), or a missing-candidate self-check failure surfaces at the earliest-richest point (§2.9) with full context — strictly before any async construction. The OUTPUT fixes DEFINITION registration order/contents; instantiation order stays dependency-driven in the async phase (doc 1234 boundary preserved as an execution-context boundary the engine never crosses). At the dyn edge, a lite-config's async Factory is boxed-future (RPITIT/AFIT not dyn-safe — nightly doc 162/171), per the shared configuration-classes seam.

#### R2 — Capability-keyed dependency-based engine: 'starter present' is a CAPABILITY fact; auto-config is gated primarily by OnCapability (cfg/feature) with OnMissingBean as the runtime backoff, candidate set scoped by enabled capabilities not a global manifest
Lean into the cross-crate doc's 'Cargo features are the natural analogue of the classpath deciding the wiring' and probe the DEPENDENCY-BASED-AUTO-CONFIG keystone (§3): instead of one global manifest scanned at runtime (R1), make a CAPABILITY (an enabled, force-linked integration crate) the PRIMARY gate. Each integration crate's #[auto_configuration] is compiled ONLY when its capability feature is on (`#[cfg(feature = \"redis\")]` on the descriptor), so the candidate set is SCOPED to enabled capabilities by COMPILATION — the rust-native 'read without loading': an absent optional dependency is physically removed, OnClass-against-absent-class can NEVER error (the cleanest realization of doc 1224's intent). The engine then runs over a MUCH SMALLER candidate set (only enabled capabilities), so the expensive global filter Spring needs (doc 1220) is largely unnecessary — most of the prune happened at compile time.\n\nConditions split into TWO tiers the engine treats distinctly:\n- OnCapability / OnClass-analogue = COMPILE-TIME cfg/feature fact (gates whether the candidate exists at all);\n- OnMissingBean / OnProperty / OnProfile = RUNTIME backoff (gates whether the present candidate WIRES, after user defs).\n\nSo a Spring 'starter brings opinionated defaults that back off' becomes: ADD the dependency (capability on → candidate compiled + force-linked) → the auto-config's beans wire UNLESS the user already defined them (OnMissingBean) or overrode a property (OnProperty). The deferred runtime phase still runs (for OnMissingBean correctness) but over the capability-scoped set:\n\n```\n#[auto_configuration(capability = \"redis\")]   // cfg(feature=\"redis\") gates the whole descriptor\nmod redis_autoconfig {\n  #[bean]\n  #[on_missing_bean(RedisClient)]            // runtime backoff\n  #[on_property(\"leaf.redis.url\")]            // runtime gate\n  async fn redis_client(env: &Environment) -> RedisClient { .. }\n}\n```\n\nThe ENGINE's job shrinks to: collect capability-scoped candidates → order → run the runtime-backoff conditions → register. 'Opinionated' = the defaults ship with the capability; 'overridable' = OnMissingBean/OnProperty. This is the DEPENDENCY-BASED model (the candidate set is a function of which capabilities are linked), held explicitly as a CANDIDATE probing the §3 'does dependency-based auto-config exist?' question.

**Pros:** Strongest, most HONEST 'read without loading' (doc 1224 intent): cfg-gating physically removes an absent optional dependency, so naming a missing capability can NEVER cause a build/link error — a cleaner guarantee than Spring's ASM trick, and it eliminates the per-startup global-filter cost (most candidates were pruned at COMPILE time, the rust-native version of Boot's build-time spring-autoconfigure-metadata pre-filter, doc 1226).; Best low-overhead (§2.2): the candidate set is already scoped to enabled capabilities, so the runtime deferred phase iterates a SMALL set and evaluates only the runtime-backoff conditions — no hundreds-of-candidate global prune; closest to the Spring fast-path's actual effect without a runtime ASM pass.; Maps the 'add a Spring starter → get opinionated defaults' mental model directly onto idiomatic Rust (add a dependency / enable a capability feature) — arguably the MOST intuitive DX for a Rust user (§2.1), and the cleanest expression of the cross-crate doc's 'enabling a feature is the analogue of adding a starter'.; Earliest-richest diagnostics for the capability tier (§2.9): a misspelled capability or an impossible cfg is a COMPILE error with a span; an enabled-capability-with-zero-wired-beans is a loud self-check — beating Spring's runtime-only no-match for the class-presence dimension.; Probes the dependency-based-auto-config keystone concretely (a §3/§5 deferred decision), giving Phase 2 a worked candidate for 'the candidate set is a function of linked capabilities' rather than 'a global manifest scanned at runtime' — high signal for the meta-architecture.

**Cons:** PRE-LEANS on the dependency-based-auto-config keystone (§3 explicitly defers 'whether it exists at all and its ripple effects') AND the conditional strategy — presenting capability-as-primary-gate biases those signals hard; must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, the most coupled-to-undecided-meta-architecture of the three on the gating axis.; cfg-as-condition collides with Cargo feature semantics: features only OR-on, can't be un-set, and a sibling test/example can flip a capability on for a binary that never asked (unification) — so a capability gate is only honest for ADDITIVE presence; any 'backend A xor B' auto-config (which Spring does with mutually-exclusive OnProperty) MUST stay a runtime/profile decision, a discipline the engine must enforce and document per capability (doc 190-194).; cfg gating compilation does NOT force LINK retention (Layer 0): a capability-true auto-config must ALSO trigger force-link of the integration crate, coupling this feature to the discovery-substrate decision more tightly than R1 — the cfg verdict and the force-link must stay consistent or the 'enabled' opinionated default silently vanishes (doc 201-208).; Splits the engine's mental model across compile-time (capability) and runtime (backoff) — a 'why didn't my auto-config wire' answer comes from TWO places (gated out at compile time vs backed off at startup), which must be reconciled into ONE accountable report (doc 1160) or the 'magic' becomes harder to debug, not easier.; Diverges from Spring's actual mechanism where OnClass is a RUNTIME condition over the full candidate set (Spring DOES scan all .imports regardless of which starter you added, then filters) — leaf's compile-scoping is intent-faithful but mechanism-divergent, and it cannot express a candidate that should be considered-then-rejected for diagnostic transparency (it's simply absent), weakening the ConditionEvaluationReport's 'we considered X and it didn't match' accountability for the capability dimension.

**Mechanisms considered:** CAPABILITY (enabled+force-linked integration crate) as the PRIMARY gate; #[cfg(feature=\"x\")] on the whole #[auto_configuration] descriptor so the candidate set is scoped by COMPILATION (rust-native read-without-loading, doc 1224); two-tier conditions: OnCapability/OnClass = compile-time cfg/feature fact; OnMissingBean/OnProperty/OnProfile = runtime backoff after user defs; deferred runtime phase still runs (for OnMissingBean correctness) but over the SMALL capability-scoped candidate set — compile-time prune replaces Spring's runtime global filter (doc 1220-1226); 'add a dependency / enable a capability feature' = the rust-native 'add a Spring starter' (cross-crate doc 177/196-208); dependency-based-auto-config probed as a CANDIDATE (§3); capability-true MUST also force-link the integration crate (cfg gates compilation not linkage — both required); self-check warns on enabled-capability-zero-wired-beans; additive-capability discipline: backend-choice stays runtime/profile (mutually-exclusive features unsupported — doc 190-194); macro/lint enforces per capability; compile-time + runtime outcomes reconciled into ONE accountable condition report (doc 1160-1164) distinguishing 'compile-gated-out' from 'runtime-backed-off'; linkme/codegen/explicit substrate for the capability-scoped candidates PLUS optional dynamic WASM-module source (which has NO capability cfg → gated only by runtime conditions) — CANDIDATES

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The realization MOST entangled with T1 and the deepest probe of 'starter = capability'. A capability is a `dep:`-hidden umbrella Cargo feature over the integration crate; enabling it gates compilation of the #[auto_configuration] descriptor AND must trigger force-link (`use leaf_redis as _;`) from the generated app-root — both required because cfg gates compilation NOT linkage (doc 201-208), else empty registry. resolver=3 is MANDATORY so a sibling/test/build feature doesn't flip a capability on for a production binary that never asked (feature unification correctness, documented to differ between -p and --workspace, doc 184-188/209). Because the candidate set is compile-scoped, the runtime engine sees a SMALLER, capability-determined set — the rust-native version of dependency-based auto-config, where 'what could contribute' is answered by link-time capabilities and 'what does wire' by runtime backoff (doc 209). The build.rs/proc-macro single-crate wall matters less here than in a build-time-freeze approach because the gating is per-crate cfg (each crate gates its own descriptor) — but cross-crate 'is bean X defined elsewhere' is structurally RUNTIME (OnMissingBean), never a capability fact, so the two-tier split is forced by T1, not chosen. The anti-DCE self-check is still mandatory (a capability-true-but-not-force-linked crate → silently absent default → warn loudly). wasm/embedded (no reliable link sections) push MORE of the gating to capability/cfg (Architecture C territory) — making this the more portable substrate there, but the dynamic WASM-module source is the awkward case: a WASM-contributed auto-config has NO capability cfg and no Rust type, so it can ONLY be gated by RUNTIME conditions and must compose indistinguishably (origin-agnostic) — a flagged tension. Generics hard-error with a concrete shim. Stable identity dual (TypeId + module_path stable_name) as in R1 for exclude/before/after refs.

**T2 — execution context:** Split across COMPILE-TIME (capability tier) and COLD-PATH RUNTIME (backoff tier); no hot path, nothing async in the engine. Capability gates are decided at COMPILATION — the descriptor is simply present or absent; the only failure surface is compile_error!/cargo::error for an unknown feature or a contradictory cfg (§2.9, earliest possible). The runtime backoff tier behaves like R1: a single deferred, synchronous, non-blocking planning phase after the Environment is sealed and all user defs are registered, evaluating OnMissingBean/OnProperty/OnProfile over the read-mostly ConditionCtx and registering the surviving capability-scoped candidates' seeds incrementally (so later candidates' OnMissingBean sees the growing set). MUST NOT block/IO/await; cancellation irrelevant (short synchronous phase). ERRORS: capability failures at compile time; runtime failures (a backoff condition typo, an ordering cycle from the delegated sort, a self-check missing-candidate) at the cold planning phase, still before async construction; a graceful runtime backoff is a recorded report entry, NOT an error (preserving 'opinionated but overridable', doc 1166). The cross-tier RECONCILIATION point is the report: a capability-gated-out auto-config contributes a 'compile-time gated out (capability redis absent)' entry; a runtime-backed-off one a 'startup no-match (OnMissingBean found user RedisClient)' entry — both threaded to one accountable account (doc 1160-1164) so the 'why didn't my default wire' answer is single and coherent despite the two timing tiers. Lite-config Factories run async/boxed-future at the dyn edge in the later instantiation phase (doc 162/171), unchanged; the definition-order-vs-creation-order boundary (doc 1234) is preserved.

#### R3 — Build-time frozen auto-config plan: leaf-codegen aggregates per-crate manifests via cargo metadata, runs the assembly + ordering + build-decidable filtering at build time, emits an inspectable plan; runtime evaluates only the residual OnMissingBean backoff
Question whether the assembly/ordering/filtering must happen at runtime at all. Spring ALREADY reads conditions/order/before/after from build-time `spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties` (doc 1226) precisely to avoid runtime cost — R3 is exactly that intent made first-class and inspectable (the sqlx model the cross-crate doc endorses, Arch C). A leaf-codegen pass (build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare`) in the binary crate reads a per-crate MANIFEST of auto-config descriptors (each integration crate emits its candidates + order/before/after + BUILD-DECIDABLE conditions as a build-time const descriptor / manifest entry, aggregated via cargo metadata), then AT BUILD TIME does what `AutoConfigurationImportSelector` does at runtime:\n(a) UNION every crate's candidates, dedup by id;\n(b) merge the BUILD-KNOWN exclusion sources (the app's typed exclude + exclude_name) + run check_excluded against the build-known inventory (typo-guard at BUILD time — earliest possible);\n(c) evaluate BUILD-DECIDABLE conditions to PRUNE — OnClass/OnCapability (is the crate/feature in the resolved graph?), known target-cfg, build-config — the rust-native equivalent of the ASM pre-filter (doc 1220-1224);\n(d) run auto-config-ordering's three-pass sort + cycle detection over the survivors;\n(e) emit a FROZEN, ordered `autoconfig_plan.rs` (include!'d into the binary): a flat ordered list of (candidate id, lite-config seeds, the RESIDUAL runtime-only conditions — chiefly OnMissingBean, which needs the live user-definition set).\n\nThe runtime then does NEAR-NOTHING: read the kill-switch + the leaf.autoconfigure.exclude Environment property (the only RUNTIME exclusion source — subtract order-preservingly), then iterate the frozen ordered plan evaluating ONLY the residual OnMissingBean/OnProperty backoff against the user defs, registering seeds incrementally. The generated `autoconfig_plan.rs` is the killer feature: a human-readable, checked-in, `--check`-able manifest of the ENTIRE opinionated-default batch (which candidates, in what order, gated out why, residual conditions) — the strongest realization of Spring's build-time-metadata intent AND the anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time plan DIFF rather than a runtime count. A cycle, a typo-guarded bad exclusion, or a duplicate fails the BUILD.

**Pros:** Earliest-richest diagnostics of all three (§2.9): an ordering cycle, a bad exclusion, or a duplicate fails at BUILD time with the offending contributor named and the FULL proposed batch inspectable in the generated file; the `--check` catches a silently-changed batch or a lost contributor in CI (the anti-DCE self-check as a build-time DIFF, doc 235) — strictly earlier than R1/R2's cold phase.; Lowest startup overhead (§2.2): the union + dedup + exclusion merge + build-decidable prune + three-pass sort all run at BUILD time and freeze into a flat ordered slice; runtime only subtracts the late Environment-property exclusions (order-preserving) and evaluates the residual OnMissingBean backoff — near-zero cold-start cost, the truest analogue of Boot's build-time spring-autoconfigure-metadata fast-path (doc 1226).; Fully platform-independent (Arch C): no link-time sections, so it works cleanly on wasm/embedded/staticlib where R1/R2's linkme-fed candidate tables are fragile (doc 171/225); the frozen plan NAMES every candidate, force-linking them and sidestepping all three DCE layers for the PLANNED batch (doc 232).; The generated, checked-in, inspectable ordered plan IS the documentation of the app's opinionated-default batch — exceptional debuggability ('why did X order before Y, why was Y gated out'), a single legible artifact far better than reconstructing a runtime decision, and the natural place to attach the ConditionEvaluationReport's compile-time-gated entries (doc 1160-1164).; Most faithful to Spring's ACTUAL fast-path mechanism (doc 1220-1226 — Boot reads order/before/after/conditions from a build-time generated metadata file) rather than re-deciding it at runtime; this is the realization Spring itself converged toward for performance and native-image friendliness.

**Cons:** PRE-DECIDES the metadata/codegen boundary AND the compile-vs-runtime split (both explicit §3 keystones) — presenting build-time freezing as THE shape biases those signals hard; must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, the most coupled-to-undecided-meta-architecture of the three (the deepest reason it cannot be the lone Phase-1 answer).; CROSS-CRATE is the structural wall: a build.rs/proc-macro sees ONLY its own crate (doc 121/232), so the binary's codegen cannot introspect foreign crates' auto-config annotations directly — each contributor crate must emit a build-time MANIFEST/const descriptor the binary's pass aggregates via cargo metadata, a convention with NO compiler enforcement; a contributor that forgets its manifest entry is silently absent and only the plan diff catches it.; The Environment-property exclusion (leaf.autoconfigure.exclude), the kill-switch, AND every OnMissingBean/OnProperty backoff are inherently RUNTIME (not known at build time) — so the model is NOT purely build-time; it is build-frozen-batch + a runtime residual (exclusion subtract + backoff eval). The frozen/residual SEAM is a new authoring/ops surface and a confusion source ('why didn't my build-time plan change when I set the exclude property?' — because property exclusions are residual by design).; Heaviest machinery of the three (a manifest convention, a cargo-metadata aggregator, the union/dedup/exclusion-merge/typo-guard/build-prune/three-pass-sort in codegen, the plan emitter, a `--check`) — in tension with thin-macros (§2.10) UNLESS all heavy logic lives in a normal leaf-codegen crate the macro merely feeds (which the charter permits, §2.10/§6); still the most to specify, keep idempotent (OUT_DIR hygiene, deterministic codegen), and test.; A dynamically-loaded WASM-module auto-config has NO build-time presence (not in the cargo graph), so it cannot participate in the frozen plan and must be assembled/ordered/condition-gated at RUNTIME — reintroducing a (smaller) runtime engine for exactly the dynamic case; the frozen-plan shape and the dynamic-directory 'classpath' are in direct tension here, a flagged Phase-2 question.

**Mechanisms considered:** leaf-codegen (build.rs / cargo leaf prepare) aggregates per-crate auto-config manifests via cargo metadata and runs the WHOLE AutoConfigurationImportSelector pipeline (union/dedup → exclusion merge + typo-guard → build-decidable prune → three-pass sort) at BUILD time; build-decidable conditions (OnClass/OnCapability = crate/feature in resolved graph, target-cfg, build-config) evaluated at build to PRUNE — rust-native analogue of the ASM build-time metadata pre-filter (doc 1220-1226); emit a frozen, ordered autoconfig_plan.rs (include!'d): flat ordered (id, lite-config seeds, RESIDUAL runtime conditions); residual = OnMissingBean/OnProperty/the leaf.autoconfigure.exclude property + kill-switch; split conditions BUILD-decidable (pruned at build) vs RUNTIME-residual (OnMissingBean over live user defs) — the deferral-for-correctness moment realized as build-order + runtime-residual; checked-in, --check-able plan as both the anti-DCE self-check (build-time DIFF, doc 235) and the app's opinionated-default-batch documentation (the ConditionEvaluationReport's compile-gated entries attach here); per-crate manifest/const-descriptor convention aggregated via cargo metadata (the binary's build can't read foreign annotations — the hard single-crate wall, doc 121/232); runtime residual engine ONLY for dynamic WASM-module candidates with no build presence + the runtime backoff — fallback reintroducing a small runtime pass; CANDIDATE not a decision; native analogue of Boot's spring-autoconfigure-metadata fast-path (doc 1226) made first-class + inspectable

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Strongest fit for the build-time-codegen substrate (Arch C, the sqlx model — doc 227-236) and the ONLY realization that works cleanly on wasm/embedded for this feature (no link-time slices needed for the batch itself). The codegen NAMES every planned candidate, force-linking them and sidestepping all three DCE layers for the PLANNED batch — and the plan `--check` turns a silently-lost contributor into a loud build-time DIFF, the best possible form of the mandated self-check (doc 152/235). BUT the central T1 limitation is severe and structural: a build.rs/proc-macro sees ONLY its own crate (doc 121), so the binary's codegen cannot introspect foreign crates' #[auto_configuration] annotations — each contributor crate must emit a build-time MANIFEST entry (or const descriptor) the binary's pass aggregates via cargo metadata, a convention with no compiler enforcement (a contributor that forgets it is silently absent → the plan diff is the only guard). The 'starter = enable a capability feature' mapping still holds (the feature gates whether the contributor's manifest entry is emitted/compiled), and resolver=3 still governs sibling leakage (doc 209). Class-names-as-public-API (doc 1244) is realized as the plan's stable module_path-derived identity that downstream exclude_name/before_name reference — and a mismatch can FAIL THE BUILD rather than silently resolve-to-nothing (a diagnostic improvement over R1/R2). The honest split: candidates + typed/name refs + build-decidable conditions known at build FREEZE cleanly; the leaf.autoconfigure.exclude Environment property, the kill-switch, every OnMissingBean backoff, AND any dynamic WASM-module candidate are RUNTIME residuals — an intra-build vs runtime asymmetry the user model must surface. Generics hard-error with a concrete shim. Two-source duality: the cargo-graph manifest is the default 'classpath' (frozen); the dynamic WASM-module 'classpath' has no build presence → its auto-configs must be assembled/ordered/gated at runtime — direct tension with the frozen-plan shape, flagged, CANDIDATE not a decision. leaf-codegen owns the compiler; leaf-core hosts the plan/descriptor ABI; leaf-boot consumes the plan (charter §6).

**T2 — execution context:** Inverts the phase split toward BUILD time. The union/dedup + exclusion merge + typo-guard + build-decidable prune + three-pass sort + plan emission run as a SYNCHRONOUS BUILD-TIME pass (build.rs / CLI) — single-threaded, NOT in the application's async runtime; it may do build-time IO (read manifests, cargo metadata) but produces only DATA (the generated plan). At STARTUP the runtime does almost nothing auto-config-related: read the kill-switch + subtract the late leaf.autoconfigure.exclude Environment-property exclusions (an in-memory, order-preserving filter — no sort, no IO, no await), then iterate the frozen ordered plan evaluating ONLY the residual OnMissingBean/OnProperty backoff against the user defs and registering seeds incrementally — cold-path, synchronous, trivially fast. The ONLY runtime assembly/sort reappears if a dynamic WASM-module auto-config with no build presence must be merged, and that, if it exists, runs in the same cold planning window, synchronous, non-blocking. ERRORS split by TIMING: build-decidable failures (cycle, duplicate, typed/name typo-guard, missing manifest entry) fail the BUILD — earliest, richest, with the full proposed batch inspectable and a --check for CI; only residual failures (an Environment-property exclusion naming a non-auto-config, an unexpected runtime backoff) surface at the cold startup phase as a diagnostic, still before async construction; a graceful runtime backoff is a recorded report entry, NOT an error (doc 1166). Cancellation is irrelevant to the build pass (offline) and the residual is too short to matter. Async/execution-context discipline (§2.3) barely touches this feature in R3 — all assembly/ordering logic is build-time data production; the downstream lite-config Factories run async/boxed-future at the dyn edge in the unchanged instantiation phase (doc 162/171), and the definition-order-vs-creation-order boundary (doc 1234) is preserved. The residual risk is the build-frozen/runtime-residual SEAM legibility: an author setting a property exclusion or wondering why a default backed off must understand build-time gating (in the plan) vs runtime backoff (a residual on top) — which the generated artifact + report must make explicit.

### Rust clashes
- NO RUNTIME CLASSPATH to scan every library's opinionated-defaults file. Spring's `ImportCandidates.load` calls `classLoader.getResources(\"META-INF/spring/...AutoConfiguration.imports\")` to enumerate EVERY jar's candidate file at runtime (doc 1196) — the literal 'the classpath decides the opinionated defaults'. Rust has no classpath and no runtime resource enumeration across crates. So 'every library contributes its auto-configs' must be reframed as link-time/build-time CONTRIBUTION over the descriptor stream (R1 linkme manifest), capability-scoped compilation (R2), or a cargo-metadata-aggregated build-time manifest (R3) — and the 'enable a starter' gesture becomes 'enable a Cargo capability feature that force-links the integration crate', because a feature gates COMPILATION not LINKAGE (doc 201-208). None can faithfully reproduce a runtime classpath scan; discovery is SCOPED to what the binary opts in, made explicit rather than pretending at a global classpath (doc 362/231).
- The TWO-PHASE BUILD-TIME METADATA FAST PATH (doc 1220-1226) is the load-bearing performance + robustness mechanism, and it tugs directly at the undecided metadata/codegen boundary. Spring generates `spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties` at BUILD time via an annotation processor so OnClass/OnBean can pre-filter HUNDREDS of candidates via ASM WITHOUT loading classes — this is WHY OnClass can safely name an absent class and WHY startup stays fast. leaf has no ASM and no runtime class loading; the rust-native realization of this exact intent (cheap pre-filter without loading) is either compile-time cfg-pruning of absent-capability candidates (R2), a build-time frozen plan (R3), or a runtime cheap-Parse-prune over const descriptors (R1) — and choosing how much pre-filtering is build-time vs runtime IS the §3 metadata/codegen-boundary + compile-vs-runtime keystone. The intent (discard most candidates cheaply, safely, before expensive work) transfers; the timing does not, and pre-deciding it would bias Phase 2.
- DEFERRAL-FOR-@Conditional-CORRECTNESS depends on a definite 'all user config is registered' moment — clean in Rust but entangled with the conditional strategy. Spring's `DeferredImportSelector` (ORDER=LOWEST_PRECEDENCE-1, doc 1204) defers auto-config PRECISELY so OnMissingBean sees the FINAL user-bean set and backs off (doc 1166 — correctness, not performance). leaf can reproduce this as a definite runtime deferred phase after user-def registration (R1/R2) or a build-order + runtime-residual split (R3). But WHEN OnMissingBean is evaluated relative to definition assembly is partly the §3 conditional-strategy question (cfg vs codegen vs runtime gate); if conditions are partly compile-time, preserving the 'back off after seeing ALL user beans' guarantee for cross-crate auto-config needs care. The deferral INTENT transfers cleanly; the exact mechanism is entangled with an undecided keystone.
- 'OPINIONATED DEFAULTS THAT NEVER FIGHT THE USER' via OnMissingBean backoff INVERTS Rust's eager-Result/fail-fast bias. Spring's whole philosophy (doc 1166-1170) is that a missing/overridden default is SILENT (graceful no-bean), never an error — the user's bean transparently wins with zero opt-out flags. Rust idiom tempts treating 'condition not met' as a Result::Err. leaf MUST keep TWO outcomes distinct and time-separated: condition-not-met = a silent no-bean now (recorded in the report, NOT an error) vs wiring-broken = a loud failure LATER when something actually needs the dropped bean. Collapsing them into one eager error would destroy the opinionated-but-overridable model — the single most important behavioural invariant of this feature.
- 'CLASS NAMES AS PUBLIC API' for exclusions/ordering has no classloader-resolved analogue (doc 1244, inherited from auto-config-ordering). Spring lets `spring.autoconfigure.exclude=com.x.FooAutoConfiguration` and `excludeName=` name an auto-config by FQCN STRING resolved at runtime — a crate excluding/ordering relative to a config it has no compile dependency on. Rust cannot resolve a string to a type at runtime. So identity splits into TYPED refs (TypeId, compile-checked + DCE-safe, require a compile dependency) and STRING refs (a canonical module_path-derived stable_name resolved at runtime against the candidate name index, the only way to express the no-dependency case) — making the stable name a refactor-fragile, version-stable, semver-relevant public surface authors must consciously maintain. This feature consumes that dual identity for its exclusion merge and inventory typo-guard.
- The kill-switch + the three-source EXCLUSION MERGE cross the compile/runtime boundary unevenly. Spring's kill-switch (`spring.boot.enableautoconfiguration=false`, doc 1218) and the third exclusion source (`spring.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property, doc 1238) are inherently RUNTIME (the Environment isn't populated until startup), while the typed `exclude=` is compile-known. So a build-time-freeze realization (R3) CANNOT freeze the whole pipeline — it must keep a runtime residual for the kill-switch + property exclusions + OnMissingBean backoff. An asymmetry Spring's uniform-runtime engine hides, coupling this feature to environment/binder/relaxed-binding and the compile-vs-runtime split.
- LITE-ONLY-BY-MANDATE (proxyBeanMethods=false, doc 1184-1188) is half-free, half-irrelevant in Rust. Spring hardwires lite mode on @AutoConfiguration because CGLIB-subclassing hundreds of configs is too expensive and auto-configs already parameter-inject and never self-call @Bean methods. Rust has no CGLIB proxying, so the COST motivation evaporates — but the DISCIPLINE (never self-call a @Bean method; wire via parameters) maps to a leaf macro LINT (a #[bean] method calling another #[bean] method on self is a footgun → loud compile diagnostic, the flip of Spring's silent 'lite mode buys you nothing'). The intent (fast, native-friendly, parameter-injected library configs) survives as the default; the mechanism (interception toggle) is simply absent.
- DEFINITION-ORDER vs CREATION-ORDER separation (doc 1234) must be an explicit, enforced boundary, not assumed. Spring is explicit that auto-config ordering affects only DEFINITION registration order (so OnMissingBean evaluates against deterministic predecessors), while instance creation is dependency/@DependsOn-driven. In leaf's async-first world the temptation is to conflate 'ordered batch' with 'instantiation schedule'. The engine MUST output definition order/contents ONLY and never touch the async instantiation scheduler (which stays dependency-driven, possibly with background-bootstrap concurrency) — else auto-config ordering would silently serialize/reorder construction, violating doc 1234 and the async-first invariant (§2.3).
- DEPENDENCY-BASED AUTO-CONFIG is a §3 deferred keystone this feature can't avoid touching. Spring's candidate set is the FULL .imports union regardless of which starter you added (then filtered by OnClass); but the cross-crate doc frames 'enabling a feature = adding a starter' (doc 177/196-208), which naturally scopes the candidate set to enabled capabilities (R2). Whether leaf's candidate set is a GLOBAL contributed manifest (R1, Spring-faithful) or a FUNCTION of linked capabilities (R2, dependency-based) is precisely the §3 'does dependency-based auto-config exist?' question — this feature is where it bites hardest, and the realizations probe it as candidates without deciding.
- SILENT-DCE makes a MISSING opinionated-default the worst failure mode for THIS feature specifically. A dropped registration yields an empty iterable, never a compile/link error (doc 152), and can pass in debug but fail in release or vary by linker (doc 143-147). For auto-config the symptom is an opinionated default that silently never wired — indistinguishable to the user from 'it backed off' UNLESS the engine has the mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per source crate; warn when an enabled capability/starter contributed ZERO). This is a hard dependency of all three realizations on the cross-crate composition decision, not an optional nicety.
- GENERICS CANNOT carry a 'static auto-config descriptor. A generic #[auto_configuration] has no monomorphized 'static value/symbol for the descriptor table, no stable TypeId until instantiated, and no canonical identity for string refs — so the macro must HARD-ERROR with a register_auto_config!(Concrete) per-instantiation shim (doc 153/349), the same constraint every contributor kind hits, here applied to the opinionated-default candidate and its exclude/before/after reference graph.
- ASYNC at the dyn edge for lite-config Factories (nightly doc 162-171). Auto-config beans are constructed by the same async Factory seam as configuration-classes' #[bean] methods; RPITIT/AFIT traits are NOT dyn-compatible, so a lite-config's async constructor is routed through a boxed-future shim at the dyn boundary regardless of nightly. This feature inherits that seam unchanged — it does NOT introduce its own async surface (the engine itself is synchronous cold-path planning); the only async is downstream construction, so the clash is contained to the shared Factory edge.

### Interactions
- **import-composition** — THE foundational supplier — auto-configuration IS the headline consumer of import-composition's DeferredImportSelector + Group machinery (doc 1204-1216). import-composition supplies the WHEN (the deferred batch phase that runs after ALL user config so OnMissingBean backs off correctly) and the global merge/dedup semantics; auto-configuration is the concrete engine that rides that deferral. In Spring, `AutoConfigurationImportSelector` is literally a DeferredImportSelector whose AutoConfigurationGroup is the Group. leaf's R1 deferred phase, R2 capability-scoped deferred phase, and R3 build-frozen-plus-residual all sit ON import-composition's deferred-phase seam; the 'opinionated but overridable' soul depends entirely on its deferral-for-conditional-correctness intent.
- **auto-config-ordering** — Direct, delegated supplier — auto-configuration DELEGATES its batch ordering + exclusion merge + typo-guard to auto-config-ordering (the upstream design's order_batch/check_excluded). auto-config-ordering owns the three-pass sort (alphabetical → @AutoConfigureOrder → topological before/after with cycle detection, doc 1230-1234) and the three-source exclusion merge (typed + name + Environment property, doc 1236-1238); auto-configuration owns invoking it on the assembled candidate set and consuming the ordered result to drive incremental definition registration. The doc-1234 definition-order-not-creation-order boundary is honored by BOTH: the sort fixes definition order so this engine's incremental OnMissingBean evaluation sees deterministic predecessors.
- **condition-family** — Direct, delegated supplier — auto-configuration's per-candidate gating DELEGATES to condition-family's OnMissingBean/OnBean/OnSingleCandidate (the runtime backoff that makes defaults overridable), OnClass/OnCapability (the absent-dependency-safe presence gate), OnProperty/OnBooleanProperty, OnProfile, etc. Spring scopes OnBean/OnMissingBean to auto-config ONLY because that's the one place 'defined so far' is stable (doc 1170) — this engine is exactly that place: the deferred, ordered, incremental batch where the register-phase bean conditions are well-defined. R2's two-tier split (capability=compile-time, OnMissingBean=runtime) is condition-family's tier-map applied; R3 splits build-decidable vs runtime-residual condition-family members.
- **conditions** — Foundational SPI two levels down (condition-family sits on conditions, this engine consumes both). The two-phase parse-vs-register model (doc 1126-1135) is what makes this engine correct: OnClass-family is PARSE (prunes cheaply, possibly compile-time), OnBean-family is REGISTER (order-sensitive, evaluated against the complete user-def set this deferred phase guarantees). The deferral-for-correctness intent is the runtime realization of the REGISTER_BEAN phase. ConditionContext's read-mostly 'observe and vote, never mutate' discipline (doc 1116-1124) is exactly the execution-context discipline this engine's planning phase honors (synchronous, non-blocking, no IO).
- **condition-report** — Primary diagnostic SINK — this engine's accountability requirement (doc 1160-1170: auto-config is 'magic' that must remain accountable). Every assembled candidate's match/no-match/exclusion/gated-out decision feeds condition-report with a human-readable reason ('OnMissingBean(RedisClient): found user-defined bean → backed off'; 'excluded via leaf.autoconfigure.exclude'; R2/R3: 'compile-time gated out: capability redis absent'). The report is what converts an opaque 'why is my bean missing?' into a lookup, preserving trust in heavy convention-over-configuration. R3's frozen plan is itself a superset of the report's ordering/exclusion view.
- **configuration-classes** — The UNIT being assembled — each auto-config is a LITE-ONLY config (Spring hardwires @Configuration(proxyBeanMethods=false), doc 1184-1188) whose #[bean]-method seeds are the bean definitions this engine registers in batch order. configuration-classes provides the lite-config marker + the typed async Factory seeds + the 'is-this-an-auto-config' marker the typo-guard needs; auto-configuration arranges/orders/defers/condition-gates those config units. The lite-only mandate maps to a leaf macro lint forbidding @Bean-method self-calls (the parameter-injection discipline); the async Factory dyn-edge boxing is shared, not reinvented.
- **environment** — Supplies three runtime inputs: the kill-switch (leaf.enable-autoconfiguration=false short-circuiting the whole batch, doc 1218), the third exclusion source (leaf.autoconfigure.exclude property, doc 1238), and the property/profile values that OnProperty/OnProfile candidate conditions read. The Environment is sealed BEFORE this deferred phase runs (a refresh-lifecycle ordering constraint) so these are synchronous in-memory reads (no IO/await). This is the source that is inherently RUNTIME — the part R3's build-time freeze cannot capture, forcing its runtime residual.
- **binder / relaxed-binding** — The leaf.autoconfigure.exclude exclusion property is BOUND via the binder as a LIST (Spring binds it via Binder with relaxed binding + list support, doc 1238). So this engine consumes binder to turn the raw property into a typed exclusion list, inheriting relaxed-binding so an ops user can set the exclusion via an UPPER_SNAKE env var or kebab-case key mapping to the same canonical list — decoupling the property KEY's transport syntax from the canonical auto-config NAME identity (a separate refactor-fragile surface).
- **refresh-lifecycle** — This engine occupies a precise, fixed slot in the refresh template's cold planning window: it runs AFTER all eager user-config contribution + user-definition registration (so deferral-for-backoff correctness holds, doc 1204) and BEFORE eager singleton instantiation. Its position IS what gives the back-off-after-user-config guarantee. In R3 most work moves to BUILD time, leaving only the runtime residual (kill-switch + property exclusions + OnMissingBean backoff) in the lifecycle template; in R1/R2 the full deferred assembly+order+gate phase runs in this window.
- **component-scanning** — Provides the whole-binary descriptor INVENTORY the exclusion typo-guard consults to answer 'is this excluded name an auto-config, a regular component, or absent?' (Spring's AutoConfigurationExcludeFilter ensures auto-configs enter ONLY via the import path, never double-registered by scanning, doc 1180 — so a scanned crate that happens to contain an auto-config doesn't register it twice). leaf needs the analogous guarantee: an #[auto_configuration]-marked config enters via the engine's batch, NOT via component-scanning, exactly once; the marker distinguishes the channels. The typo-guard quality rides component-scanning's inventory completeness (a missing crate makes a real exclusion look like a typo).
- **programmatic-registration** — The escape hatch beneath auto-config: where an opinionated default needs imperative/looping/conditional bean minting below the #[bean] level, an auto-config can carry a Registrar (= Spring 7 BeanRegistrar, import-composition's altitude-4). auto-configuration assembles/orders/gates the auto-config; the Registrar mints definitions in the same deferred definition-editing window. The 'registrar can't register a definition-phase post-processor' rule (it runs too late) is enforced as a loud diagnostic, inherited from import-composition.
- **profiles** — @Profile is just a @Conditional, so a profile-gated auto-config rides the same condition path: it is still ORDERED in the batch (so later candidates' OnMissingBean predecessor set stays deterministic) but its definitions back off when the profile is inactive. Ordering is profile-independent (the sort runs over all candidates); activation is the condition layer. This lets a library ship environment-specific opinionated defaults (a prod-only auto-config) that activate structurally.
- **bean-definition / bean-registry** — The OUTPUT is consumed at the DEFINITION level — the ordered batch fixes the sequence in which each auto-config's RawBeanDefinition seeds enter the registry, so OnMissingBean (reading the bean-registry's read-mostly definition view) sees a deterministic predecessor set. The engine registers DEFINITIONS, never instances (doc 1234); a backed-off candidate is simply never added (graceful no-bean), aligning with bean-definition's parse-then-instantiate split. OnMissingBean reads definitions, not live beans — it must not trigger construction.
- **primary-fallback** — Complementary override mechanism — where OnMissingBean is the BINARY 'user defined one → I back off entirely' lever, @Fallback (demote a library default) and @Primary (promote a user bean) let an auto-config ship a default that LOSES to a user bean without the auto-config having to drop it (the default stays a registered candidate, just not the winner). Spring's auto-config increasingly uses @Fallback alongside OnMissingBean; leaf's engine should register an auto-config's beans with a fallback role so the user's bean transparently supersedes across the crate boundary even when both are present — a softer override than OnMissingBean's all-or-nothing backoff.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- DEPENDENCY-BASED AUTO-CONFIG (§3 keystone, decided AT THIS FEATURE): is leaf's candidate set a GLOBAL contributed manifest scanned/collected regardless of which starters are present (R1, Spring-faithful — every library's .imports unioned, then filtered by OnClass), or a FUNCTION of which capability features/integration crates are linked (R2, dependency-based — the candidate exists only if its capability is compiled+force-linked)? This is precisely the §3 'does dependency-based auto-config exist and what are its ripple effects?' question, and auto-configuration is where it bites hardest. Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model and the conditional strategy. UNRESOLVED.
- HOW MUCH of the assembly+ordering+filtering pipeline is BUILD-TIME-frozen vs RUNTIME? R3 freezes union+dedup+exclusion-merge+build-decidable-prune+sort into an inspectable plan (earliest diagnostics, lowest startup cost, wasm-friendly, faithful to Boot's spring-autoconfigure-metadata fast-path); R1/R2 resolve at a runtime deferred phase. This pre-touches the §3 metadata/codegen-boundary AND compile-vs-runtime keystones AND the diagnostic-timing call (§2.9). Even a build-time answer keeps a runtime residual (kill-switch + property exclusions + OnMissingBean backoff are inherently runtime), so the build-frozen/runtime-residual SEAM legibility is itself unresolved. Held as a candidate axis, NOT pre-decided.
- HOW is the deferral-for-@Conditional-correctness moment realized, and does it survive a partly-compile-time conditional strategy? The 'back off after ALL user config is registered' guarantee (doc 1166) needs a definite 'user config complete' point. R1/R2 make it a runtime deferred phase; R3 splits build-decidable vs runtime-residual conditions. Entangled with the §3 conditional strategy (cfg vs codegen vs runtime gate): if conditions are partly compile-time, preserving the cross-crate back-off guarantee for OnMissingBean is non-trivial. UNRESOLVED.
- WHAT is the rust-native realization of the TWO-PHASE BUILD-TIME METADATA FAST PATH (doc 1220-1226 — Boot pre-filters hundreds of candidates via ASM metadata without loading classes)? Is the cheap pre-filter compile-time cfg-pruning of absent capabilities (R2), a build-time frozen plan (R3), a runtime cheap-Parse-prune over const descriptors (R1), or a blend? This IS the metadata/codegen-boundary keystone viewed from the performance angle, and it determines whether OnClass-against-absent-dependency is a compile fact or a runtime fact (and how OnMissingClass asserts ABSENCE of a capability that Cargo features can only turn ON). UNRESOLVED.
- WHAT is the 'starter' analogue and how does it reconcile with Cargo feature semantics? Spring starters are 'add the jar, get opinionated defaults that back off'. The cross-crate doc frames a capability feature as the analogue (doc 177/196-208), but a feature gates COMPILATION not LINKAGE (doc 201-208), features only OR-on and can't be un-set, and a sibling can flip one on via unification (doc 184-194). So 'enable the starter' requires BOTH a compiled descriptor AND a force-link, additive-capability discipline (backend-choice stays runtime/profile), resolver=3, and a self-check warning when an enabled starter contributed zero candidates.
