The exact starter mechanism + its DX is unresolved and cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model. UNRESOLVED.
- HOW does the mandated ANTI-DCE self-check integrate with this feature's exclusion typo-guard so 'missing opinionated default' (a crate the binary never force-linked → silently absent) and 'genuine backoff' (OnMissingBean matched a user bean) and 'typo'd exclusion' are DISTINGUISHABLE as distinct rich diagnostics rather than one indistinguishable bare-graph symptom? R1/R2 = runtime expected-vs-found count; R3 = build-time plan diff. Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model and the unified-diagnostics model (§2.9). UNRESOLVED.
- HOW are condition-not-met (silent no-bean now, recorded in the report, NOT an error) and wiring-broken (loud failure LATER when something needs the dropped bean) kept DISTINCT and time-separated across a possibly-cross-tier engine (some candidates compile-gated, some runtime-backed-off), while still yielding ONE coherent accountable account (the ConditionEvaluationReport intent, doc 1160-1170)? This is the behavioural soul of 'opinionated defaults that never fight the user' and it cross-cuts the unified error/diagnostics model (§3) and condition-report. UNRESOLVED.
- The TWO-SOURCE candidate duality: the static link-time/codegen set (default 'classpath' of opinionated defaults) PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source whose auto-configs have NO build-time presence and no capability cfg. R1/R2 absorb a dynamic candidate naturally (it rides the runtime engine, gated only by runtime conditions); R3's frozen plan is in direct tension (dynamic candidates must be runtime-assembled). HOW does a WASM-contributed auto-config compose, order, and back off INDISTINGUISHABLY from a native one (origin-agnostic), given it has no Rust type for typed exclude/before/after refs and no capability to read? CANDIDATE, not a decision; origin-agnostic provider seam mandated.
- HOW is the curated TEST-SLICE mode (@ImportAutoConfiguration, doc 1240-1242 — same ordering/backoff rules over an EXPLICIT subset, with optional-if-absent entries) realized so test slices (the leaf analogue of @WebMvcTest/@DataJpaTest) get a deterministic, minimal opinionated-default subset without the whole app's auto-config? Does it reuse the SAME engine over an explicit candidate list (R1's slice!()) and how do optional-if-absent entries interact with the force-link/DCE story (an optional entry whose crate isn't linked is simply skipped)? Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model and testing ergonomics. UNRESOLVED.
- WHERE does the engine's read-mostly world view come from and what is its ownership/lifetime shape (a borrowed snapshot of the sealed Environment + the GROWING definition registry vs an Arc handle), given the engine must register definitions INCREMENTALLY so each candidate's OnMissingBean sees the predecessors registered so far (doc 1234)? This incremental mutate-then-read pattern is an instance of the deferred scope/lifetime/ownership keystone (§3) applied to the engine's evaluation inputs, and it must avoid a global lock (§2.5) while threading a mutating registry through a synchronous planning loop. UNRESOLVED.

### Notes
Confidence: HIGH on intent. The three realizations are genuinely divergent on the axis that matters MOST for THIS feature given the upstream suppliers are already designed — HOW the opinionated-default candidate set is assembled and WHEN the pipeline runs: R1 = runtime deferred-batch engine over a per-crate contributed manifest (most Spring-faithful: global union, deferral-for-correctness, incremental in-batch registration so OnMissingBean sees the growing set, slice!() test mode) but pays full runtime assembly cost + rides every DCE hazard; R2 = capability-keyed dependency-based engine where 'starter present' is a compile-time cfg/capability fact that SCOPES the candidate set, with OnMissingBean as the runtime backoff (most intuitive Rust DX 'add a dependency = add a starter', cleanest read-without-loading, lowest runtime cost, but PRE-LEANS on the dependency-based-auto-config keystone §3); R3 = build-time frozen plan via leaf-codegen + cargo-metadata aggregation (earliest diagnostics, near-zero startup, wasm-friendly, faithful to Boot's own build-time-metadata fast-path) but pre-touches the metadata/codegen + compile-vs-runtime keystones and hits the build.rs single-crate wall, requiring a manifest convention + runtime residual. R1 vs R2 differ on global-manifest-vs-capability-scoped candidate set (the dependency-based-auto-config question); R3 differs on runtime-vs-build-time pipeline resolution.

Things I deliberately did NOT decide (held as Phase-2 questions): whether dependency-based auto-config exists (global manifest vs capability-scoped); how much pipeline is build-time vs runtime; how the deferral-for-correctness moment survives a partly-compile-time conditional strategy; the rust-native fast-path pre-filter; the 'starter' mechanism + Cargo-feature reconciliation; how the anti-DCE self-check distinguishes missing-default vs genuine-backoff vs typo'd-exclusion; how condition-not-met-vs-wiring-broken stays distinct/time-separated and accountable across tiers; the two-source (link/codegen + WASM-module) candidate duality vs a frozen plan; the curated test-slice mode realization; and the incremental mutate-then-read registry ownership/lifetime shape. Every realization keeps the descriptor/Factory seam ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a native, test-double, or WASM-module-contributed auto-config assembles/orders/backs-off indistinguishably) and substrate-neutral (the engine consumes whatever candidate table linkme/codegen/explicit produces). I built CONCRETELY on the three provided upstream designs: import-composition (this engine IS the headline consumer of its deferred Group phase — the WHEN), auto-config-ordering (this engine DELEGATES the three-pass sort + three-source exclusion merge + typo-guard — the HOW-ordered), and condition-family (this engine DELEGATES OnMissingBean/OnClass/OnProperty gating — the HOW-gated), plus configuration-classes (auto-configs are lite-only configs whose #[bean] seeds it registers). I did NOT redesign any of those — auto-configuration is the thin orchestrator above them.

## Auto-Configuration Ordering & Exclusions  `[auto-config-ordering]`

This feature is the deterministic-ordering + exclusion-merging engine that turns the unordered, multi-crate auto-config CANDIDATE SET (assembled by `auto-configuration` via `import-composition`'s deferred-group machinery) into a single, totally-ordered, exclusion-filtered batch — Spring's `AutoConfigurationSorter.getInPriorityOrder` + `getExclusions`/`checkExcludedClasses`. It is NOT about instantiation order; the load-bearing hidden concept (doc 1234) is that ordering affects DEFINITION order only — `before`/`after` guarantee that bean *definitions* are added in that order so `@ConditionalOnMissingBean`/`@ConditionalOnBean` evaluate against a correct, deterministic predecessor set; actual instance creation order is still dependency-driven (`@DependsOn`-style). So the deliverable is a deterministic function over auto-config DESCRIPTORS, run during the cold planning phase, that condition evaluation and definition registration consume.\n\nThe MARQUEE MECHANIC is a precise three-pass sort (doc 1230-1234): (1) sort ALPHABETICALLY by class name — a stable, deterministic, total base order that makes the whole result reproducible regardless of discovery/link order (critical given the cross-crate doc's 'ordering is unspecified for linkme/inventory — never rely on registration order'); (2) STABLE-sort by an `@AutoConfigureOrder` integer priority (DEFAULT_ORDER = 0, same semantics as `@Order` but a dedicated annotation so auto-config priority is decoupled from collection-injection `@Order`); (3) a TOPOLOGICAL sort honoring `@AutoConfigureBefore`/`@AutoConfigureAfter` edges (and the inline `before`/`beforeName`/`after`/`afterName` attributes on `@AutoConfiguration`, doc 1190) WITH EXPLICIT CYCLE DETECTION emitting 'AutoConfigure cycle detected between X and Y'. The topo-sort must preserve the alphabetical+order base whenever the constraints leave freedom (a stable topo-sort), so two batches with the same edges always produce the same sequence. Crucially, Spring reads order/before/after from BUILD-TIME metadata (`spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties`, doc 1226) when available, else from ASM annotation metadata — i.e. ordering data is read WITHOUT loading the class, a fast-path leaf can mirror as ordering-as-DATA on each descriptor.\n\nThe second deliverable is EXCLUSIONS (doc 1236-1238): `getExclusions` MERGES THREE SOURCES into one set — (a) the `exclude=` attribute (typed class references on `@SpringBootApplication`/`@EnableAutoConfiguration`), (b) the `excludeName=` attribute (string class names), and (c) the `spring.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property (bound via the Binder with relaxed binding + list support). The merged exclusion set is subtracted from the candidate set. A typo-guard `checkExcludedClasses` throws if you try to exclude a class that IS present but is NOT actually an auto-configuration class — a rich early diagnostic. There is also the `spring.boot.enableautoconfiguration` global kill-switch (doc 1218) that disables the whole batch at once.\n\nThe deepest INTENT to preserve is 'CLASS NAMES AS PUBLIC API': in Spring, an auto-config's fully-qualified class name is a stable identifier other crates depend on — they write `@AutoConfigureBefore(SomeOtherAutoConfig.class)` / `excludeName=\"com.x.FooAutoConfiguration\"` / `spring.autoconfigure.exclude=...` naming a config they may not even have a compile dependency on. So ordering edges and exclusions form a cross-crate REFERENCE-BY-IDENTITY graph that must work even when the referencer cannot `use` the referenced type. leaf must realize the SAME determinism, three-tier precedence, cycle diagnostics, three-source exclusion merge, and typo-guard — using ordering-as-data + a runtime/build-time topo-sort (never link order), and a stable cross-crate identity for each auto-config (TypeId for typed refs, plus a string/path identity for name-based refs and the Environment-property path) — WITHOUT a runtime classpath, ASM metadata reading, or reflective class-name resolution.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Runtime three-pass sorter over ordering-as-DATA descriptors; dual TypeId+stable-name identity; exclusions merged from typed refs + name refs + Environment
Make auto-config ordering a pure, deterministic RUNTIME function `order_batch(candidates: &[AutoConfigDescriptor], exclusions: &ExclusionSet) -> Result<Vec<&AutoConfigDescriptor>, OrderingError>` that runs in the cold planning phase, consuming the candidate set `auto-configuration` already assembled (via `import-composition`'s deferred group). Each candidate carries ORDERING-AS-DATA on its thin `const` descriptor — never relying on link/section/collection order (the cross-crate doc's hard rule):

```
struct AutoConfigDescriptor {
  id: AutoConfigId,            // dual identity (below)
  type_id: TypeId,             // typed identity
  stable_name: &'static str,   // string identity = the 'class name as public API'
  order: i32,                  // @AutoConfigureOrder, DEFAULT 0
  before: &'static [AutoConfigRef], // @AutoConfigureBefore / inline before
  after:  &'static [AutoConfigRef], // @AutoConfigureAfter  / inline after
  // ... (definition seeds, conditions live on the configuration-classes descriptor)
}
enum AutoConfigRef { ByType(TypeId), ByName(&'static str) }  // class-name-as-API
```

The macro lowers `#[auto_configuration(order = -100, before = [OtherCfg], after_name = "crate_x::FooAutoConfig")]` into this descriptor. The three passes run exactly as Spring: (1) sort by `stable_name` (alphabetical, total, deterministic base); (2) STABLE-sort by `order` (preserving pass-1 order on ties); (3) a STABLE topological sort over `before`/`after` edges that preserves the pass-1+2 order whenever constraints permit (Kahn's algorithm with a priority queue keyed by the pass-2 index → deterministic among ready nodes), with explicit cycle detection that reconstructs and names the cycle ('AutoConfigure cycle detected: A → B → A', listing each contributor crate). DUAL IDENTITY resolves the class-name-as-API clash: a `ByType` ref needs the referenced type in scope (compile dependency) and is DCE-safe (path-references it); a `ByName` ref is a `&'static str` resolved against the candidate set's `stable_name` index at sort time — letting crate C order before crate D's auto-config WITHOUT a compile dependency, exactly Spring's `beforeName`/`afterName`. An edge naming an absent name is tolerated (Spring ignores absent before/after targets) but RECORDED for the diagnostic report.

EXCLUSIONS merge three sources into one `ExclusionSet` keyed by both TypeId and stable_name: (a) typed `exclude = [FooAutoConfig]` from the app's `#[leaf::main]`/enable annotation; (b) `exclude_name = ["crate_x::FooAutoConfig"]`; (c) the `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property (bound via the binder with relaxed-binding + list support — interaction with `binder`/`relaxed-binding`/`environment`). The set is subtracted before the sort. The typo-guard `check_excluded`: if an exclusion (by type or name) matches a LINKED descriptor that is NOT an auto-config (it's a regular component/config), or matches NOTHING while a same-named regular type is present, emit a rich error ('excluded "X" is on the build but is not an auto-configuration'). The global kill-switch is the Environment property `leaf.enable-autoconfiguration=false` short-circuiting the whole batch. Output ordering drives DEFINITION registration order so conditions see deterministic predecessors — instantiation order stays dependency-driven (the doc-1234 separation is preserved as a hard boundary the sorter never crosses).

**Pros:** Faithful to all three Spring passes AND the class-names-as-public-API intent: `ByName` refs + `exclude_name` + the Environment-property path all let a crate order/exclude an auto-config it has no compile dependency on (Spring's `beforeName`/`afterName`/`spring.autoconfigure.exclude`), which a pure TypeId model cannot express.; Ordering-as-DATA + a runtime stable topo-sort obeys the cross-crate doc's hardest rule ('never rely on registration/link/constructor order') head-on — the alphabetical base pass makes the result reproducible even though linkme/inventory hand back candidates in unspecified, possibly randomized order. Determinism is a property of the data + algorithm, not the substrate.; Pure, side-effect-free function over `&[Descriptor]` — trivially UNIT-TESTABLE in isolation (feed candidate lists + exclusions, assert the order and the cycle/typo errors) without a container, a runtime, or the link step; the highest-confidence way to validate the marquee mechanic.; Substrate-agnostic: the descriptor table can come from linkme (Arch A/B), build-time codegen (Arch C), or explicit `with()` (Arch D) — the sorter is identical across all four, so this feature does not pre-commit the Phase-2 cross-crate decision.; Rich early diagnostics (§2.9): the cold sort fails BEFORE any async construction with a full causal chain — the cycle path naming contributor crates, the typo-guard naming the bad exclusion + what it actually matched, and a 'this name resolved to nothing' note — strictly the richest-context point for these failures.

**Cons:** The `ByName`/`exclude_name` string identity reintroduces a STRINGLY layer the rest of leaf works hard to avoid: a misspelled `after_name`/`exclude_name` cannot be caught at compile time (the referenced crate may not even be a dependency), only as a runtime 'resolved to nothing' note — a softer diagnostic than a type error, and a genuine DX regression vs typed refs.; Requires a stable, canonical STRING identity for every auto-config (the analogue of an FQCN) that is consistent across crate versions and refactors — `module_path!()::TypeName` is the obvious candidate but is refactor-fragile (renaming a type or moving a module silently breaks downstream `before_name`/`exclude` references), so 'class name as public API' becomes a semver-relevant surface authors must consciously maintain.; The sort runs at RUNTIME every startup; for hundreds of candidates the topo-sort is cheap (O(V+E)), but the alphabetical pass + string-keyed exclusion index pay a small per-startup cost that a build-time approach (R3) avoids — a low-overhead (#2) ding, dominated by DX but real on cold-start-sensitive targets.; Dual identity (TypeId AND stable_name) on every descriptor and every ref is conceptual overhead — two ways to name the same thing, with subtle rules (a `ByType` and a `ByName` ref to the same config must dedupe), and the exclusion set keyed by both must reconcile a type-exclude and a name-exclude of the same config.; The typo-guard needs to know which LINKED types are auto-configs vs regular configs/components to distinguish 'excluded a non-auto-config' from 'excluded an absent config' — coupling this feature to the whole-binary descriptor inventory and to `component-scanning`/`configuration-classes`' notion of 'is this an auto-config', which is more cross-feature reach than a pure sorter implies.

**Mechanisms considered:** thin `const` AutoConfigDescriptor carrying order/before/after as DATA (the cross-crate doc's prescribed shape), routable through linkme / build-codegen / explicit `with()` identically; dual identity `AutoConfigRef::{ByType(TypeId), ByName(&'static str)}` — typed refs DCE-safe + compile-checked, name refs realize class-name-as-API for no-dependency ordering (Spring beforeName/afterName); three-pass deterministic sort: alphabetical-by-stable-name base → stable-sort by i32 order → STABLE Kahn topological sort (ready-queue keyed by the pass-2 index) with cycle reconstruction; cycle detection via DFS back-edge / Kahn residual, reconstructing the actual cycle path and naming contributor crates in the diagnostic; three-source exclusion merge (typed `exclude`, string `exclude_name`, `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property via binder/relaxed-binding) into one TypeId+name-keyed ExclusionSet, subtracted pre-sort; `check_excluded` typo-guard distinguishing excluded-non-auto-config vs excluded-absent, against the whole-binary descriptor inventory; global kill-switch via `leaf.enable-autoconfiguration=false` Environment property short-circuiting the batch; ordering drives DEFINITION-registration order ONLY; instantiation stays dependency-driven (doc-1234 boundary never crossed)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization that directly confronts the class-names-as-public-API cross-crate requirement. Spring's classpath makes `@AutoConfigureBefore(X.class)` and `excludeName="x.Y"` uniform; leaf has neither a classpath nor runtime name→type resolution, so ordering/exclusion edges split into TWO kinds: (1) `ByType`/typed `exclude` — the referencer has a compile dependency on the referenced auto-config's crate, which usefully PATH-REFERENCES it (DCE-safe, Layer-0-safe, compile-checked); (2) `ByName`/`exclude_name`/the Environment property — pure string identity resolved at runtime against the candidate set's `stable_name` index, the only way to express Spring's no-compile-dependency ordering/exclusion. The sorter consumes whatever descriptor table the substrate produces (linkme slice / codegen / explicit), so it is substrate-neutral; but the candidate set's COMPLETENESS still rides the cross-crate doc's DCE hazards — an auto-config in a crate the binary never references is silently absent (Layer 0), so a `ByName` edge to it 'resolves to nothing' and an alphabetical base over a SHORTER list silently reorders. Hence this feature DEPENDS ON, and must surface, the mandated anti-DCE self-check: an expected-vs-found count per source crate, so a missing candidate is a loud diagnostic rather than a silently-different order. The exclusion typo-guard is a second cross-crate self-check: it can only classify 'excluded a non-auto-config' for types actually LINKED, so on a binary missing a crate it must say 'excluded "X" — no such auto-config found among N candidates from M crates' (and warn if a same-named regular type IS linked). Stable string identity must be canonical and version-stable across crates (a `module_path!`-derived FQ name), since downstream crates encode it in `before_name`/`exclude`. Generics can't carry a `'static` descriptor → the macro hard-errors with a `register_auto_config!(Concrete)` shim. The two-source duality applies: link-time/codegen candidates are the default 'classpath'; an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source would contribute additional candidates whose `stable_name` slots into the SAME alphabetical+topo sort and the SAME name-keyed exclusion index — origin-agnostic, a candidate not a decision.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely COLD-PATH, single-threaded planning logic — there is no hot path and nothing async here. The sorter runs once, synchronously, during the deferred batch / planning window of refresh-lifecycle, AFTER the candidate set + user definitions are assembled and (per import-composition) conditions are about to be / are being evaluated, and BEFORE any bean Factory runs. It is a pure CPU function: read descriptors, build the alphabetical base, stable-sort by order, run the topo-sort, subtract exclusions, read the Environment property (a synchronous in-memory read — the Environment is already populated this early; NO IO, NO blocking, NO await). It MUST NOT block, do IO, or be async — mirroring the read-mostly ConditionContext discipline; any work that wants to await belongs to a bean Factory, not the sorter. Cancellation is irrelevant (the function is short and synchronous; if startup is cancelled it simply isn't called). ERRORS propagate as a planning-phase `OrderingError`/`ExclusionError` Result — a cycle, a typo-guard violation, or (configurably) an unresolved name — surfaced at the earliest-richest point with the full causal chain, strictly before async construction. The OUTPUT is consumed by definition registration to fix DEFINITION order (so conditions see deterministic predecessors); it explicitly does NOT touch instantiation scheduling, which stays dependency/concurrency-driven in the async instantiation phase — preserving the doc-1234 definition-order-vs-creation-order boundary as an execution-context boundary too.

#### R2 — TYPED ordering lattice: ordering & exclusions are typed relations (no string FQCNs in the common path); name/property refs are an explicit, lint-flagged escape hatch
Lean into Rust's strengths: make the COMMON ordering/exclusion path fully TYPED and compile-checked, treating Spring's stringly `beforeName`/`afterName`/`excludeName`/`spring.autoconfigure.exclude` as a deliberately-narrowed escape hatch rather than a co-equal mechanism. The insight: most real ordering edges are between auto-configs that already share a dependency (a DB auto-config orders after a DataSource auto-config it must compile against), so a TYPED edge is both expressible and strictly better — and Rust can make the alphabetical 'base order' a TYPED, stable key too.

Ordering is expressed as typed marker traits / typed refs the macro lowers to TypeId edges:
```
#[auto_configuration(order = -100, before = [JpaAutoConfig], after = [DataSourceAutoConfig])]
struct HikariAutoConfig;
```
`before`/`after` take TYPE paths (compile-checked, refactor-safe, DCE-safe — the referenced type is path-referenced so its crate is forced onto the link graph). The deterministic base order is NOT a runtime string sort but a stable, total order over a CANONICAL TYPE KEY (a `const`-derived stable hash of `module_path!() + type name`, computed at compile time and stored on the descriptor as a `u64` + the source string for diagnostics only) — so the alphabetical-equivalent base is precomputed, and the runtime sort is just stable-sort-by-(key, order) then topo-sort over TypeId edges. The three Spring passes are preserved in spirit (deterministic base → priority → topological with cycle detection) but operate on typed keys + TypeId edges, eliminating runtime string comparison from the common path.

Exclusions are likewise TYPED first: `exclude = [FooAutoConfig]` (TypeId-keyed). The typo-guard becomes a near-COMPILE-TIME check: excluding a type that isn't an auto-config is detectable because the macro/codegen knows (from the descriptor's marker) whether a type is an auto-config — so `exclude = [SomeRegularService]` can be a loud build/plan error, the richest possible form of `checkExcludedClasses`.

The STRINGLY path survives ONLY as an explicit, documented escape hatch for the genuine no-compile-dependency case (excluding/ordering relative to a crate you can't depend on): `exclude_name = ["crate_x::FooAutoConfig"]` and the `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property are honored, but a macro/clippy-style LINT flags every string ref ('prefer a typed `exclude`/`before`; string refs are unchecked and refactor-fragile'), and they resolve at runtime against the same canonical-key index with a 'resolved to nothing' diagnostic. So leaf's surface NUDGES toward typed refs (compile-checked, the default DX) while still covering Spring's full expressive range through a clearly-marked, second-class string channel.

**Pros:** Best DX/diagnostics on the COMMON path (§2.1, §2.9): typed `before`/`after`/`exclude` are autocompleted, refactor-safe, and compile-checked; an ordering ref to a renamed/removed auto-config is a COMPILE error, and excluding a non-auto-config is a build/plan error — a strict improvement over Spring's runtime-only `checkExcludedClasses` and stringly `beforeName`.; Typed refs PATH-REFERENCE the target, so the ordering/exclusion graph is largely Layer-0 DCE-safe by construction (the cross-crate doc's core hazard) — naming `before = [DataSourceAutoConfig]` forces that crate onto the link graph, shrinking the surface the anti-DCE self-check must cover to entry-point + name-referenced configs only.; Precomputing the deterministic base key at COMPILE time (a const stable hash) removes runtime string sorting from the hot common path — lowest per-startup overhead (#2) among the runtime approaches, while still deterministic and reproducible.; Honestly scopes the stringly mechanism as a second-class, lint-flagged escape hatch — preserves full Spring expressive range (no-dependency ordering/exclusion, the Environment property) for the cases that genuinely need it, without letting the fragile path become the default, aligning with 'thin macros + escape hatch at every level' (§2.10).; Keeps the typo-guard mostly at build/plan time where the descriptor markers are known — the richest, earliest diagnostic for the most common authoring mistake (excluding the wrong thing).

**Cons:** Diverges hardest from Spring's mental model: a Spring user reaches for `@AutoConfigureBefore("some.Name")` / `excludeName` as co-equal, but leaf demotes string refs to a lint-flagged escape hatch — a parity-surface judgment call that may surprise porters who treat the string form as primary (it is common in real Spring auto-config and in `spring.autoconfigure.exclude` ops usage).; The 'typed edge needs a compile dependency' assumption is not always true in Spring's intent: Spring deliberately lets a downstream crate order BEFORE an upstream auto-config it must NOT depend on (to avoid a cycle or a heavy dep) — forcing those cases through the lint-flagged string channel may push a non-trivial fraction of real edges onto the second-class path, undercutting the 'typed is the default' premise.; The canonical compile-time key (stable hash of module_path + type name) still encodes a refactor-fragile string identity UNDER the hood for the diagnostic + string-ref-resolution path — so 'class name as public API' fragility isn't eliminated, just hidden from the typed common path; a rename still breaks downstream `exclude_name`/Environment-property references silently.; Two parallel mechanisms (typed lattice + stringly escape hatch) that must produce IDENTICAL ordering/exclusion semantics — a typed `before` and a string `before_name` to the same target must behave the same, and a typed-vs-string exclusion of the same config must dedupe — more to specify and test than R1's uniform dual-ref or R3's frozen plan.; The near-compile-time typo-guard depends on the macro/codegen knowing the auto-config marker of the EXCLUDED type, which only holds when that type is in scope at the exclusion site (a compile dependency); for `exclude_name`/property exclusions the guard degrades back to runtime — so the 'richest possible checkExcludedClasses' claim only holds for typed excludes, splitting the diagnostic quality by channel.

**Mechanisms considered:** typed `before`/`after`/`exclude` taking TYPE paths → TypeId edges (compile-checked, refactor-safe, DCE-safe, path-references the target); deterministic base order as a COMPILE-TIME const stable hash of module_path!()+type name (u64 key on the descriptor) — removes runtime string sort from the common path; source string kept for diagnostics only; three passes over typed keys: stable-sort by (base-key, order) then STABLE topo-sort over TypeId edges with cycle detection; near-compile-time typo-guard: excluding a type whose descriptor marker says it is NOT an auto-config is a build/plan error (richest checkExcludedClasses); stringly path (`before_name`/`after_name`/`exclude_name` + `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property) preserved as a LINT-FLAGGED escape hatch resolved at runtime against the canonical-key index; macro/clippy-style lint nudging string refs → typed refs ('unchecked, refactor-fragile'); typed and string refs to the same target must dedupe to identical ordering/exclusion semantics; ordering affects DEFINITION order only (doc-1234 boundary preserved)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Optimizes for the cross-crate case where a compile dependency EXISTS (the common one): typed `before`/`after`/`exclude` path-reference the target auto-config's crate, which is simultaneously the Layer-0 force-link guarantee AND a compile-time existence check — so the typed ordering graph is DCE-safe and verified by the compiler, the strongest cross-crate posture of the three realizations. The deterministic base key being a COMPILE-TIME const hash means the base order is fixed per-type at build time and is identical no matter which substrate (linkme/codegen/explicit) hands back the candidates, and no matter their unspecified collection order — squarely satisfying 'never rely on registration order' while moving the cost off the runtime. The honest cross-crate LIMIT is the no-compile-dependency case Spring supports first-class: a crate ordering/excluding relative to an auto-config it must not depend on can only use the lint-flagged string channel, which resolves at runtime against the canonical-key index and rides the same DCE-completeness hazard as R1's `ByName` (a string ref to a non-linked candidate 'resolves to nothing'); so the anti-DCE self-check is still mandatory for the string channel, just unnecessary for the typed channel. The build/plan-time typo-guard is a cross-crate WIN for typed excludes (the macro/codegen knows the marker) but degrades to runtime for string/property excludes. Canonical key stability across crate versions/refactors is the residual semver surface (a rename changes the hash → silently breaks downstream string refs and the Environment-property path). Generics hard-error with a concrete shim. Two-source WASM-module duality: a dynamically-contributed auto-config has no compile-time type for downstream typed refs, so cross-module ordering can ONLY use the string channel — a flagged tension (the typed-first model is weakest exactly at the dynamic-source boundary), candidate not a decision.

**T2 — execution context:** Same cold-path, single-threaded, synchronous planning execution as R1 — no hot path, nothing async — but with LESS runtime work: the deterministic base is a precomputed const key, so the planning-phase sort is stable-sort-by-(key,order) + a TypeId-keyed topo-sort + exclusion subtraction, all in-memory, no string comparison on the common path. It reads the `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property synchronously (in-memory, populated this early) only for the string channel. MUST NOT block/IO/await; runs in the refresh-lifecycle planning window before any Factory, after candidate assembly. The KEY execution-context difference is TIMING OF DIAGNOSTICS: typed-channel failures (ordering ref to a removed/renamed type, excluding a non-auto-config) surface at COMPILE/build time — earlier than any runtime phase — while string-channel failures (unresolved `exclude_name`, bad property) surface at the cold planning phase as a Result error/diagnostic, still before async construction. Cancellation irrelevant (short synchronous function). Output fixes DEFINITION order only; instantiation stays dependency-driven in the async phase. The execution-context risk is purely that the SPLIT diagnostic timing (compile-time for typed, runtime for string) must be legible so an author isn't surprised that one channel catches a typo at build and the other only at startup.

#### R3 — BUILD-TIME frozen ordering plan: leaf-codegen runs the three-pass sort + exclusion merge at build time and emits an inspectable, ordered, `--check`-able manifest; runtime just reads it
Question whether ANY ordering or exclusion resolution needs to happen at runtime. The sort is a pure function of build-known data (candidate identities, order ints, before/after edges) plus a small amount of late-bound input (the Environment-property exclusions, the kill-switch). So move the heavy, deterministic part to BUILD time — the sqlx model the cross-crate doc endorses (Arch C), and the native analogue of Spring's build-time `spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties` fast-path (doc 1226) that already lets the sorter read order/before/after WITHOUT loading classes.

A leaf-codegen pass (build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare`) in the binary crate reads a per-crate MANIFEST of auto-config descriptors (each crate emits its order/before/after/identity as a build-time const descriptor or a manifest entry, aggregated via cargo metadata), then AT BUILD TIME: (a) runs the exact three passes — alphabetical base → order → stable topological sort with cycle detection; (b) merges the build-known exclusion sources (the app's typed `exclude` + `exclude_name`); (c) runs `check_excluded` against the build-known descriptor inventory (typo-guard at build time — the earliest possible); (d) emits a FROZEN, ordered `auto_config_order.rs` (`include!`d into the binary): a flat `&[AutoConfigId]` in final batch order, plus the resolved exclusion set, plus a record of any name refs that didn't resolve. The runtime then does NEAR-ZERO ordering work: it reads the frozen order, applies the LATE-BOUND residual — subtract the `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment-property exclusions (which can't be known at build time) and honor the kill-switch — and proceeds. Subtracting a late exclusion from an already-ordered list is order-preserving and trivial, so no runtime topo-sort is needed.

The generated manifest is the killer feature: it is a human-readable, checked-in, `--check`-able artifact (sqlx-style) showing the ENTIRE auto-config batch order and exclusions — exceptional debuggability, a CI guard that catches a silently-changed order or a lost candidate (the anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time manifest DIFF, not a runtime count), and the strongest realization of Spring's build-time-metadata intent. A cycle, a typo-guarded bad exclusion, or a duplicate fails the BUILD.

**Pros:** Earliest-richest diagnostics of all three (§2.9): a cycle, a duplicate, or a typo-guarded bad exclusion fails at BUILD time with the offending edge/contributor named and the full proposed order inspectable in the generated file — strictly earlier than R1/R2's cold planning phase, and the manifest `--check` catches a silently-changed order in CI (the anti-DCE self-check as a build-time diff).; Lowest startup overhead (#2): the three-pass sort + topo-sort + exclusion merge run at build time and freeze into a flat ordered slice; runtime only subtracts the late Environment-property exclusions from an already-ordered list (order-preserving, no topo-sort) and checks the kill-switch — near-zero cold-start cost.; The truest native analogue of Spring's build-time `spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties` (doc 1226): Spring ALREADY reads order/before/after from build-time metadata without loading classes — R3 is exactly that intent, made first-class and inspectable rather than a hidden optimization.; Fully platform-independent (Arch C): no link-time sections, works on wasm/embedded/staticlib where R1/R2's linkme-fed candidate tables are fragile; and the frozen plan sidesteps all three DCE layers for the PLANNED batch (it names every candidate, forcing references) — the most reliable substrate for this feature.; The generated, checked-in ordered manifest IS the documentation of the app's auto-config batch — a single legible artifact for debugging 'why did X order before Y', far better than reconstructing a runtime sort, and a natural place for the condition-report to attach reasons.

**Cons:** PRE-DECIDES the metadata/codegen boundary AND the compile-vs-runtime split (both explicit Phase-2 keystones, charter §3) — presenting build-time ordering as THE shape biases that signal hard; must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, the most coupled-to-an-undecided-meta-architecture of the three (this is the deepest reason it cannot be the lone answer in Phase 1).; CROSS-CRATE is the structural wall: a build.rs/proc-macro sees ONLY its own crate, so the binary's codegen cannot read foreign crates' `before`/`after`/identity from their annotations directly — it must rely on each contributor crate emitting a build-time MANIFEST/const descriptor aggregated via cargo metadata, a convention every contributor must honor; a contributor that doesn't emit its manifest entry is invisible to the build-time sort (and the manifest diff must catch it).; The Environment-property exclusion source (`leaf.autoconfigure.exclude`) and the kill-switch are inherently RUNTIME (the Environment isn't known at build time), so the model is NOT purely build-time — it is build-time order + a runtime residual exclusion subtraction; the split between frozen and residual is a new authoring/ops surface and a potential confusion ('why didn't my build-time order change when I set the exclude property?' — because property exclusions are residual by design).; Heaviest machinery of the three (a manifest convention, a build-time aggregator, the three-pass sort + topo-sort + typo-guard in codegen, the emitter, a `--check`) — in tension with thin-macros (§2.10) unless ALL heavy logic lives in a normal leaf-codegen crate the macro merely feeds (which the charter permits), but it is still the most to specify, keep idempotent (OUT_DIR hygiene, deterministic codegen), and test.; A dynamically-loaded WASM-module auto-config has NO build-time presence — its identity/order/before/after aren't in the cargo graph, so it cannot participate in the frozen plan and must be merged into the ordering at RUNTIME, reintroducing a (smaller) runtime topo-sort for exactly the dynamic case — the frozen-plan shape and the dynamic-directory 'classpath' are in direct tension here, a flagged Phase-2 question.

**Mechanisms considered:** leaf-codegen (build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare`) runs the three-pass sort (alphabetical → order → stable topo with cycle detection) + exclusion merge + typo-guard at BUILD time over a cargo-metadata-aggregated per-crate descriptor manifest; emit a frozen `auto_config_order.rs`: a flat `&[AutoConfigId]` in final batch order + resolved exclusion set + unresolved-name record, `include!`d into the binary; split exclusions into BUILD-known (typed `exclude` + `exclude_name`) merged at build vs RUNTIME-residual (`leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property + kill-switch) subtracted order-preservingly at startup; native analogue of Spring's build-time spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties (read order/before/after without loading classes) — made first-class + inspectable; checked-in, `--check`-able ordered manifest as the anti-DCE self-check (build-time DIFF) and the app's auto-config-batch documentation; per-crate manifest/const-descriptor convention aggregated via cargo metadata (the binary's build can't read foreign annotations directly — the hard cross-crate wall); runtime residual topo-merge ONLY for dynamic WASM-module-contributed auto-configs with no build-time presence — fallback that reintroduces a small runtime sort; candidate not a decision; cycle / duplicate / bad-exclusion fail the BUILD

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Strongest fit for the build-time-codegen substrate (Arch C) and the only realization that works cleanly on wasm/embedded for this feature (no link-time slices needed for the order itself). The codegen names every candidate in the frozen plan, force-linking them and sidestepping all three DCE layers for the PLANNED batch — and the manifest `--check` turns a silently-lost candidate into a loud build-time diff, the best possible form of the mandated self-check. BUT the central T1 limitation is severe and structural: a build.rs/proc-macro sees ONLY its own crate (the hard wall), so the binary's codegen cannot introspect foreign crates' `before`/`after`/order/identity — each contributor crate must emit a build-time MANIFEST entry (or const descriptor) the binary's pass aggregates via cargo metadata, a convention with no compiler enforcement (a contributor that forgets it is silently absent → the manifest diff is the only guard). Class-names-as-public-API is realized as the manifest's stable string identity (canonical module_path-derived name), which downstream `before_name`/`exclude_name` reference — same version/refactor-stability semver surface as R1/R2, but now resolved at build time where a mismatch can fail the build rather than silently resolve-to-nothing (a diagnostic improvement). The honest split: typed/name refs and exclusions known at build freeze cleanly; the Environment-property exclusion source and any dynamic WASM-module candidate are RUNTIME residuals — so the model is build-frozen order + runtime residual exclusion, an intra-build vs runtime asymmetry the user model must surface. Generics hard-error. Two-source duality: the cargo-graph manifest is the default 'classpath' (frozen); the dynamic WASM-module 'classpath' has no build presence → its auto-configs must be topo-merged into the frozen order at runtime — direct tension with the frozen-plan shape, flagged, candidate not a decision.

**T2 — execution context:** Inverts the phase split toward BUILD time. The three-pass sort + topo-sort + exclusion merge + typo-guard run as a SYNCHRONOUS BUILD-TIME pass (build.rs / CLI) — single-threaded, NOT in the application's async runtime; it may do build-time IO (read manifests, cargo metadata) but produces only data (the generated ordered slice). At STARTUP the runtime does almost nothing: read the frozen order, subtract the late `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment-property exclusions (an in-memory, order-preserving filter — no topo-sort, no IO, no await), honor the kill-switch, hand the ordered batch to definition registration. This residual is cold-path, synchronous, trivially fast. The ONLY runtime topo-sort reappears if a dynamic WASM-module auto-config with no build presence must be merged — and that, if it exists, runs in the same cold planning window, synchronous, non-blocking. ERRORS split by TIMING: build-decidable failures (cycle, duplicate, typed/name typo-guard violation) fail the BUILD — earliest, richest, with the full proposed order inspectable and a `--check` for CI; only residual failures (an Environment-property exclusion naming a non-auto-config) surface at the cold startup phase as a diagnostic, still before async construction. Cancellation is irrelevant to the build pass (offline) and the residual is too short to matter. Async/execution-context discipline (§2.3) barely touches this feature in R3 — all ordering logic is build-time data production; the downstream definition registration and instantiation are unchanged. The residual risk is the build-frozen/runtime-residual SEAM legibility: an author setting a property exclusion must understand it applies as a runtime residual to the already-frozen order (the manifest shows the build-time order; the residual is applied on top), which the generated artifact + diagnostics must make explicit.

### Rust clashes
- NO RUNTIME CLASSPATH + NO RUNTIME NAME→TYPE RESOLUTION, yet Spring treats CLASS NAMES AS PUBLIC API for ordering and exclusions. Spring's `@AutoConfigureBefore("x.Y")`, `beforeName`/`afterName`, `excludeName`, and `spring.autoconfigure.exclude=x.Y` all name an auto-config by FULLY-QUALIFIED STRING that the classloader resolves at runtime — letting a crate order/exclude relative to a config it has NO compile dependency on. Rust cannot resolve a string to a type at runtime. So leaf must split identity into TYPED refs (TypeId/path, compile-checked + DCE-safe, but require a compile dependency) and STRING refs (a canonical `module_path!`-derived stable name resolved at runtime against the candidate set's name index, for the genuine no-dependency case). The string identity becomes a refactor-fragile, version-stable, semver-relevant public surface authors must consciously maintain — a misspelled or renamed name ref 'resolves to nothing' rather than erroring (R1), is lint-flagged as second-class (R2), or fails the build via the manifest (R3). There is no faithful reproduction of a classloader-resolved FQCN.
- ORDERING MUST BE DATA + A TOPO-SORT — NEVER LINK/SECTION/CONSTRUCTOR ORDER. Spring's sorter works over candidates whose order is read from build-time metadata or ASM; leaf's candidates arrive from linkme distributed-slices or inventory constructors whose ORDER IS UNSPECIFIED and may be deliberately randomized (the cross-crate doc's hard rule). So the alphabetical BASE pass is not a cosmetic detail — it is THE mechanism that makes the result reproducible despite a non-deterministic substrate; without a deterministic data-derived base, two builds (or two linkers, or debug vs release) could emit different auto-config orders silently. The `@AutoConfigureOrder` int and before/after edges must likewise live as DATA on each descriptor, resolved by a STABLE topological sort, never inferred from collection order. This is a direct, non-negotiable clash with the substrate's unordered/randomized delivery.
- BUILD-TIME `spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties` (read order/before/after WITHOUT loading classes) maps cleanly to ordering-as-DATA but tugs toward the undecided codegen boundary. Spring's hidden fast-path (doc 1226) already reads ordering metadata at build time to avoid ASM-loading every candidate — the rust-native analogue is trivially ordering-as-const-data on the descriptor (R1/R2) OR a full build-time frozen sort (R3). The clash is that the MOST faithful realization of this specific Spring optimization (R3) pre-touches the metadata/codegen-boundary and compile-vs-runtime keystones (§3) — so honoring Spring's build-time-metadata intent risks pre-deciding a Phase-2 question. The intent (ordering data available without loading the class) transfers cleanly; HOW MUCH of the sort itself moves to build time does not.
- DEFINITION-ORDER vs CREATION-ORDER separation (doc 1234) is clean in Spring but must be an explicit, enforced boundary in leaf. Spring is explicit that `@AutoConfigureBefore`/`After` order only the DEFINITION registration (so conditions evaluate against deterministic predecessors), while instance creation is dependency/`@DependsOn`-driven. In leaf's async-first world the temptation is to conflate 'ordered batch' with 'instantiation schedule'. The sorter MUST output definition order ONLY and never touch the async instantiation scheduler (which stays dependency/concurrency-driven, possibly with background-bootstrap concurrency) — otherwise auto-config ordering would silently serialize or reorder construction, violating the doc-1234 intent and the async-first invariant. This is a clash of mental models that must be designed against, not assumed away.
- CYCLE DETECTION must produce a RICH, CROSS-CRATE causal diagnostic, but the cycle may span crates that don't compile-depend on each other. Spring emits 'AutoConfigure cycle detected between X and Y'. In leaf a cycle can form via STRING refs across crates with no compile dependency (A's before_name → B, B's after_name → A), so reconstructing and naming the cycle requires resolving the mixed typed+string edge graph and reporting each node's contributor crate — at the earliest-richest point (§2.9: cold planning phase, R1/R2; build time, R3). The clash: the richest diagnostic wants compile-time, but a string-ref cycle is only knowable once the candidate set is assembled (runtime in R1/R2; build-time-with-manifest in R3) — so the diagnostic timing is entangled with how identity is realized.
- THE THREE-SOURCE EXCLUSION MERGE crosses the compile/runtime boundary unevenly. Spring merges typed `exclude=`, string `excludeName=`, and the `spring.autoconfigure.exclude` Environment property into one set. In leaf, typed `exclude` is compile-known (and its typo-guard can be a build error — R2/R3), string `exclude_name` is build-or-runtime-known depending on substrate, but the Environment-property exclusion is INHERENTLY RUNTIME (the Environment isn't populated until startup). So the merge cannot be wholly build-time (R3 must keep a runtime residual) nor uniformly diagnosed (the typo-guard is build-time for typed excludes, runtime for property excludes) — an asymmetry Spring's uniform runtime merge hides, and which couples this feature to `environment`/`binder`/`relaxed-binding` and the (undecided) compile-vs-runtime split.
- `checkExcludedClasses` TYPO-GUARD needs to know 'is this an auto-config?' which requires the whole-binary descriptor inventory + an auto-config MARKER, not a classpath query. Spring throws if you exclude a class that's present-but-not-an-auto-config. leaf has no classpath to ask 'is X present?'; it must consult the LINKED descriptor inventory and a per-descriptor 'is-auto-config' marker (from `#[auto_configuration]`) to distinguish 'excluded a regular component/config' (loud error) from 'excluded an absent config' (softer note) — coupling a feature that looks like a pure sorter to component-scanning/configuration-classes' inventory and to the DCE-completeness of that inventory (a missing crate makes a real exclusion look absent).
- GENERICS CANNOT CARRY A `'static` ORDERING DESCRIPTOR. A generic `#[auto_configuration] struct FooAutoConfig<T>` has no monomorphized `'static` value/symbol for a descriptor table, no stable TypeId until instantiated, and no canonical module-path identity for string refs — so the macro must HARD-ERROR with a `register_auto_config!(ConcreteFoo)` per-instantiation shim, the same constraint every contributor kind hits, here applied to ordering identity and the before/after/exclude reference graph.

### Interactions
- **auto-configuration** — The PARENT feature and sole consumer of this sorter. `auto-configuration` assembles the multi-crate auto-config candidate set (loaded via import-composition's deferred selector, backing off after user config) and DELEGATES the deterministic batch ordering + exclusion subtraction to THIS feature, exactly as Spring's `AutoConfigurationImportSelector.getAutoConfigurationEntry` calls `AutoConfigurationSorter.getInPriorityOrder` and `getExclusions`/`checkExcludedClasses`. The 'opinionated but overridable' soul depends on this: ordering fixes deterministic DEFINITION order so the back-off conditions evaluate against a stable predecessor set, and exclusions are the hard override. This feature is a pure function auto-configuration invokes; it does not assemble candidates itself.
- **import-composition** — This feature IS the realization of `DeferredImportSelector.Group`'s merge/sort step (doc 1044-1048): the Group collects candidates across every selector and returns ONE merged, de-duped, @Order-sorted batch — the merge+order is precisely the three passes here. import-composition supplies the WHEN (the deferred batch phase, after all user config) and the candidate stream; auto-config-ordering supplies the HOW (alphabetical → order → topological with cycle detection) and the exclusion subtraction. The doc explicitly notes (1048) the Group is 'what makes that batch coherent' — this feature is that coherence-maker.
- **conditions** — Deeply causal and the REASON ordering exists. The doc-1234 hidden concept: ordering affects DEFINITION order so @Conditional (especially @ConditionalOnMissingBean/@ConditionalOnBean) on a later auto-config evaluates against a deterministic, correct set of earlier definitions. If A is ordered before B, B's OnMissingBean sees A's contributed beans and backs off. So this feature's output is the INPUT ASSUMPTION conditions rely on — a non-deterministic order would make condition outcomes non-deterministic. The interaction is a hard ordering contract: definitions registered in batch order, conditions evaluated against the resulting predecessor state.
- **condition-report** — The natural sink for this feature's diagnostics. Spring's ConditionEvaluationReport records positiveMatches, negativeMatches, AND EXCLUSIONS (doc 1162) — the merged exclusion set this feature computes feeds the report's exclusions section, and the resolved batch ORDER + any unresolved name refs / typo-guard findings are exactly the 'accountable, debuggable' record condition-report exists to provide. R3's frozen ordered manifest is itself a superset of what condition-report would show for ordering.
- **environment** — Supplies two of this feature's inputs: the `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` exclusion property (the third exclusion source, read synchronously at planning time) and the `leaf.enable-autoconfiguration=false` global kill-switch (doc 1218). The Environment is populated before the planning phase, so these are in-memory reads (no IO/await). This is the source that is inherently RUNTIME (the rustClash on the three-source merge crossing the compile/runtime boundary) — the part R3 cannot freeze at build time.
- **binder** — The Environment-property exclusion source (`leaf.autoconfigure.exclude`) is BOUND via the binder with LIST support — Spring binds it as a String list via the Binder. So this feature consumes the binder to turn the raw property into a typed list of exclusion name refs, inheriting relaxed-binding (next interaction). The exclusion list is a small, concrete bind target the binder handles before the sort runs.
- **relaxed-binding** — The `leaf.autoconfigure.exclude` property gets relaxed binding (Spring: camelCase/kebab/UPPER_SNAKE env-var forms, list/index conventions). So an ops user can set the exclusion via an UPPER_SNAKE env var or a kebab-case key and it maps to the same canonical exclusion list — relaxed-binding governs how the exclusion property's KEY is recognized across transports, decoupled from the canonical auto-config NAME identity (which is a separate refactor-fragile surface).
- **configuration-classes** — The UNIT being ordered. Each auto-config is a lite-only configuration (doc 1186: @AutoConfiguration hardwires proxyBeanMethods=false) whose #[bean]-seeds are the bean definitions registered in batch order. This feature orders the CONFIGS (configuration-classes provides the marker + the typed Factory seeds + the 'is-auto-config' marker the typo-guard needs); the ordered sequence determines the DEFINITION registration order of those configs' seeds. The doc-1234 boundary means this feature touches definition order, not the config's instantiation.
- **bean-definition** — The output of ordering is consumed at the DEFINITION level: the ordered batch fixes the sequence in which each auto-config's RawBeanDefinition seeds enter the definition registry, so condition evaluation and any definition-rewriting see a deterministic predecessor set. Ordering never touches the instances — strictly a definition-order concern (doc 1234), aligning with bean-definition's parse-then-instantiate split.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — This feature occupies a precise, fixed slot in the refresh template's cold planning window: it runs AFTER candidate assembly + user-definition registration (so back-off correctness holds) and BEFORE definition registration of the auto-config batch / instantiation. Its position is what makes the ordering meaningful. In R3 most of the work moves to build time, leaving only the runtime residual exclusion subtraction + kill-switch in the lifecycle template; in R1/R2 the full three-pass sort runs in this window.
- **annotation-model** — The `#[auto_configuration(order=, before=, after=, before_name=, after_name=)]` surface (and the app-level `exclude=`/`exclude_name=`) rests on the annotation model — Spring's @AutoConfiguration @AliasFor-forwards its inline before/after to the standalone @AutoConfigureBefore/@AutoConfigureAfter (doc 1190). leaf's annotation model lowers these attributes to the typed ordering DATA + the typed/string ref enum on the descriptor; the meta-annotation composition (an @AutoConfiguration that carries all four ordering attributes, doc 1192) is realized here as the macro emitting the descriptor fields directly.
- **collection-injection** — A deliberate CONTRAST to keep separate, not a dependency. Spring uses a DEDICATED @AutoConfigureOrder (not @Order) precisely so auto-config batch priority is decoupled from collection-injection's @Order/@Priority (which orders injected List/Set members at the CONSUMER, a runtime concern). This feature must NOT reuse collection-injection's ordering — they are different axes (definition-batch order vs injected-collection order); conflating them would be a category error the dedicated-annotation split exists to prevent.
- **component-scanning** — Provides the whole-binary descriptor INVENTORY the exclusion typo-guard consults to answer 'is this excluded name an auto-config, a regular component, or absent?' (Spring's AutoConfigurationExcludeFilter ensures auto-configs enter only via the import path, not scanning — doc 1180). The typo-guard's quality depends on the completeness of this inventory, which rides component-scanning/cross-crate DCE hazards: a crate the binary never references is absent from the inventory, making a real exclusion look like a typo.
- **profiles** — @Profile is just a @Conditional, so profile-gating interacts with ordering the same way conditions do: a profile-gated auto-config that is inactive is still ORDERED in the batch (so a later config's predecessor set is deterministic) but its definitions back off when the profile is inactive. Ordering is profile-independent (the sort runs over all candidates); activation is the condition layer's job — keeping ordering deterministic regardless of active profiles.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- IDENTITY: is a stringly, refactor-fragile canonical NAME (the 'class name as public API') a first-class co-equal mechanism (R1), a lint-flagged escape hatch behind typed refs (R2), or a build-time-resolved manifest key (R3)? Spring makes the FQCN co-equal and ops-facing (spring.autoconfigure.exclude names strings); Rust has no runtime name→type resolution, so the choice determines whether a renamed/misspelled before_name/exclude resolves-to-nothing, lint-warns, or fails the build — and it is entangled with the type-erasure & registry substrate (how is a stable cross-crate identity minted and kept version-stable?) and the cross-crate composition model. UNRESOLVED.
- BUILD-TIME vs RUNTIME: how much of the three-pass sort + exclusion merge + typo-guard runs at build time (R3's frozen ordered manifest, native to Spring's spring-autoconfigure-metadata fast-path) vs the cold planning phase (R1/R2)? This pre-touches the metadata/codegen boundary AND the compile-vs-runtime split (both §3 keystones) and the diagnostic-timing call (§2.9) — and the Environment-property exclusion source + kill-switch are inherently runtime, so even a build-time answer keeps a runtime residual. The build-frozen/runtime-residual SEAM legibility is itself unresolved. Held as a candidate axis, not pre-decided.
- DEFINITION-ORDER vs CREATION-ORDER enforcement: doc 1234 mandates ordering affects only definition registration order, never instantiation (which stays dependency/@DependsOn/background-bootstrap-concurrency-driven). How is this boundary ENFORCED so the async instantiation scheduler cannot accidentally inherit the batch order and silently serialize/reorder construction? Cross-cuts the async execution model, bean-instantiation, and background-bootstrap — UNRESOLVED whether the ordered batch is a pure definition-phase artifact discarded before instantiation, or carried (and at what risk).
- THE THREE-SOURCE EXCLUSION MERGE crosses the compile/runtime boundary unevenly (typed exclude = compile-known; exclude_name = substrate-dependent; the Environment property = runtime). How is the merge specified so the result is uniform regardless of where each source is known, and so the typo-guard's diagnostic quality (build-time for typed, runtime for property) is legible rather than surprising? Cross-cuts environment/binder/relaxed-binding and the conditional strategy. UNRESOLVED.
- CANONICAL IDENTITY STABILITY as a SEMVER surface: if the stable name is module_path!-derived, a type rename or module move silently breaks downstream before_name/exclude_name/Environment-property references. Is there a stabler identity (an explicit author-assigned id? a registered alias?), and how is breakage surfaced (a build-time alias check? a self-check warning)? Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model and bean-naming's alias/identity machinery. UNRESOLVED.
- CYCLE & TYPO DIAGNOSTIC TIMING: the richest diagnostic wants compile-time, but a STRING-ref cycle or a string/property exclusion typo-guard is only knowable once the candidate set is assembled (runtime in R1/R2; build-time-with-manifest in R3). What is the earliest point that yields the FULL causal chain (cycle path + contributor crates; bad-exclusion + what-it-matched) given the chosen identity + build/runtime split? Cross-cuts the unified error/diagnostics model (§2.9). UNRESOLVED.
- ANTI-DCE COMPLETENESS feeding ordering: the alphabetical base + name-ref resolution + the typo-guard all assume the candidate inventory is COMPLETE; a crate the binary never path-references is silently absent (Layer 0), silently shortening the batch and reordering the alphabetical base, and making a real exclusion/before_name look like a typo. How does the mandated expected-vs-found self-check (R1/R2 runtime count; R3 build-time manifest diff) integrate with THIS feature's typo-guard so 'missing candidate' and 'typo' are distinguishable? Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model. UNRESOLVED.
- THE TWO-SOURCE DUALITY for candidates: the static link-time/codegen set (default 'classpath') PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source whose auto-configs have NO build-time presence. R1/R2 absorb a dynamic candidate naturally (its stable_name slots into the runtime sort + name-keyed exclusion index); R3's frozen plan is in direct tension (dynamic candidates must be runtime-topo-merged into the frozen order). How is a WASM-contributed auto-config ordered/excluded indistinguishably from a native one (origin-agnostic), and how does its identity participate in the typed-vs-string ref graph (it has no compile-time type for downstream typed refs)? CANDIDATE, not a decision.

### Notes
Confidence: HIGH on intent. I read the dedicated feature material precisely: the AutoConfigurationSorter three-pass section (1230-1234: alphabetical base → @AutoConfigureOrder stable-sort → topological before/after with explicit cycle detection, reading order/before/after from build-time metadata else ASM, and the load-bearing 1234 hidden concept that ordering affects DEFINITION order NOT creation order); the Exclusions section (1236-1238: getExclusions merges THREE sources — typed exclude=, string excludeName=, and the spring.autoconfigure.exclude Environment property bound via Binder with relaxed binding + list support — and checkExcludedClasses as the typo-guard for excluding a present-but-not-auto-config class); the @AutoConfiguration inline before/beforeName/after/afterName @AliasFor attributes (1190) + the 'you rarely need the standalone ordering annotations' concept (1192); the build-time spring-autoconfigure-metadata.properties fast-path that reads conditions/order/before/after WITHOUT loading classes (1226); the kill-switch spring.boot.enableautoconfiguration (1218); and the consuming engine — AutoConfigurationImportSelector as a DeferredImportSelector whose AutoConfigurationGroup unions configs, subtracts exclusions, and runs getInPriorityOrder over the WHOLE set as a single ordered batch (1204-1216) — plus the DeferredImportSelector.Group 'coordinated global merging' that this sort IS (1044-1048), and that deferral is for @Conditional correctness not performance (1050). I confirmed the marquee mechanics: three passes in exactly that order; the alphabetical base as the deterministic anchor; topological with named cycle detection; three-source exclusion merge; the typo-guard; definition-order-not-creation-order; and class-names-as-public-API (downstream crates name configs by FQCN in before/after/exclude they may not compile-depend on).\n\nI grounded the deepest clashes against the cross-crate doc: ordering-is-unspecified-for-linkme/inventory-and-may-be-randomized → the alphabetical base + ordering-as-DATA + runtime topo-sort is the prescribed answer (154, 170, 355); Layer-0 DCE makes the candidate inventory possibly-incomplete → the mandated expected-vs-found self-check (149, 152, 345-346) which this feature's alphabetical base and typo-guard depend on; generics-cannot-register → hard-error + concrete shim (153, 349); the build-time-codegen sqlx model + checked-in --check manifest (227-236) for R3; Architectures A-D as substrate-neutral candidates (277-337); scope-discovery-not-global (362). The class-names-as-public-API requirement is the dominant clash: Spring's classloader-resolved FQCN strings (before_name/after_name/excludeName/the Environment property) have no Rust analogue, forcing the typed-ref-vs-string-ref split that distinguishes R1 (dual co-equal), R2 (typed-first, string as lint-flagged escape hatch), and R3 (build-time manifest key). T2 grounded against §2.3/§2.4 (this feature is entirely cold-path, synchronous, non-blocking planning logic — no hot path, nothing async, the definition-order-vs-creation-order boundary kept as an execution-context boundary so instantiation stays dependency-driven), §2.5, §2.9 (rich early diagnostics: cycle path + contributor crates, typo-guard naming what-it-matched), §2.10 (thin macros: heavy sort logic in a normal/codegen crate, descriptor emit is hand-writable), §2.11.\n\nThe three realizations are genuinely divergent on the axis that matters for THIS feature — HOW identity is realized and WHEN the sort runs: R1 = runtime three-pass sorter over ordering-as-DATA descriptors with DUAL co-equal TypeId+stable-name identity and a runtime three-source exclusion merge (most faithful to Spring's vocabulary incl. no-dependency name ordering, but reintroduces a stringly fragile surface); R2 = TYPED ordering lattice making typed before/after/exclude the compile-checked default (build-time typo-guard, DCE-safe, lowest runtime cost) with the stringly path demoted to a lint-flagged escape hatch (best DX on the common path, but pushes Spring's first-class no-dependency ordering onto a second-class channel); R3 = BUILD-TIME frozen ordering plan run by leaf-codegen emitting an inspectable, --check-able ordered manifest (earliest-richest diagnostics, near-zero startup cost, native to Spring's build-time-metadata fast-path, wasm-friendly) with a runtime residual only for the Environment-property exclusions + dynamic candidates (but pre-touches the codegen-boundary + compile-vs-runtime keystones and hits the build.rs single-crate wall). R1 vs R2 differ on co-equal-string-identity vs typed-first; R3 differs on runtime-vs-build-time resolution.\n\nThings I deliberately did NOT decide (held as Phase-2 questions): the identity mechanism (co-equal string vs typed-first vs manifest key); build-time vs runtime resolution; how the definition-order-vs-creation-order boundary is ENFORCED against the async scheduler; how the three-source exclusion merge is specified uniformly across the compile/runtime boundary; canonical-identity stability as a semver surface; cycle/typo diagnostic timing under the chosen identity+split; anti-DCE completeness feeding the alphabetical base + typo-guard; and the two-source (link/codegen + WASM-module) candidate duality vs a frozen plan. Every realization keeps the descriptor/sort seam ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a native or WASM-module-contributed auto-config sorts/excludes indistinguishably) and substrate-neutral (the sorter consumes whatever descriptor table linkme/codegen/explicit produces). I built concretely on the upstream import-composition design (this feature IS the Group's merge/sort step; auto-configuration is the consumer; the deferred batch is the WHEN, this is the HOW) and on configuration-classes (auto-configs are lite-only configs whose seeds are ordered at the DEFINITION level; the 'is-auto-config' marker feeds the typo-guard).\n\nNaming ('#[auto_configuration]', 'AutoConfigDescriptor', 'AutoConfigRef::{ByType,ByName}', 'order/before/after/before_name/after_name', 'exclude/exclude_name', 'leaf.autoconfigure.exclude', 'leaf.enable-autoconfiguration', 'OrderingError', 'auto_config_order.rs', 'register_auto_config!', 'stable_name') is Phase-1 placeholder. ## Area coherence notes

- Duplicated mechanism — the anti-DCE / Layer-0 self-check is reached for by FOUR features (conditions, condition-report R3, configuration-classes, import-composition, auto-config-ordering, auto-configuration all describe an 'expected-vs-found' count/manifest-diff), and condition-report explicitly flags 'should the report DOUBLE as the substrate's DCE self-check or is that SEPARATE?' as unresolved. This is one cross-cutting mechanism currently described per-feature; it must be unified into a single substrate-level self-check that the report CONSUMES, otherwise each feature invents its own expected-count manifest and they will disagree on what 'silently dropped' means vs 'legitimately backed off'.
- Cross-tier reconciliation is co-owned without a single owner — both condition-report (R3 cross-tier ledger) and auto-configuration ('how much pipeline is build-frozen vs runtime, with a runtime residual') and condition-family ('per-kind tier-map is a load-bearing kernel ABI') each claim a piece of the compile/build/runtime tier reconciliation. The per-kind TIER-MAP is asserted to be a 'load-bearing kernel ABI' by condition-family, but condition-report and auto-configuration both depend on knowing each element's tier to render/freeze correctly. These three must co-review to a SINGLE authoritative tier-map artifact; today three features each assume they can read tier per element but none defines where that datum is minted and frozen.
- ElementId / identity keying is asserted to be shared but defined nowhere — condition-report keys records by 'ElementId that MUST match autowiring-resolution/bean-registry lookup key', auto-config-ordering keys by 'TypeId + stable-name dual identity', auto-configuration's typo-guard keys exclusions by name against the inventory, and import-composition's edge targets key by typed-or-string ref. These are four overlapping identity schemes (TypeId, module_path-derived name, ElementId, ImportRef) that all need to JOIN for the silent-now/loud-later bridge and the cross-crate ordering graph to work. No feature owns the canonical identity; all defer to 'the registry-substrate keystone'. This is the single highest-risk unresolved coherence dependency in the area — if the identity shapes don't unify, the report-join, the ordering graph, and the exclusion typo-guard all break independently.
- @Enable*/ImportAware multi-importer attribute resolution is an orphaned injection KIND — import-composition correctly flags 'when a config is imported by TWO importers with different @Enable* attributes, whose does the importee receive?' as a new injection kind distinct from bean injection, but neither annotation-model nor autowiring-resolution (the two it cross-cuts) claims it, and configuration-classes (which owns config-as-unit) doesn't model importer-metadata injection at all. This semantic must be assigned a clear owner (likely import-composition itself, with an explicit per-edge-instance-vs-error-on-conflict rule) before annotation-model freezes its descriptor shape.
- Realization-tier mismatch risk between configuration-classes and auto-configuration on the 'config as runtime bean vs compile-time grouping' axis — configuration-classes offers R1/R2 (config is a runtime managed bean holding shared state) and R3 (pure compile-time grouping that dissolves). auto-configuration MANDATES lite-only and leans toward R3-style build-frozen plans. If configuration-classes lands on R1/R2 (runtime config bean with @Autowired fields) while auto-configuration assumes configs dissolve into per-bean definitions, auto-config classes and user configs would have DIFFERENT lifetime/identity models — a split-brain where 'config' means two things. The lite-only mandate needs to be reconciled with whichever config realization is chosen so there is ONE config model, not a user-config model and an auto-config model.
- Definition-order-not-creation-order boundary is asserted by three features but enforced by none — auto-config-ordering, auto-configuration, and bean-definition all repeat doc-1234's rule that ordering affects DEFINITION order only, never instantiation order. auto-config-ordering's Phase-2 question 'how is this boundary ENFORCED so the async scheduler cannot inherit batch order' correctly identifies the risk, but the enforcement (the ordered batch must be a definition-phase artifact discarded before the instantiation scheduler sees it) crosses into refresh-lifecycle and the async-execution model with no single owner. Coherence depends on the ordered batch being explicitly NON-readable by the instantiation scheduler.
- OnSingleCandidate delegation is consistently deferred to autowiring-resolution by BOTH conditions and condition-family (unification #11, 'one definition of unambiguous'), which is coherent — but note that condition-family evaluates in the REGISTER phase against DEFINITIONS while autowiring-resolution's candidate-resolver typically operates over the resolvable candidate set at injection time. The 'would by-type autowire resolve unambiguously' verdict must run the candidate-resolver's primary/fallback/qualifier policy over the DEFINITION view (not live beans, no construction). Both features assume the shared primitive can run definition-only; this must be verified with autowiring-resolution that its candidate-resolver has a no-instantiation, definition-level mode.
